Commentary

Recent Relations Between Japan and the Soviet Union 10

— Li

Conflicts occurred between the Japanese-Manchukuoan forces and the Soviet forces near Khabarovsk on the 6th, 8th, and 12th of this month, resulting in casualties on both sides. Afterwards, the Soviet authorities, in addition to dispatching more than twenty cruisers and submarines and concentrating them near Khabarovsk, mobilized 200,000 troops to Manchuria to prevent another attack by the Japanese-Manchukuoan forces. Furthermore, they instructed their ambassador to Japan, Yurenev, to lodge a serious protest with Japan and request the formation of a joint committee to determine responsibility for previous border conflicts. The puppet Manchukuoan authorities then consulted with the Kwantung Army on countermeasures and were reported to have accepted the Soviet demand to establish a joint committee. This matter has probably gradually become more moderate and should not immediately lead to significant consequences.

Since the September 18th Incident, disputes between Japan and the Soviet Union have emerged one after another, numbering more than three hundred to date. The easing and intensification of these disputes are invariably related to the world political situation and Japan's continental policy. After the illegal sale and purchase of the Chinese Eastern Railway was completed, relations between the two countries gradually became harmonious. However, with the occurrence of the Hebei-Chahar Incident, tensions re-emerged. The situation calmed down somewhat in February. Now, with the outbreak of the Italian-Abyssinian War and the unrest in Europe, and with Germany's anti-Soviet activities proceeding actively, the Japanese-Manchukuoan provocation against the Soviet Union this time was certainly also prompted by the current international situation.

Japan and the Soviet Union have different political systems and different beliefs, and their situation in the Far East is inherently confrontational. Moreover, Japan's continental policy must take anti-Sovietism as its guiding principle. Therefore, the evolution of the disputes between the two countries is bound to resort to force eventually. However, Japan believes that preparations are not yet sufficient. Although it is eager to try, it does not dare to act rashly. It must wait until the completion of the arc-shaped line surrounding Siberia and obtain greater control over the mainland to facilitate the supply of resources in wartime before it can contend with the Soviet Union. As for the Soviet Union, it is always on guard. Judging from the emphasis placed on locating the center of the Second Five-Year Plan's military industry in the east of the Ural Mountains and the special emphasis on cold-resistant horseback riding, ice skating, skiing, and other training for the army, this is evident. It is only because its economic construction plan needs to be completed urgently and the eastward ambition of Germany needs to be guarded against that it is also unwilling to lightly initiate war with Japan.

Although the opportunity for war between the two countries has not yet matured, the deterioration of international politics and the radical advance of Japan's continental policy can at any time cause the disputes between the two countries to deepen, leading to the possibility of war. In this kind of crisis, the difficulty of the position in which our country finds itself can be imagined. I sincerely hope that the people of our country will understand the dynamics of international politics and accumulate the blood and vitality of the nation to cope with the difficult situation that may become increasingly worse in the future.

Carefully Clarifying Britain's Position: Foreign Secretary Hoare's Concise Speech Summary 11

Resolutely Refuting the Fallacy of Semi-Independent Action, Loyally Upholding the Collective Security System

(London) With the British House of Commons elections imminent, the final session was held today at 2 PM to discuss foreign policy. The audience chamber was packed. Foreign Secretary Hoare delivered an important speech, providing a detailed explanation of the government's foreign policy and the Italo-Abyssinian issue. Here is an excerpt of his address:

Caring for Peace Without Selfish Intentions

"Britain, as a vast global empire, is constantly concerned with maintaining world peace. Britain's actions regarding the Abyssinian affair are entirely based on this concern, without any imperialistic selfish intentions whatsoever. To think that Britain seeks to take this opportunity to attack Fascism is absurd and requires no further refutation. All countries have the right to resolve their own political system issues. Our country is particularly unwilling to interfere in the internal affairs of other nations.

Maintaining the Covenant as the Sole Aspiration

Our only aspiration in participating in the Geneva negotiations is to uphold the principles of the League of Nations covenant. If the world does not understand and believes that Britain is acting alone in Geneva, then it should be known that the representatives of Britain and the various dominions of the British Empire attending the League of Nations conference cannot take a secondary position when discussing all major international issues. This is their duty, which cannot be shirked or concealed. Unfortunately, the Geneva negotiations cannot always be completely open.

Independent Action Needs No Refutation

If not, then the truth will be revealed, and the fallacy of so-called British independent action will be self-defeating. This fallacy not only slanders Britain but also poses a great danger, as there is no better way to plunge Europe into the calamities of war. I must also solemnly declare that the actions of Under-Secretary Eden in Geneva are in complete agreement with my own and the entire cabinet's opinions, without the slightest difference between them.

Diplomatic Negotiations Continue Uninterrupted

As for the rumors that the British government's actions on the Abyssinian issue have been too slow, and that Italy requested an explanation of Britain's position on the Abyssinian issue months ago but Britain did not respond, this is simply a misunderstanding of the truth. Since the end of 1934, Britain has been constantly negotiating with Italy on the Abyssinian issue. In January of this year, the French and Italian governments established the Rome Accords, and the Abyssinian issue was also part of it. However, France, in addition to fulfilling existing obligations and the interests of the Djibouti-Addis Ababa railway, is not interested in Abyssinia from an economic point of view. It was not until January 29 of this year that the Italian government notified the British government of the full text of the Franco-Italian Rome Accords and expressed its willingness to exchange views with Britain to ensure the harmonious development of British and Italian interests in Abyssinia. Because the Italian proposal at the time was quite serious, the British government immediately appointed a committee to be responsible for conducting a comprehensive review of Anglo-Abyssinian relations and British interests in Abyssinia to determine the attitude Britain should take. However, this type of research must consult experts and witnesses from various parties and must also consult with the governments of Anglo-Egyptian Sudan and the British colony of Kenya. From this, it can be seen that if Britain could not respond to Italy's proposal in a timely manner, the reason was that Italy's actions in Abyssinia progressed too quickly, preventing the British government from taking a leisurely and cautious approach to long-term planning.

Seeking a Solution Without Bias

It is also inaccurate to say that the Abyssinian issue was not included on the agenda of the Stresa Conference. At that time, the British, French, and Italian delegations discussed the issue, and the Italian government was fully aware of Britain's views. Britain also expressed its hope that the Italian-Abyssinian dispute would be resolved amicably. It can be seen that since the beginning of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, we have always shown Britain's attitude, not allowing Italy to have any doubts. Not only Britain but also the member states of the League of Nations have been preparing to find a way to achieve an honorable resolution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute every day, every week. Now, I take this opportunity to reiterate that the Italian-Abyssinian issue must be resolved within the framework of the League of Nations. The government has never taken an extreme attitude and has not shown partiality towards either Italy or Abyssinia. Members of the House can all recall that, not only that, I dare to confidently say that I was the first responsible politician to remind the world to acknowledge Italy's rights to security and economic expansion. However, the final resolution of the Italian-Abyssinian issue must be honorably accepted by the League of Nations and the three parties of Italy and Abyssinia.

Leaving Room for Breath Before Sanctions

Now, before economic sanctions take effect, we still have room to breathe and take the opportunity to conduct negotiations and seek a resolution. Why is it impossible? Moreover, Italy is still a member state of the League of Nations, which is the most gratifying thing. Italy is not only a member state of the League of Nations with us but also an old friend and our old ally. If we say that at this final hour, we can no longer have the opportunity to seek a resolution and must take further action beyond difficult economic measures against our old friend, why must that be the case? Furthermore, the Italian-Abyssinian issue is not merely a local dispute in East Africa but a much more significant issue. Whether there is still some hope for resolving this issue is not something I know. However, our vision looks far into the future of humanity, and our aspiration is to maintain the principle of collective action. Therefore, no matter what, we must still hope that the terrifying conflict will quickly come to an end.

Important Test of Collective Security

As for military sanctions, this must be collectively agreed upon by the Geneva side. However, this kind of collective agreement does not exist. Since the outbreak of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, we have declared that although we are prepared to participate in all actions within our capacity, our actions should be limited to the scope of collective action. The word "collective" must be given special attention, as it is the soul of the League of Nations. French Prime Minister Laval has already stated this in his speech in Clermont-Ferrand. We have not proposed any military measures to France. We now only have one thought: if treaties continue to be violated, then the League of Nations and our civilization cannot continue to survive. Currently, our difficulty is that some foreign countries, although they know that there is no perfect solution, still do not have the courage to face the facts. They often criticize the League of Nations, saying that it cannot fulfill its obligations. However, when they need to fulfill their obligations to the League of Nations, they often shy away. In short, the great experiment we are currently undertaking is unprecedented in the world for generations. The mechanism of collective security is now being tested for the first time. If the trial is successful, we can easily sit back and watch its effectiveness. If the trial is unsuccessful, then all those who advocate not using war as an instrument of national policy will feel a major blow of disappointment. If this experiment fails, then those who participate in action with a hesitant attitude should bear a heavy responsibility. In conclusion, if collective action is reliable, we should recognize it. If collective action can gain our trust, we should also recognize it. If so, then who are those who faithfully support the collective security system, and who are those who verbally call for supporting the collective security system but attack and provoke the countries that implement collective security? We should be able to distinguish between them," he concluded. (Havas News Agency, 22nd)

Speech by the New Leader of the Labour Party

The new leader of the Labour Party, Attlee, rose to speak, stating that the Labour Party's policy is based on prioritizing the interests of the League of Nations and the entire world over the needs of national interests. He welcomed Foreign Secretary Hoare's position of upholding the League of Nations covenant but did not agree with the British government's past passivity, as the current situation is largely due to the lack of action in the Sino-Japanese dispute. The Labour Party supports economic sanctions and the League of Nations system, but the League of Nations must become a vibrant organization in the future. He advocated that the British government should abandon any preferential treatment granted by treaties to eliminate the various suspicions that others have about Britain having a special relationship with the Abyssinian issue. The Nile River water source should be resolved by the League of Nations, Egypt should be allowed to terminate its current relationship with Britain, and Sudan should be placed under the trusteeship of the League of Nations. Attlee then attacked the government's policy of heavily expanding armaments, stating that the Labour Party is prepared to support the armaments necessary to fulfill Britain's obligations to the League of Nations, but it cannot give the government a blank check. The Labour Party plans to go to the polls with the party platform of socialism and peace, believing that the two are inseparable, he said.

The Liberal Party Expresses Its Views

Sir Samuel rose to say that the Liberal Party is willing to support the government and urge the League of Nations to adopt a constructive peace policy and establish mechanisms to alleviate suffering. Regarding this, Sir Samuel said that the current nine political entities occupy three-quarters of the world, while the remaining fifty countries occupy only one-quarter. Countries such as Japan, Germany, and Italy have actually been isolated. Regarding this issue, he advocated urgently seeking an economic solution.

Lansbury Ends the Debate

Former Labour Party leader Lansbury spoke from the back row, stating that the economic problems facing today's civilization cannot be resolved by collective security or force. Britain should make a bold and generous gesture, inviting all countries to hold a conference to discuss how world products can be distributed and declare to the public as an example, "We are willing to place everything into the common distribution." The debate ended at this point, and it was decided to continue the meeting tomorrow so that the Labour Party could present a motion of impeachment on unemployment on Thursday (Reuters News Agency, 22nd).

Upper House Foreign Policy Debate: Filled With an Atmosphere of Friendship Towards Italy 12

(London) During today's debate on foreign affairs in the Upper House, many speakers expressed friendship towards Italy. Lord Londonderry, Minister and Leader of the Upper House, reiterated the government's policy, which was largely the same as what Foreign Secretary Hoare said in the Lower House. Lord Snell, the new leader of the Labour Party in the Upper House, announced that the Labour Party intends to support the government but only to the extent of seeking collective security, and it cannot support the government's urgent expansion of armaments. Lord Ponsonby, a Conservative Party member, criticized Italy's aggressive actions but called Italy "an old friend of Britain" and also criticized the Abyssinian government's slow abolition of slavery and arms trafficking, saying that it would be better to entrust Abyssinia to a civilized country for trusteeship as soon as possible. Earl of Cavan, the commander-in-chief of the British forces stationed in Italy from 1918 to 1919, praised the bravery of the Italian soldiers. Lord Northcliffe, who served as Secretary of War for two years before the European War, advocated reimposing the ban on arms exports to Abyssinia (Reuters News Agency, 22nd).

Good Impression in Europe: Abyssinian Government Expresses Disappointment 13

(London) Today's speech by Foreign Secretary Hoare in the Lower House was well-received in Europe. The impression in Paris was extremely good, praising his speech for being straightforward, clear, and visionary. Geneva was also satisfied but regretted that the Foreign Secretary did not mention how to use the "breathing time" before implementing sanctions. There has been no official reaction from Rome, but the general public acknowledges that the Foreign Secretary's words were friendly and moderate, which indicates that there is no possibility of war in Europe (Reuters News Agency, 22nd).

(Rome) Semi-official sources have expressed some satisfaction with the speech delivered by British Foreign Secretary Hoare in the House of Commons yesterday, as Britain does not disagree that resolving the Italian-Abyssinian dispute should take into account Italy's perspective and the structure of the League of Nations, which can be seen in Hoare's speech. The semi-official sources here are particularly pleased that Hoare reiterated his guarantee that the United States will not currently block the Suez Canal and the two ends of the Italian coast. However, Hoare's speech, which firmly declared that Britain would support the League of Nations' collective action to implement sanctions against Italy, has been criticized by people here (Havas News Agency, 23rd).

Addis Ababa: According to a dispatch from our special correspondent Oschina, officials here expressed disappointment after British Foreign Secretary Hoare delivered a speech in the House of Commons yesterday explaining the country's foreign policy. Although they did not expect military sanctions from Britain, they still hoped that it would propose sanctions of a semi-military nature. Regarding the League of Nations' decision on various economic sanctions against Italy, officials here also expressed pessimism about whether these sanctions will be effective if certain European countries continue to trade with Italy directly or indirectly (Havas News Agency, 23rd).

Differing Opinions Among British Newspapers 14

French Newspapers Believe Reconciliation is Hopeful, Italian Newspapers Criticize with Cold Ridicule

(London) British newspapers have different opinions on Foreign Secretary Hoare's speech in the House of Commons yesterday. The Daily Telegraph said that since the Abyssinian war is still in Mussolini's hands, the most important part of the Foreign Secretary's speech was his powerful appeal directly to Italy. The Morning Post said that the fact that military sanctions were not discussed is welcome, but the Daily News said that the British government seems to be pursuing an incomplete policy, which on the one hand does not condone the violation of covenants and on the other hand cannot bring the aggressor to justice. The Daily Express said that our remarks only confirm the general public's anxiety and suspicion about the government's foreign policy. The Times said that for those who faithfully study British policy, not a single sentence in the Foreign Secretary's entire speech does not represent the truth. The Daily Mail said that many people now feel that trusting the League of Nations is a mistake (Reuters News Agency, 23rd).

(Paris) French newspapers today have commented on the speech delivered by British Foreign Secretary Hoare in the House of Commons yesterday. Le Matin said that this speech not only reassures people about Britain's future role in the Italo-Abyssinian war but also brings comfort, considering it the beginning of a peaceful resolution to the case. However, several newspapers said that the British Foreign Secretary's speech was intended to cater to popular sentiment in view of the upcoming general election (Reuters News Agency, 23rd).

(Rome) Only Il Popolo di Roma criticized British Foreign Secretary Hoare's speech yesterday, but in a cold tone. The newspaper's headline referred to it as "appropriate talk for domestic sales," and said that Italy is now waiting for Britain to express a word of justice, and the world is still hoping for practical peace talks. Officials did not comment on the British Foreign Secretary's speech, but most Italians are more hopeful that the Italian-Abyssinian dispute can be resolved and that the League of Nations sanctions can be avoided (Reuters News Agency, 23rd).

No War in East Africa: Silence on Both the Northern and Southern Routes 15

If Diplomatic Negotiations are Ineffective, the Great War Will Begin Next Month: The Abyssinian Emperor Flies for the First Time, Piloted by a German

(Rome) A communiqué was released here today stating that according to a telegram from General De Bono, Commander-in-Chief of the Italian forces in East Africa, there is nothing to report on both the northern and southern routes, and the residents in the areas occupied by the Italian army have returned to normal (Reuters News Agency, 23rd).

Asmara: Although there are widespread rumors that a major battle between the main forces of Italy and Abyssinia is imminent, many people here now believe that if diplomatic mediation is not effective by November, then there will be a major decisive battle on the northern front before the end of that month. Italian staff officers are currently unaware of any Abyssinian forces gathered in the Amba Aradam area south of Mek'ele. They now believe that this gathering will take a month due to poor transportation, lack of transport, and many difficulties in supplying food. However, Italian aircraft are still engaged in reconnaissance and are very active. It is reported that Italian aircraft today detected that the troops of General Kassa, Commander-in-Chief of the Abyssinian forces on the northern route, are currently advancing north from Addis Ababa, hoping to join the forces of General Seyoum, who commands the troops guarding Mek'ele in Tigray Province. Large numbers of Abyssinian troops are stationed near Gondar, outside the Tekeze River, and north of Lake Tana. However, the number of Abyssinian soldiers seen near the Italian front line in Tigray Province is very small, so the Italian army expects that when it launches a general offensive on the city of Mek'ele in the future, it will not encounter fierce resistance in front of the city. According to reports from Harar, everything is quiet on the southern front. However, some Italian troops are being transferred from Eritrea in the north to Italian Somaliland in the south in preparation for the start of the great battle in the Ogaden Province. According to news from Addis Ababa, the Abyssinian Emperor flew for the first time today for two hours, flying halfway to Dessie and turning back. Dessie will be the main base for the Abyssinian forces on the northern route. The aircraft used by the Emperor was a Fokker aircraft with three engines. From the sky, he saw tens of thousands of Abyssinian soldiers who had successively departed and were heading to the northern front line in the past ten days, rushing along the way. After the aircraft took off, the Emperor's close attendants were worried and gathered at the airfield, constantly looking up at the sky. After safely returning, they expressed joy and praised the German pilot's aviation skills. In the morning, the Emperor spent half an hour using hand-thrown grenades to hit targets to show his ability to aim (Reuters News Agency, 23rd).

Addis Ababa: General Tasfaye, commander-in-chief of the Abyssinian 7th Army defending the strategically important town of Geladi on the southern Bari Province, received instructions today stating, "Geladi must be defended at all costs." It is now believed that the fierce battle between the main forces of Abyssinia and Italy on the southern front may be seen on the Geladi to Jijiga front line. The Abyssinian army has 300,000 soldiers, while the Italian army has 130,000 soldiers. If the Italian army captures Geladi, it will eliminate more than half of the suffering experienced in the stalemated battles in the waterless plains of the Ogaden, as the Italian army can then continue to advance along the Webi Shabelle River basin (Reuters News Agency, 23rd).

(London) According to a report today from the Addis Ababa correspondent of The Morning Post, the East African war has so far resulted in the deaths of 20,000 Abyssinian soldiers and 6,000 Italian soldiers. In addition, 200 Abyssinian women and children have also been affected. Two-thirds of the Italian army's casualties were from the 10th Corps. According to another telegram, General Graziani today led the Somali troops forward again and has occupied the village of Qitel northeast of Donnali. Abyssinian Army Minister Getachew will personally lead a million soldiers to meet the enemy. Experts watching the front lines believe that the Abyssinian army's weapons have improved because many firearms have recently been transported after European countries lifted the arms embargo on Abyssinia (National News Agency, 23rd).

Abyssinian Army Reinforces Defenses, Prepares for Counterattack and Resistance 16

Addis Ababa: According to reliable sources obtained here today, after two weeks of preparation, the Abyssinian army has now arrived at the line between Adwa and Adigrat and plans to launch a counterattack on Adigrat before the end of this week (National News, 22nd).

Addis Ababa: Abyssinian Prince Ras Desta has recently led 200,000 troops towards the Webi Shabelle River basin to resist when the Italian army invades the Ogaden Province. On the Tigray Province front, Italian aircraft dropped leaflets in the Mek'ele area, urging residents to betray the Abyssinian government. In the Walqayt area, bombs were dropped several times, but there were no casualties. There are still widespread rumors here that General Seyoum's troops are engaged in fierce battles with the Italian army, and it is also rumored that a column of Italian troops is advancing towards Lake Ashange, but the government believes that this is impossible because the climate in the Danakil area is harsh and there are many deserts, which are not suitable for large-scale troop movements (Havas News Agency, 22nd).

British Government Decides to Convene Naval Preparatory Conference: Italy and Germany Are Also Invited 17

(London) It was learned here today that Britain intends to invite major naval powers to a conference to be held in London in early November. Italy and Germany are also among those invited. The main agenda item will be the mutual notification of shipbuilding plans among the various countries (National News, 22nd).

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Navy studied the contents of the British government's invitation to the Japanese military disarmament conference on the 22nd. The British government, in accordance with Article 23 of the treaty, proposed to hold a conference of the signatory countries of the Washington and London treaties in London starting on December 2nd. France intends to invite Soviet Russia, Germany, and other member states of the League of Nations to participate in the conference. According to the Japanese government's speculation, the British government intends to convene a five-nation conference first, and if there is hope, then convene a general disarmament conference of various countries in the world. On the Japanese side, due to treaty provisions, it will naturally attend the conference, but the agenda and other hopes will be decided after the official invitation arrives (Japan United Press, 23rd).

(London) According to naval observers, part of Britain's desire to ease the tensions caused by the Italo-Abyssinian dispute lies in allowing Italy to participate in the future naval conference. The British government is very hopeful for a naval limitation policy. The Washington and London naval treaties will both expire at the end of next year. The two treaties stipulated that a naval conference be convened before the end of this year. Therefore, Britain held preliminary naval talks with the United States and Japan separately at the end of last year and hoped to have similar talks with France and Italy to find a basis for future naval treaties. During the preliminary British-Japanese-American naval talks last year, Britain initially proposed (1) quantitative restrictions and (2) graded restrictions. However, because Japan refused to consider them, it suggested qualitative restrictions on the tonnage and gun caliber of each warship. In addition, each naval power would mutually notify shipbuilding procedures. This suggestion has been accepted by the United States, but Japan has attached conditions, namely that the maximum total tonnage of the navy should be equal for Japan and other countries. As for Italy and France, they have not yet responded to the above suggestions. Recently, because time is pressing, Britain has contacted the countries concerned through diplomatic channels and announced that a preparatory meeting will be convened on December 2 of this year and will end in January next year. It also advocates that the nature of this conference should not be too formal, and the participating countries can only be represented by the ambassador to Britain and the naval attaché without having to send special representatives. Naval observers here believe that since the United States has accepted the British suggestion, Italy and France will soon accept it as well. Therefore, whether a naval agreement can be established depends on Japan's attitude. However, due to the current Italo-Abyssinian dispute, the diplomatic relations between Britain and Italy are tense, and Italy's participation in the conference is inevitably hindered. Britain is so eager to ease the diplomatic situation with Italy, and this is one reason (Havas News Agency, 22nd).

Japanese Naval Attaché: Taiwan Will Hold a Meeting to Discuss Development Strategies for South China and Southeast Asia 18

Taipei: Commander Tadao Honda, section chief of the Naval Ministry Command, attended the Shanghai meeting and boarded the Tatsuta Maru this morning to go south. It is scheduled to arrive in Keelung at 9:30 tomorrow morning. The Taiwan Army plans to hold a meeting at the Governor-General's Office in the near future to welcome Commander Honda. At the same time, a joint meeting of naval attachés stationed in Taiwan and important consular officials in South China will be held to discuss policies towards China and various issues related to development in South China and Southeast Asia (China United Press, 23rd).

Taipei: Japan considers Southeast Asia its southern lifeline and has decided to actively advance south. The Taiwan Governor-General's Office is the main base for the southern advance. It is currently planning a ten-year plan to acquire hegemony in Greater Southeast Asia. This time, when Taiwan held an unprecedented exhibition, it specially set up pavilions for Southeast Asia, Fujian, Siam, and the Philippines to encourage Japanese and Taiwanese people to advance into Southeast Asia and South China. In next year's budget, it will set up a Southeast Asian Trade Specialization Department within the Taipei Higher School of Commerce and also open night classes to teach general Southeast Asian knowledge, with special emphasis on Siamese, Malay, Dutch, French, and various dialects of Chinese, such as Chaozhou and Cantonese, to learn the skills to be active in Southeast Asia and practically advance into Southeast Asia (China United Press, 23rd).

香河秩序漸吿恢復　農民入城後組維持會另推縣長　趙縣長潛行到通奉令仍回原任　通縣駐軍開往彈壓變亂漸敉平 19

Fragrant River Order Gradually Restored; Peasants Enter City and Form Maintenance Committee, Appointing New County Magistrate; County Magistrate Zhao Secretly Arrives in Tongzhou, Ordered to Return to Original Post; Tongzhou Garrison Deployed to Suppress Riot, Gradually Pacifying

(Beiping) After the peasant uprising in Xianghe County, County Magistrate Zhao Chongyi had secretly fled. The peasants entered the city yesterday and organized a temporary maintenance committee, with local notable An Houzhai as the temporary county magistrate. According to Shang Zhen's written reply to reporters' questions, the conflict between the Xianghe militia and the county government was due to the manipulation by unscrupulous gentry in the county. The county magistrate has left the county, but local order has gradually been restored, and the situation will not escalate. The provincial government has dispatched Councilor Liu Yaodong to thoroughly investigate the matter. After obtaining detailed information, concrete measures for handling it will be decided. To maintain peace and tranquility, it is planned to dispatch a portion of the 32nd Army to suppress the uprising. I am scheduled to return to Baoding within two or three days. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) This afternoon, Shang Zhen sent Counselor Zheng Wenxuan to the Japanese Embassy to visit military attaché Takahashi, expressing that the Xianghe incident would be resolved peacefully. After the outbreak of the Xianghe peasant uprising, Zhang Qingyu, the commander of the First Regiment of the War Zone Security Force, came to Ping this morning to report the latest situation in Xianghe to the Ji-Mi District Office. It is rumored that similar incidents have occurred in Sanhe, Wuqing, and other counties due to the Xianghe peasant uprising, but relevant parties have strongly denied this. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The rioters in Xianghe had not retreated by the night of the 22nd. All gates of the county town were tightly closed and fortified with sandbags, guarded by the security corps. The rioters focused on the east gate, constantly clamoring and firing guns. The whereabouts of County Magistrate Zhao Xiyu are still unknown. The chief of the public security bureau, Bai Chunzhi, and the chief inspector, Bai Xiangshun, were detained outside the city in the Chenghuang Temple. One battalion of the 135th Division of the 32nd Army has been concentrated in Tongzhou awaiting deployment. The rioters issued absurd declarations on the 23rd, exceeding the original four demands. Tongzhou was placed under martial law on the 23rd, with County Magistrate Cao Zhen and Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Xiu guarding the city with police forces. Zhang Qingyu, the commander of the First Security Regiment, went to Ping early on the 23rd to meet with Shang Zhen for instructions. It is heard that the leader of the rioters, Wu Zhenyi, has been arrested by the Japanese army and sent to Ping for questioning. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Military Branch held a routine meeting on the morning of the 23rd, attended by Bao Wen-yue, Shang Zhen, Qin Dechun, and more than ten others. Bao Wen-yue presided over the meeting. After passing several routine cases, Shang reported on the Xianghe peasant uprising. It was resolved that the provincial government would be responsible for handling the matter. Also, Shang sent personnel to the Japanese Embassy in the afternoon to explain the Xianghe incident, deciding to resolve it peacefully. The Japanese side was quite understanding. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Beiping) The provincial government appointed Councilor Liu Yaodong as the acting county magistrate of Xianghe. Liu, escorted by one battalion of the 32nd Army, went to Xianghe today to take office but was rejected by the rioters. Liu is currently in the city. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to a telephone call from Xianghe on the afternoon of the 23rd, many people have gathered again in the villages outside the city, and efforts are being made to resolve the situation. The order within the city is still good, with the local police maintaining public security. It is also reported that there is instability in Sanhe, but the situation is not very serious. Security teams in each county have been dispatched to strictly guard against any escalation of the situation. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Beiping) Regarding the Xianghe peasant uprising, relevant parties received a telephone call from the county on the 23rd, stating that the rioters entered the city on the afternoon of the 22nd, and County Magistrate Zhao Xiliang and other staff members abandoned their posts and fled. County administration is currently without leadership. According to Shang Zhen's reply to reporters' questions, the disappearance of the Xianghe County Magistrate has been confirmed. The provincial government has sent personnel to investigate thoroughly. Zhang Qingyu, the commander of the First Security Regiment, and Li Yun-sheng, the commander of the Fifth Regiment, both came to Ping on the morning of the 23rd to meet with Shang and report on the defense of each county. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Beiping) It is reported here that villains in Wuqing and Changping counties are also inciting troublemakers to riot. Bai Jianwu's bandit gang previously attempted to launch an uprising in Zunhua and other places, but because it was detected and suppressed, they knew they could not succeed and secretly hid in counties bordering the war zone, plotting a comeback. Bai himself issued orders from Dalian. It is heard that the Japanese side is very dissatisfied with this and hopes to eliminate them as soon as possible. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Beiping) According to a telephone call from Tongzhou on the evening of the 23rd, County Magistrate Zhao Xiyuan of Xianghe arrived in Tongzhou at noon on the 23rd and reported to the Ji-Mi Special Office. At the same time, Provincial Councilor Liu Yaodong and Meng Zhaoen, the commander of the First Security Regiment, also returned to Tongzhou from Xianghe to investigate. As a result of their joint deliberation, it was decided that since the rioters in Xianghe had dispersed and the situation had stabilized, Zhao was ordered to return to the county to resume his duties and be responsible for handling the issue of tax increases. Zhao immediately complied with the order and went to the county. Also, An Houzhai, who was elected as the acting county magistrate by the rioters, also came to Tongzhou on the 23rd to welcome Zhao back to the county. One report said that An had been detained, but the truth remains to be seen. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Baoding) Regarding the Xianghe peasant uprising, the provincial government dispatched inspector Wang Runsheng from the Department of Civil Affairs on the morning of the 22nd to investigate and handle the matter. At 5:00 PM on the 23rd, Wang reported to the Department of Civil Affairs by telegram from Tongzhou that the garrison in Tongzhou had been deployed to Xianghe to suppress the uprising as appropriate. The city gates had been opened, and order was gradually being restored, but County Magistrate Zhao Zhongpu and Chief of Public Security Section Bai Chunzhi were still missing. According to Li Peiji's statement to reporters, the rioters' claims of opposing tax increases were not true. According to another report, the Xianghe incident was initiated by the local unscrupulous gentry Wu Huan (i.e., Wu Yi). Wu and Bai Jianwu are sworn brothers, so there may be some collusion between them. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Beiping) According to news received at night, the Xianghe Security Corps had opened the city and surrendered to the peasants. After the peasants' initial attack on the city failed yesterday, they gathered a large force again in the evening and approached the city. The Security Corps, seeing that they were outnumbered and to avoid bloodshed, opened the city and admitted them. After entering the city, the peasants immediately organized a Security Committee and appointed Hu Yuting (transliteration), the leader of this uprising, to preside over everything. An Houzhai, the former president of the Beiping Chamber of Commerce, was elected as the county magistrate. As of yesterday, six Japanese plainclothes ronin who participated in the riot were detained by the Japanese military police. There have been no further reports, and it is now believed that they have been sent to Tianjin. (23rd Reuters)

中央政治會議 20

Central Political Conference

通過水災工賑公債發行原則

Passes the Principle of Issuing Public Bonds for Flood Relief and Public Works

(Nanjing) The Central Political Conference held its 480th meeting at 8:00 AM on the 23rd, attended by more than thirty people including Wang Zhaoming, Yu Youren, Ye Chucang, Chen Guofu, Sun Ke, Ju Zheng, Chen Gongbo, Bai Wenwei, Dai Chuanxian, Chuan Rulin, and Hong Ludong. Sun Ke chaired the meeting, which resolved the following important cases: (1) Passed the principle of the Regulations on the Registration of Military and Civilian Personnel and the principle of the Regulations on the Examination of Qualifications, Grades, and Salaries for the Transfer of Military and Civilian Personnel to Ordinary Civil Servants, to be submitted to the Legislative Yuan. (2) Passed the principle of issuing public bonds for flood relief and public works in the year 1935, to be submitted to the Legislative Yuan. (3) Ratified the National Government's approval of the resignation of Wang Yingyu, chairman of the Gansu Provincial Committee and concurrently director of the Department of Civil Affairs, and appointed Sun Xiwen to fill the vacancy. (4) Ratified the National Government's removal of Wang Youyong from all posts, including chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Committee and concurrently director of the Department of Civil Affairs, and appointed Wang Cifu to fill the vacancy. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) The principle of issuing public bonds for flood relief and public works, which was passed by the Central Political Conference on the 23rd, has been submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. The amount is 20 million yuan, to be issued in nine installments. It will be submitted to the National Government for approval next month. The repayment period is set at twelve years, with interest paid twice a year in April and late October, until October 31, 1947, when the entire amount will be repaid. The method of repayment will still be determined by lottery. The repayment and interest payment fund will be allocated from the disaster relief reserve fund. Repayment will be allocated from customs duties. When the public bonds are issued, a portion may be allocated to the salaries of civil servants. The percentage and duration of this allocation will be drafted by the Ministry of Finance. It is heard that the Ministry is already studying this matter, and after drafting it, it will be submitted to Minister of Finance Kong for review and then submitted to the Executive Yuan for decision. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Yu Youren, the president of the Control Yuan, returned to Nanjing from Shanghai on the morning of the 23rd to attend the Central Political Conference. In the afternoon, he went to the Yuan to handle official business. (23rd Special Dispatch)

立法院　今日開臨時會　專審議憲草修正案 21

Legislative Yuan to Hold Extraordinary Session Today, Solely to Deliberate Draft Constitution Amendment

(Nanjing) Sun Ke and Chuan Bingchang returned to Nanjing from Shanghai on the morning of the 23rd. Sun attended the Central Political Conference and then summoned the committee members responsible for reviewing the draft constitution amendment at his residence for discussions. Also, the Legislative Yuan will convene an extraordinary session on the afternoon of the 24th, solely to deliberate the draft constitution amendment. The regular session on the 25th will still be held as usual and will deliberate on important cases such as the Organization Law of the Provincial Civil Service Commission. (23rd Central News Agency)

Dai Mingli from the Ministry of Finance attended the meeting to present his views. The committee has now compiled all the opinions on the revision of the stamp tax rate from all parties and has thoroughly reviewed them. It will prepare an amendment to the stamp tax rate table based on the review results and submit it to the Yuan for deliberation. (23rd Central News Agency)

秦德純返張垣 22

Qin Dechun Returns to Zhangjiakou

(Beiping) Qin Dechun arrived in Ping a few days ago to welcome Song Zheyuan to inspect the stationed troops of the 29th Army under his command in Chahar. Song has been busy with military affairs and will not go to Chahar for the time being. Qin left Ping tonight to return to Zhangjiakou to manage provincial affairs. (23rd Special Dispatch)

蒙會三屆大會　審醒經費自治各案　責成妥員草防花有效辦法雲委長病已霍然蒞會視察 23

Third Session of the Mongolian Conference Reviews Financial and Autonomous Matters; Competent Personnel Tasked with Drafting Effective Measures to Prevent Bandits; Chairman Yun, Recovered from Illness, Attends the Conference to Inspect

Bailingmiao The members of the Mongolian Political Council have arrived in the temple one after another to attend the Third General Assembly. The first meeting was held at 2:00 PM on the 21st, with 19 members including Yideqin attending. Chairman Yun presided over the meeting, leading the members to perform the rituals as required. During the subsequent discussion of the agenda, the matter of defending against communist bandits was discussed in detail. The task of drafting effective measures to defend against communist bandits has been assigned to competent personnel, who are currently working on it based on the decisions of the General Assembly. It was also decided to divide the attending members into the first and second groups to review the agenda separately. The first group review meeting was held from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM on the 22nd, with 14 members attending, chaired by convener Yideqin. The group reviewed many cases, including how to reduce the budget of the Council for the year 1935, which had been reduced by 5% by the Central Government, in order to balance income and expenditure. The second group review meeting was held from 3:00 PM to 5:00 PM, with 14 members attending, chaired by convener Ni Guanzhou. The group reviewed many cases, including the prompt establishment of an autonomous training institute. (22nd Central News Agency)

Bailingmiao Chairman Yun of the Mongolian Political Council, due to his advanced age, has been recuperating at home due to illness. His condition has suddenly improved, and he has recovered without medication. He visited the conference on the 13th to personally inspect the various offices and departments, walking strongly and in high spirits. (23rd Central News Agency)

行政院審查　連雲港設市案 24

Executive Yuan Reviews Case of Establishing Lianyungang as a City

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan convened the Ministries of Interior and Finance, among others, at 9:00 AM on the 23rd to review the case of establishing Lianyungang as a city. As a result, opinions on the matters that should be prepared in advance have been drafted and will be submitted to the Yuan for approval before being submitted to the Yuan's meeting for discussion. (23rd Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) There are conflicting reports about the establishment of Lianyungang as a city. An official in charge of the Executive Yuan said that there is no formal proposal to establish Lianyungang as a city. The Jiangsu Provincial Government only established a Lianyungang Municipal Preparatory Office and requested to file a report. The Yuan discussed and submitted it for review, and there were some opinions on the preparatory matters that should be noted. These are still being sorted out and will be submitted to the President of the Yuan for review before being submitted to the meeting for discussion. The news that the Executive Yuan did not approve the establishment of Lianyungang as a city is a misunderstanding. (23rd Special Dispatch)

訪晤汪院長即晚復來滬

Visit Premier Wang and Return to Shanghai the Same Evening

(Nanjing) U.S. Secretary of War Dern and his wife, accompanied by their son and Major General Kirk, as well as U.S. Ambassador Johnson and others, arrived in Beijing at 7:00 AM on the 23rd. Cao Haosen from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and staff from the U.S. Embassy greeted them. After getting off the train, they went to the embassy to rest. At 4:00 PM, they went to the official residence of the Minister of Railways to visit Premier Wang and convey their greetings. At 5:00 PM, they attended a tea party at He Yingqin's private residence. At 8:00 PM, Wang hosted a banquet for Dern and other heads of various ministries and commissions at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. At 11:00 PM, they returned to Shanghai by night express train with their entourage. They are scheduled to leave Shanghai for the Philippines by the same ship on the 25th. Dern told reporters in the morning that he was very pleased to have the opportunity to visit the capital of your country. He had no other mission in Beijing besides paying respects to the authorities. He wanted to visit the villages of your country and see the lives of the people, but unfortunately, he could not fulfill his wish due to the short time. (23rd Central News Agency)

Wang, accompanied by Tan Shaohua, Secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, received him and exchanged pleasantries for twenty minutes before he departed. At 4:00 PM, he attended a tea party hosted by Minister He. He attended a banquet hosted by Premier Wang in the evening. He returned to Shanghai by night train at 11:00 PM. (23rd Special Dispatch)

津日人商會　請減輕進口稅 34

Tianjin Japanese Chamber of Commerce Requests Reduction of Import Taxes

(Tianjin) The Japanese Chamber of Commerce here will submit a letter to Ambassador Arima, requesting him to convey to the Nanjing government a request to reduce import tariffs on foreign goods. The Japanese Chamber of Commerce passed this resolution today, believing that reducing import tariffs on foreign goods is the only way to reduce large-scale smuggling, as the legitimate business of the Japanese is greatly affected by smuggling. The Chamber of Commerce also passed a resolution requesting Japanese Chambers of Commerce in Shanghai and other places to make the same request. It is heard that the Japanese will advocate for (1) reducing the current import tax on cotton yarn by half, and (2) reducing the import tax on wool textiles by one-third. (23rd Reuters)

榆關人力車夫罷工　向日領館請願 35

Shanhaiguan Rickshaw Pullers Strike, Petition Japanese Consulate

(Tianjin) Rickshaw pullers in Shanhaiguan went on a general strike on the 20th and petitioned the Japanese Consulate, demanding: 1. Severely punish the perpetrators; 2. Compensate for medical expenses and losses; 3. Guarantee that similar incidents will not occur again in the future. On the morning of the 22nd, after persuasion by the Japanese military police and the consulate, some have resumed work. The reason for the strike is that a Korean guest, Park Fenglin, at the Tiantai Inn hired 19 rickshaws to transport smuggled goods back and forth, paying only three dimes per trip. Afterwards, he refused to pay and gathered a crowd to beat the rickshaw pullers, seriously injuring 17 and slightly injuring several others, leading to public outrage. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Shi and Liu's Followers Secretly Incite Bandits

Beining Railway Constructs Luggage and Ticket Offices at Yuguan Station

The funds will be advanced by the Beining Railway from its own revenue. The Bureau has recently completed the design and will purchase all materials this year and begin construction next spring. Some of the construction will continue after the completion of the second phase of the project. The Beining Railway, due to the cramped office space of the Tianjin General Bureau, is building a three-story building next to the General Bureau at a construction cost of 300,000 yuan. Construction has already begun and is scheduled to be completed in July of next year. All affiliated agencies of the Bureau will be moved in for the convenience of operations. (23rd Special Dispatch)

窰灣被災極重 40

Yaowan Severely Affected by Disaster

宿城以上運水見跌海屬各河漲落無定

Shipping Water Above Sucheng Declines; Rivers in Coastal Region Experience Erratic Fluctuations

(Xuzhou) Report from Sucheng: Yaowan has been severely affected by the disaster. The province previously allocated 500 yuan for rescue efforts. Subsequently, the Provincial Disaster Relief Committee and the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association each allocated 2,000 yuan for relief. The provincial government has now allocated another 6,000 yuan and dispatched Du Yuncheng to Suqian to immediately investigate and distribute emergency relief in the disaster areas of Yaowan and Zhaohe. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Xuzhou) The rivers in the coastal region experience erratic fluctuations due to the influence of tides. The Special Commissioner's Office has ordered the Donghai, Guanyun, and Muyang counties to set up water level markers at key points and report water levels to each other, specifying that Donghai report the water levels of Xinpu and Sitou Dike, Muyang report the water levels of Chengnan and Yangkou, and Guanyun report the water levels of Chengxi and Dayishan. Water levels have been falling in recent days. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Qingjiangpu) The Shuoshuida Dam in Liu Laojian, Suqian, was ordered by the provincial government to be demolished on the 22nd by the Flood Control Office. The shipping water above Suqian dropped sharply, and Youwan in Siyang overflowed. All large and small sluice gates along the inland canal below Huaiyin, a total of eight in Huaian and twenty-seven in Baoying, were opened today. According to people from Yangzhou and Zhenjiang, the shipping water below Jieshou is low, so there is no need to open the large and small sluice gates within Gaoyou. (23rd Special Dispatch)

湘魯請撥賑欵 41

Hunan and Shandong Request Allocation of Relief Funds

(Nanjing) Han Fuju, the chairman of Shandong Province, stated that the disaster situation in his province this year is extremely severe, and the financial resources of the provincial treasury and donations from various parties are limited. He has again telegraphed the Executive Yuan requesting an allocation of 10 million yuan from the water disaster public bonds issued by the Central Government for relief in Shandong Province. Also, He Jian, the chairman of Hunan Province, has telegraphed the Executive Yuan requesting an allocation of 5 million yuan from the new public bonds. The Executive Yuan has handed this over to the Ministry of Finance for consideration. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Shandong Provincial Government has requested the Central Government that all civil servant disaster relief donations and income taxes payable to the Central Government be retained for disaster relief in the province, which has been approved by the Central Government. (23rd Special Dispatch)

美方計劃太平洋航空 48

American Plans for Pacific Aviation

(Nanjing) The United States originally planned to make Hong Kong the terminus for Pacific aviation, but due to unsuccessful negotiations with the Hong Kong authorities, it changed to negotiate with the Portuguese authorities in Macau, changing the terminus to Macau. Both parties agreed. According to sources from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the air route is being organized by Xunmei Airlines. Recently, it has not contacted our side. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not received any news from the company regarding its desire to connect with our country's air routes. According to China Aviation Corporation, the air route is entirely organized by the United States and has no relationship with China or China Aviation Corporation. (23rd Special Dispatch)

鐵部編竣工作報吿 49

Ministry of Railways Completes Work Report

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways' work report for the Sixth Plenary Session of the Fifth National Congress has been completed and submitted to the Executive Yuan on the 23rd, for transmittal to the Secretariat of the Congress. It totals 120 pages and includes: 1. Railway Construction, such as the construction of the Yue-Han, Long-Hai, and Su-Jia railway lines, and the Qiantang River Bridge on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. 2. Seaport Construction, such as the construction of Lianyungang. 3. Business Consolidation, divided into old management items, reform items, and consolidation items. 4. Financial Consolidation, such as the liquidation of old and new debts, preparation of funds for construction materials, and auditing of business income and expenditure. 5. Promotion of Railway Education, including specialized education, Rotary education, and employee education. 6. Consolidation of old railways, such as repairing the tracks of various lines and improving the application of machinery. 7. Railway Police Management. 8. Other railway policies. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Special telegram, 23rd)

Chief Auditor of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Completes Inspection of Branch Operations 51

Ministry of Finance Pays Attention to Salt Affairs in Border Provinces 52

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance noted that after the abolition of the salt transport offices in Gansu, Ningxia, and Qinghai provinces, salt sales have decreased year by year. This spring, Shui Chongxun was appointed as the Director-General of the Northwest Salt Affairs and Revenue Bureau. In July of this year, he took over the Gansu Salt Monopoly Bureau, which was abolished, and reorganized the Northwest Salt Affairs Commissioner's Office. The takeover of the Qinghai Salt Transport Bureau is currently being negotiated with the local authorities of that province. Salt affairs in Ningxia Province, which were originally under the joint jurisdiction of the Northwest Bureau with Gansu and Qinghai, are being negotiated with Chairman Ma. (Special telegram, 23rd)

Anti-Opium General Supervision Department Decides Not to Establish a Separate Intelligence Office 53

(Nanjing) The Anti-Opium General Supervision Department initially planned to establish an intelligence office in Kyoto to handle external anti-opium intelligence matters. However, to save expenses, it has been decided not to establish a separate office, and the General Supervision Department will handle it directly. (Special telegram, 23rd)

Wuhan Intermodal Transportation to Adopt Railway Ferry Method 54

(Nanjing) After the completion of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, intermodal transportation in Wuhan will adopt the railway ferry method. The Ministry of Railways has instructed the Pinghan and Xiang'e Railway Bureaus to jointly prepare an engineering plan for submission and approval. (Central News Agency telegram, 23rd)

Number of Examinees in This Year's Higher Civil Service Examination 55

(Nanjing) The confirmed number of examinees for this year's higher civil service examination has been announced by the Examination Commission. There are a total of 3,940 people, including 56 women. 2,263 candidates are taking the exam in Kyoto, 1,041 in Peiping, 226 in Shaanxi, and 410 in Guangdong. The most candidates are applying for general administrative and judicial positions, each exceeding 1,000 people. The fewest candidates are applying for health personnel, with only 27 people. The applicants mainly come from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, and Hebei provinces. Admission tickets will be issued starting from the 29th. (Central News Agency telegram, 23rd)

Sino-British-American Wireless Telephone Service 58

(Nanjing) According to information from the Ministry of Communications, when the Ministry signed a wireless communications contract with Japan last year, it stipulated the opening of wireless telephone service. It has been over a year, but due to unresolved technical issues, it has not been realized. It is now anticipated that official calls can commence formally by mid-February next spring. Flour and Wheat Prices Soar in Tianjin 62

(Tianjin) Overseas flour and wheat have not been imported for two weeks due to the Italo-Abyssinian War, causing flour and wheat prices in Tianjin to soar. Coarse grains have also been affected and their prices have increased. Flour mills are traveling as far as Xi'an to purchase wheat. If Australian flour does not arrive by mid-December, flour and wheat prices will rise further. The Social Affairs Bureau is preparing to stabilize prices. (Special telegram, 23rd)
