Gansu's Trade Statistics for the First Half of This Year 78

Total exports exceed 13.37 million yuan, total imports exceed 27.5 million yuan, and total import surplus exceeds 14.13 million yuan.

Gansu's trade statistics for the first half of this year (January to June) have now been formally published by the Gansu Department of Finance based on commodity tax receipts and are listed below for the reference of those concerned about the trade situation in Gansu.

(A) Exports totaled over 13,372,362 yuan, including 3,740 dan of hides and skins, valued at 6,732,415 yuan, accounting for 50.35% of total exports; 35,552 dan of medicinal materials, valued at 2,986,335 yuan, accounting for 22.33% of total exports; 36,326 dan of wool, valued at 817,341 yuan, accounting for 6.11% of total exports; 99,376 dan of shredded tobacco, valued at 656,288 yuan, accounting for 4.90% of total exports; 272 dan of sheep casings, valued at 544,960 yuan, accounting for 4.06% of total exports; 519 dan of food, valued at 519,300 yuan, accounting for 3.90% of total exports; 5,927 dan of cotton tobacco, valued at 518,976 yuan, accounting for 3.89% of total exports; 56,842 pieces of timber, valued at 284,210 yuan, accounting for 2.12% of total exports; 1,368 postal parcels, valued at 164,160 yuan, accounting for 1.20% of total exports; 1,352 dan of bamboo ware, valued at 80,965 yuan, accounting for 0.60% of total exports; and 499 dan of other goods, valued at 67,413 yuan, accounting for 0.48% of total exports.

(B) Imports totaled just under 27,507,200 yuan, including 15,290 dan of food, valued at 15,289,530 yuan, accounting for 55.56% of total imports; 13,431 dan of foreign cloth, valued at 2,887,576 yuan, accounting for 10.48% of total imports; 19,566 dan of sundries, valued at 2,636,466 yuan, accounting for 9.57% of total imports; 2,520 dan of cotton goods, valued at 1,547,293 yuan, accounting for 5.60% of total imports; 5,663 dan of porcelain, valued at 1,260,800 yuan, accounting for 4.59% of total imports; 9,104 dan of paper, valued at 1,001,486 yuan, accounting for 3.65% of total imports; 5,739 postal parcels, valued at 688,680 yuan, accounting for 2.52% of total imports; 7,939 rolls of native cloth, valued at 555,730 yuan, accounting for 2.02% of total imports; 269 tickets of official tea, valued at 473,616 yuan, accounting for 1.73% of total imports; 3,726 twists of metal, valued at 279,464 yuan, accounting for 1.02% of total imports; 1,746 dan of other goods, valued at 261,915 yuan, accounting for 0.56% of total imports; 144,484 draws of bulk tea, valued at 216,726 yuan, accounting for 0.79% of total imports; 3,605 dan of cotton, valued at 173,063 yuan, accounting for 0.63% of total imports; 203 boxes of cigarettes, valued at 101,525 yuan, accounting for 0.37% of total imports; 143 boxes of cigars, valued at 71,380 yuan, accounting for 0.27% of total imports; and 31 dan of silk fabrics, valued at 61,940 yuan, accounting for 0.23% of total imports.

Comparing the two sides of imports and exports, hides and skins have been the largest item in exports in the last half year, accounting for more than half of the total amount, followed by medicinal materials and wool, and other types of goods are the least. In the last half year of imports, food has been the largest item, accounting for about 60% of the total amount, followed by foreign cloth and groceries, and silk fabrics are the least, accounting for only 0.23% of the total amount. It can be seen that the people's livelihood in Gansu Province is declining. Apart from the daily necessities of clothing and food, there is no other purchasing power. As for the import surplus situation, it is as serious as ever. The total value of imports and exports in January was 7,240,625 yuan, and the import surplus was 4,802,976 yuan. The total value of imports and exports in February was 5,281,997 yuan, and the import surplus was 3,090,316 yuan. The total value of imports and exports in March was 8,387,418 yuan, and the import surplus was 678,482 yuan. The total value of imports and exports in April was 6,873,553 yuan, and the import surplus was 1,003,175 yuan. The total value of imports and exports in May was 7,886,243 yuan, and the import surplus was 2,693,810 yuan. The total value of imports and exports in June was 5,209,723 yuan, and the import surplus was 1,866,079 yuan. Although the import surplus amounts for the above months vary due to seasonal factors, the statistics for the first half of the year reached a huge amount of more than 14,134,800 yuan, which is enough to make people worry about the future of the social economy in Gansu Province. It is now learned that the Director of the Finance Department, Zhu Jinglei, is studying how to remedy the trade import surplus problem. In addition to revising import tax rates and increasing import taxes as a passive resistance, he also intends to promote local products as a slightly positive supplement in order to reduce the import surplus.

The Xikang Pacification Commissioner, Nona, Speaks and Acts in Kang 79

—Convening a Pacification Conference for All Sectors—

A dispatch from Kyoto states that the Communication Office in Kyoto for the representatives of 39 ethnic groups in the northwest of Kangzang recently received a report from Xikang. The Xikang Pacification Commissioner, Nona Hutuktu, has been in Kangding for nearly two months since being appointed. The Living Buddhas, abbots, managers, and lamas of the red and yellow sects from various places have traveled long distances to pay homage. Although the Living Buddha Nona is over 70 years old, he is energetic and tirelessly receives people day and night, vigorously propagating the central government's power and virtue. He has successively convened representative conferences from all sectors several times and has decided on several important cases: (1) To awaken the entire population to support the central government, urgently seek unity, and assist the national army in suppressing bandits, while training the people to organize local self-defense to prevent future troubles; (2) To achieve a great religious union, engage in rectifying religious rules, improving old systems and bad habits, promoting the true meaning of religion, and saving the world's people; (3) To eliminate all past Kang-Han divisions, guide emotional harmony, and jointly plan the construction of Xikang. The people of Kang generally express sincere love and respect for Living Buddha Nona's pacification efforts, his promotion of virtue, his concern for the people's suffering, and his prescription of appropriate remedies. The people, from now on, have leadership and will not engage in actions contrary to the central government. In the future, everything in Xikang will be impressive.

Eight Months of Trade in Fujian Province This Year 80

Far Removed from the Prosperity of the 18th and 19th Years of the Republic; Fuzhou Customs' Trade Surplus Turns into a Deficit

(Xiamen Correspondence) In recent years, Fujian Province has suffered from the global economic downturn and successive years of communist banditry. The people's livelihood has deteriorated, and industries have declined, becoming increasingly severe. This year is even worse. According to customs' figures, for the eight months from January to August this year, foreign trade through Fuzhou Min Customs shows imports valued at 5,010,000 national currency units, and exports at 2,155,000 national currency units, resulting in an import surplus of 2,855,000 national currency units. Xiamen Customs shows imports valued at 10,738,000 national currency units, and exports at 2,196,000 national currency units, resulting in an import surplus of 8,542,000 national currency units. Santu'ao Customs shows imports valued at 118,000 national currency units, and exports at 3,000 national currency units, resulting in an import surplus of 115,000 national currency units.

Page 8

The combined totals for the three customs offices show imports valued at 15,866,000 national currency units, exports at 4,354,000 national currency units, resulting in an import surplus of 11,512,000 national currency units. It is noted that Fujian Province's economy originally relied on northern Fujian as the production area and southern Fujian as the consumption area. Therefore, traditionally, Fuzhou's Min Customs has always had a trade surplus, while Xiamen has been a notorious import surplus port for more than sixty years since its opening. Considering Fujian Province's trade in the 18th and 19th years of the Republic, in the 18th year, Min Customs had imports of 8,193,618 customs taels (one customs tael is equivalent to approximately 1.5 national currency units), and exports of 14,843,900 customs taels, resulting in a surplus of 6,649,282 taels. Xiamen had imports of 17,215,879 taels, and exports of 3,909,448 taels, resulting in a deficit of 13,296,431 taels. In the 19th year, already affected by the global economic panic, Min Customs had imports of 6,718,175 taels, and exports of 8,845,953 taels, still resulting in a surplus of 2,127,778 taels. Xiamen, due to the sharp rise in gold prices and soaring foreign exchange rates, saw overseas Chinese rush to remit funds back home to invest in land and construction, hence the year saw increased prosperity. Imports reached 22,027,7018 taels, and exports reached 3,591,905 taels, resulting in a deficit of 18,435,113 taels. Trade at Santu'ao was minimal, similar to the present situation. Min Customs' surplus in the 18th year of the Republic, when converted to national currency, reached 10 million units, whereas in the eight months of this year, it has reversed to a deficit of over 2 million units. Moreover, the total value of imports is less than a quarter of that of the 18th year of the Republic, and exports are less than one-sixth. Xiamen's deficit for the eight months is over 8.5 million units. Compared to the deficit of over 27.65 million national currency units in the 19th year, it seems much less. However, in the 19th year, Xiamen's imports reached over 33 million national currency units, while this year for eight months it is only 10.73 million, a shrinkage of more than half. Exports in the 19th year amounted to over 5.38 million national currency units, while this year for eight months they are over 2.19 million, a decrease of 20 percent. From this, we can see the severity of Fujian Province's economic downturn. The reasons being that production in northern Fujian has lost its world market, remittances from overseas Chinese in southern Fujian have sharply decreased, consumption has been tightened, and purchasing power is weak, resulting in a large drop in land prices in Xiamen, with stores along the streets closing one after another, and many empty houses. The reduction in the value of imports also has one loophole, which is the large number of smuggled foreign goods entering in recent years to avoid taxes. According to reports, Pingtan County, an island along the coast separated from Taiwan by a strip of water, is reachable by sailboat in eight hours from Keelung in Taipei. Situated between Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Taiwan, it is actually a hub for smuggled, tax-evading foreign goods entering between Taiwan and Fujian. The main items are wool and cotton textiles, sugar, and opium dross. On average, foreign goods valued at over 500,000 units are imported into the coastal areas of Fujian Province through this route each month. The Xiamen Customs has set up a Guanyin'ao sub-station here, but only catches three or four out of a hundred cases. Recently, it has started to be more effective, with successive seizures. In addition, there are still many cases of goods being transported directly from Taiwan by sailboats or motorboats and landed in the Quanzhou, Zhangzhou, and Xiamen areas. In early October, on the Zengcuo'an coast outside Xiamen port, there was a shootout between smugglers protecting their cargo and customs patrol boats, resulting in the seizure of over ten bags of sugar. A few days ago, a German ship seized a smuggling sailboat off the coast of Xiamen, carrying 100 barrels of alcohol, 30 boxes of matches, 100 boxes of gasoline, and 32 bolts of cloth. According to the helmsman Cai Ziran, the cargo he was carrying was worth 1,900 Japanese yen and he was transporting it on behalf of the cargo owner. The cargo owner wouldn't lose money as long as only one out of every three shipments were seized. Therefore, taking a risky trip across the sea would net a profit of over 200 units. If one shipment is seized, the confiscation is worth 300-400 units and a fine of 80 or 100 units is also required. However, losing one out of three trips would still be enough to break even, and not losing in one out of three trips would already guarantee a solid profit of 600-700 gold units. (October 17)

Black Gang Kou Siphon of the Yellow River Holds Water Release Ceremony 81

—Six Years of Work, Partial Success in Small Test—

Kaifeng Correspondence: The idea of using siphons to draw water from the Yellow River to irrigate farmland was proposed in the 19th year of the Republic by Huang Fang, the Director of the Henan Construction Department. By the end of the 20th year, the provincial government officially decided to implement it. Now, after six years, the water release ceremony was held at Black Gang Kou at 2:00 PM on the 20th. Liu Zhi and other important party, government, and military figures, as well as Qu Dacheng, the representative of the Ministry of Finance, Zhu Guangcai, the representative of the Economic Committee, and observers from all walks of life, a total of more than 500 people, attended the meeting as scheduled. First, Zhang Jingyu, the Director of the Construction Department, reported on the progress of the project. Next, Liu Zhi, Qu Dacheng, and Zhu Guangcai delivered speeches, and Zhang Hanying gave a lecture. After taking photos, it was already 4:00 PM. Together, they traveled by car to visit the siphon and various projects along the Yellow River. Entering the city through the West Gate, it was already dark. Although the pair of siphons installed at Liuyuan Kou often had problems with water intake due to sedimentation in the water storage pool near the river, and only one-third of the three pairs installed at Black Gang Kou were actually passing water, it is difficult to expect them to raise the water level of the silted pool, consolidate river defenses, irrigate farmland along the Huiji River, and transform saline-alkali land into fertile land as hoped. However, the small test has been successful, and continued efforts will be a blessing for the people along the river. The following is a brief record of Zhang Jingyu's report: The purposes of using siphons to draw water are: (1) to supplement the water source of the Huiji River; (2) to improve the waterways in the provincial capital. The Huiji River was originally a major river in eastern Henan, passing through Chenliu, Qi County, Sui County, Tuocheng, and Luyi, and flowing into the Wo River, providing irrigation for farmland on both banks. Later, the Yellow River repeatedly breached its banks, and over 180 kilometers of fertile land on both banks were transformed into sandy soil. In January of the 22nd year, we mobilized labor to excavate the riverbed, as a source of water and to remove dirt from the provincial capital, and to improve the soil quality. A branch canal was opened from the east bank of the Huanghui River in Sunlitang Village in the western suburbs of Kaifeng, diverting water through the northwest city walls, into Pan Yang Lake, and further divided into east and west branches. The west branch follows the city south, passes through Bao Fu Keng Lake, turns east, and heads towards the Shuimen Dong gate in the east of the city. The east branch passes through Pan Yang Lake to the north, flows around Beimen Dajie, turns south along the east of the city, joins the west branch, passes through the Shuimen Dong gate out of the city walls, and into the Huiji River. However, this requires using siphons to draw water. Because Liuyuan and Black Gang are close to the city, with the riverbed close to the south bank, and each has a deep pool, the water drawn out allows sediment to settle, and the silted pool can increase river defense security. Therefore, two pipes were installed at Liuyuan Kou, totaling 126 meters in length, and six pipes were installed at Black Gang, divided into three locations. The first and second locations are 90 meters apart, and the first and third locations are 75 meters apart. The pipes are 118 meters long, and each pipe can carry approximately 0.8 cubic meters per second at low water levels, with all eight pipes carrying over 6 cubic meters, capable of irrigating over 200,000 mu of land. Accompanying projects include six newly built bridges on the Huiji River, five renovated houses, thirty culverts installed, four newly built bridges on the Huanghui River, twenty bridges built in the city's waterways, thirty-seven culverts, two protective dikes, and sluice gates built on the Black Gang dike, all of which have been completed one after another, etc. (October 20)

Two Charity Organizations Jointly Organize Relief for the Yangtze River Floods 82

—Funds allocated first to Huaianing and other counties in Anhui Province for distribution—

Wuhu Correspondence: The Yangtze River floods this summer were most severe in Hubei Province, followed by Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, and other provinces. As autumn ends and winter approaches, the disaster victims are crying out in hunger and cold, suffering terribly. In addition to the Central Relief Commission and the provincial compatriots abroad who are doing their best to provide relief, the Shanghai General Office of the Southeast China Branches of the World Red Swastika Society is also working together to provide relief. According to the person in charge of the Wuhu Red Swastika Society, the General Office has dispatched Presidents Han Fuhang and Li Tianzhen to lead relief teams to set off to the flood-stricken areas of the Yangtze River provinces to conduct district-by-district inspections and distributions. They passed through Wuhu in the middle of this month and went to Hubei and Hunan provinces to work deep in the disaster areas. In order to gather strength to help the disaster victims, the office has also negotiated with the China International Famine Relief Commission and agreed to jointly organize Yangtze River relief efforts. The total amount of relief funds stipulated by the Red Swastika Society is 100,000 units, and 80,000 units have now been collected and handed over to the relief teams for distribution. For Anhui Province, a portion will be allocated first to Huaianing, Fanchang, Dangtu, and other counties where the disaster situation is more serious. The seven or eight counties with lighter disasters, such as Tongling and Guichi, will be allocated funds after the relief funds are fully raised. Within the province, the Anhui Central and Southern Joint Office of the Red Swastika Society moved from Anqing to Wuhu on the 22nd and was attached to the Red Swastika Branch in Jihe Street. The Society will convene representatives from various county branches to Wuhu to plan relief for disaster victims throughout the province. In addition, the China Relief Committee believes that the counties in this province have suffered from widespread floods and droughts, and that there are many disaster victims. Winter is approaching, and they lack the means to keep warm. It has specially allocated 90 bundles of donated clothing from the Capital Circles Disaster Relief Donation Committee, including single-layer and padded clothing, totaling 10,000 pieces, and telegraphed the provincial government to quickly send personnel to Beijing to collect them and transport them to the disaster areas for distribution. After receiving the telegram, the provincial government immediately forwarded it to the Provincial Disaster Area Relief Committee for verification, ordering them to send personnel to collect and transport the clothing to the disaster areas for distribution as soon as possible. (October 22)

Typhoon Disaster in Southern Guangdong Province 83

Haigang Dike Breached, Southern Suburbs Become a Watery Land; Beihai Civilian Aviation Airport Destroyed; Over a Hundred People Drowned in Ship Sinking at Haikou

Guangzhou Correspondence: The areas along the southern coast of Guangdong Province are prone to typhoons during the typhoon season. Therefore, local people experience typhoon disasters almost every year. In October last year, a major typhoon struck Haigang, Suixi, and other areas, causing surging tides that destroyed hundreds of acres of embankments, and gardens and houses were wiped out. The scars have not yet healed, but on the 8th of this month, a typhoon warning was issued again, and the damage was no less than last year. Since last month, the weather in Haigang County has been clear and the temperature has been high. However, on the evening of the 7th of this month, the weather suddenly changed, and a northwest wind brought torrential rain from the ocean. For a time, the wind roared on land, and the roofs of houses shook, as if ten thousand horses were galloping. Residents were awakened from their dreams, scrambling to repair leaks and close doors, in a state of great disarray. By 5:00 AM, the wind had become even stronger, and it continued to rage until the 8th, uprooting trees, sinking boats, and collapsing houses, resulting in a major disaster. The low-lying areas outside the county seat were flooded by rising tides, causing the embankments to collapse. The Naxi area became a vast expanse of water. Villages such as Muting Township, Mochen Village, Baishawei, Nanmen Market, and Beidiaohui outside the South Gate were submerged in the flood, with only the hilltops and treetops visible. Only one or two small boats were traveling back and forth. Near the southern suburbs, the water was four to five feet deep. It is reported that most of the embankments that had collapsed last year were washed away again. The new embankment in Muting Bay was completely washed away by the seawater, and all the late-season rice and miscellaneous grains were swept away. Refugees crowded into the city. The classrooms and dormitories of Leizhou Normal School and the County First Primary School were blown down by the wind. The Haigang County Magistrate Lin Zhende, in addition to telegrahping the township chiefs in the disaster areas to investigate the disaster situation, also telegraphed a report to the province yesterday, stating that the wind suddenly rose on the morning of the 8th, and the tide surged, causing breaches in many places along the north and south embankments, and the east and west oceans were flooded, with a disaster situation no less than last year. On the evening of the 7th, a hurricane struck Lianzhou and Beihai, and the wind became even stronger on the afternoon of the 8th. Trees and temporary buildings in the county seat were destroyed. The education office and auditorium of Lianzhou Middle School were also collapsed by the wind. All telephone lines from Lianzhou to Beihai, Hepu to Lingshan, and Hepu to Qinzhou were broken, and news was blocked. More than ten fishing boats sank on the Anpu sea surface, and cargo ships were capsized in front of the customs, resulting in deaths and the loss of tens of thousands of units worth of goods. The entire Beihai civil aviation airport collapsed, and countless other residents' houses were blown down. As for Qiongya, being isolated in the ocean, it also suffered from the typhoon. According to returning passengers, hurricanes occurred from the 7th to the 10th of this month in the Haikou area of Qiongzhou, especially on the 8th. Many houses were destroyed near Haikou, and crops were almost completely lost. Dozens of ships sank off the coast of Haikou, drowning over a hundred people. The disaster situation is extremely serious. (October 18)

Telephone Expert Committee: Summary of Telephone Report 84

Advocating a Uniform Pay-Per-Call System: Initial Costs Reduced for Business and Residential Telephones; Report Accompanied by Three Contributory Opinions: Long-Distance Calls in the Chinese Concession Should Be Improved Immediately

The telephone expert's report has been released. For the convenience of readers, the key suggestions in the report are listed below: (1) The Shanghai Telephone Company has fulfilled the provisions of Article 5 of the franchise contract and should enjoy the net profit of 8.2% on its business investment as stipulated in Article 13, Section 2 of the contract, and may start raising prices from April 1st. (2) All expenditures of the company regarding machinery, equipment, and other properties are reasonable, prudent, and not excessive. (3) The company's operating and maintenance expenses are generally economical and reasonable. However, the two items of general business in operating expenses are higher than those of other companies in the East. It is suggested that the company should further seek savings in expenditures, such as advertising and promotion costs, and employ more local technical talents in addition to top-level foreign personnel. (4) In order to reduce the burden on small users and increase the effectiveness of ordinary users, a pay-per-call system including a basic number of calls should be uniformly adopted for both business and residential users. (5) The most important proposal for telephone charges is: for business telephones, 150 calls per month for 10 yuan, with an additional charge of 3 fen per call; for residential telephones, 100 calls per month for 6 yuan 5 jiao, with an additional charge of 3 fen per call. (6) Opinions are given on the three issues of call charges for Chinese concessions, long-distance telephone connection methods, and telephone charges for roads outside the settlement.

The report on the issue of telephone rate increases by the Telephone Expert Committee of the Public Concession's Bureau of Works was formally signed by experts from China, Japan, Britain, and the United States the day before yesterday evening and submitted to the Board of Directors of the Bureau of Works yesterday. A general translation is made and urgently announced as follows:

The names of the experts are: Mr. Hu Ruixiang from China, Mr. Inada San-no-suke from Japan, Mr. Brown from Britain, and Mr. Ray from the United States.

The first section of the report first excerpts the scope of the Telephone Expert Committee's investigation of telephone affairs, as previously passed by the Board of Directors of the Public Concession (see the Bureau of Works Gazette of July 24 of this year), and declares that it will answer each item within the scope of the investigation in order. However, Section 3 of the scope assumes the continued maintenance of the current unlimited call subscription system and instructs the experts to draw up a price list, so it is proposed not to discuss it. In addition, Section 1 of the scope includes the following items:

(A) Does the Shanghai Telephone Company have the right to increase telephone charges from April 1935?

(B) Are the company's expenditures on machinery, equipment, and other properties economical?

(C) Are the company's existing operating and maintenance costs economical and reasonable?

Section 1 of the scope includes the following items:

(A) Is it appropriate to adopt a pay-per-call system for business telephones or residential telephones or both?

(B) If a pay-per-call system is considered appropriate, what kind of price list should be adopted so that the company can obtain the net profit stipulated in the franchise contract? The report also involves the origin of the franchise contract, because before the Shanghai Telephone Company obtained this franchise contract, there were three telephone companies competing fiercely for this right. Among them, the terms proposed by the International Telephong and Telegraoh Corporation (i.e., the parent company of the Shanghai Telephone Company) were the most favorable, so the Bureau of Works granted the franchise. The following are the answers to the questions within the scope of the experts' work:

Section 1 - A: From the perspectives of mechanical technology and economic management, in addition to the detailed opinions expressed elsewhere in this report, the Expert Committee believes that the company can fulfill the conditions of Article 5 of the franchise contract in a reasonable and pragmatic manner and should enjoy the benefits on the price list stipulated in Article 13, Section 2 of the franchise contract. The original text is: "After the completion of the installation of the automatic machine, the company may negotiate a price list with the Bureau of Works so that the company can obtain a net annual interest of 8.2% on its investment."

Section 1 - B: Regarding this issue, the experts first stated that what they always kept in mind when preparing the report was the so-called "Optimum Condition," which refers to the reasonable cost at which a certain supplier should be able to provide competent and surplus services. Regarding machinery, the report contains the following record: "All the machinery in Shanghai is modern in all aspects and can provide the best quality telephone supply, which is also the case in fact. We have also reviewed the company's records, and there are very few expressions of dissatisfaction with the supply. The company's service tests and obstruction reports are also sufficient to show the excellent supply of the company. Users who have been consulted also say that the existing telephone is far superior to that provided by the Huayang Telephone Company in 1930." The effectiveness and universality of this service can also be seen from the rapid expansion of business. The report contains a detailed description, and the experts further stated, "The company's entire machinery is planned for the current and projected future situation of Shanghai. When the business develops and expands in the future, the input of new capital will be extremely limited. If we consider the situation at the time of purchasing or constructing the entire machinery, the company's expenditures are all reasonable and necessary in our opinion and were made with prudence. Because at that time, the public had a great demand for better telephone supply, and the installation of machinery had to be as complete as possible to meet local needs and in accordance with the provisions of the franchise contract. Under severe penalties, the company had to complete the automatic machine change within two years, and the company was able to complete the regulation in 20 months, reducing 132 days compared to what was allowed in the franchise contract. This spirit of prompt handling has great value for users.

In terms of expenditure, as of July 30, 1935, the total investment in the company's machinery and property reached 42,294,000 yuan, but by the end of this year, it is expected to increase to 42,830,000 yuan. The telephone company should be able to obtain a net profit of 8.2% on its "capital investment" (CapitalInvestear, i.e., the business investment stipulated in the franchise contract). This profit capital was 34,836,000 yuan at the end of 1934. In addition, there are other investments of about 6,000,000 yuan or more that cannot enjoy the same net profit. This distinction is because among the company's total investment, there are several types of money invested in the right to operate the company's profits, such as the rolling stock of depreciation and the surplus obtained from financial scheduling in 1933.

The report states, "Between December 31, 1934, and July 31, 1935, although the company's investment has increased by 1,346,000 yuan, the profit capital has actually decreased by 690,000 yuan due to the repayment of debts. From this, it can be seen that although the company's total investment has increased to 42,294,000 yuan in the first seven months of this year, the profit capital has decreased from 34,836,000 yuan to 34,146,000 yuan. Some say that the company's machinery has been overbuilt and that there has been waste in terms of expenditure, but according to our investigation, this is not entirely the case. On the contrary, this expenditure was reasonable and necessary under the circumstances at the time. In addition, the total amount of expenditure during the company's replacement of automatic machines, about two years, reached 17,735,000 taels, exceeding more than double what was estimated in the An Sheng report. This may also be the source of the saying that expenditure was wasted, because according to An Sheng's estimate, only 8,000,000 taels were required."

Regarding the above, the experts have the following detailed explanation: When An Sheng drafted the estimate, the Huayang Telephone Company still existed, and there was no plan to organize a new company at that time. However, when the franchise contract of the new company was drafted, the various requirements that the new supply should have were stipulated in detail. At that time, the idea seemed to be "take the essence and use the vast, one effort for all." The old system has been overthrown, and the future needs of increasing day by day and month by month had to be prepared. This is the biggest reason why the actual expenditure of the current company and the estimate in the An Sheng report cannot be reconciled. Later, the price of gold soared and the value of taels plummeted, affecting 85% of the company's construction costs, so the company's expenditure became even greater. According to the experts' investigation, when An Sheng drafted the report, every 100 taels of Kuan yuan was equivalent to 61 yuan, 8 jiao, and 3 li, but in the construction process of the new company, the average price of 100 taels of Kuan yuan was only 33 yuan, 1 jiao, and 1 li, and even on July 31, 1930, it was only 37 yuan per 100 taels of Kuan yuan.

The experts further stated that at the end of 1934, the company's total investment in machinery, business, etc. was 40,948,125 yuan, which was divided into machinery transferred from the old company that is currently in use, valued at 11,580,000 yuan, and machinery installed by the new company after August 5, 1930, valued at 29,368,000 yuan. The experts discussed whether the major categories of the company's property were economical. First, regarding the external line installation, the experts felt that the expenditure was extremely reasonable and said that the company was based on sound engineering knowledge and economic application. All investments were reasonable and prudent, so the external line machinery was modern and excellent in all aspects. As for the telephone equipment, according to the experts' observations, it was also extremely fair. It was especially commendable to uniformly change the old-fashioned telephone equipment to automatic machines in a short period of time. "It is feared that there are not many places where it can be updated uniformly in such a wide range and in such a short period of time."

Next, on the impact of the number of calls on the equipment, the experts predicted that after any kind of limited system is adopted in the future, the number of calls will be greatly reduced. At that time, "the company will be able to postpone the investment expenditure of the new equipment, which is unavoidable under the current situation, and the excess transmitters in certain sub-stations can also be temporarily stored for future expansion. The effect of this delay in transmitter equipment is the equivalent saving of the cost of each line equipment. For the same reason, the maintenance cost of each line must also be reduced accordingly."

Regarding land and real estate, the numbers indicated by the company matched the land price at the time of August 1930, and the price of the houses was also fair and reasonable. The total amount of working equipment was extremely low among companies of the same scale. In Section 1, the experts stated that they had personally inspected the company's various sub-stations to see how the machinery was maintained. The result of this inspection led the experts to believe that the methods adopted by each station were the most modern and were the same as those adopted by the Bell System Telephone Company in the United States and the British Post Office. To prove the management methods of the world's major telephone businesses, the maintenance achievements of the telephone company in this port can be regarded as satisfactory, and the number of user difficulties recorded is also impeccable. In terms of internal difficulties at each station, the numbers are generally balanced. Only the central station has a larger number than other places due to the excessive number of calls, but the work of troubleshooting can still maintain a very high standard. The report further states, "Maintenance costs only account for a portion of the total operating expenses, because the operating expenses include the following various expenses, which are all paid by the Shanghai Telephone Company: (1) General, (2) Call, (3) Business, (4) Maintenance, (5) Depreciation, (6) Taxes. We deeply feel that operating expenses do need to be considered in the long term. We have compared the above-mentioned first four items with other telephone businesses, but because the situations in each place are different, or even cannot be compared, the comparison should also be made with extreme caution. However, in terms of bookkeeping methods, the methods of the American companies are roughly the same as those of the Shanghai Telephone Company, and the telephone organizations of Eastern countries are also mostly available for reference because of the similar living standards of the people. In the bookkeeping of the American Bell System companies, the costs of long-distance calls and local costs are combined, making it impossible to analyze them. In addition, the Honolulu Mutual Telephone Company is extremely similar to the Shanghai Telephone Company in terms of its business conditions and can be compared. However, the general and business expenses in all operating expenses of the Honolulu Company are extremely low, far from those of the Shanghai Company. From this, it can be seen that the expenses of the Shanghai Company seem to have the possibility of further tightening. For example, in the first half of this year, the advertising and promotion expenses spent on each telephone in the Shanghai Telephone Company reached 2 yuan and 1 jiao and 4 fen. Although we know that the economic depression of society has to be used for advertising and publicity to attract customers, it is especially important to be cautious about whether the gains and losses are commensurate. From another aspect, the total amount of cost spent on each telephone is the highest in the United States and the lowest in the East. This is due to the huge difference in the living standards of people in the East and the West, but the average total cost per telephone of the Shanghai Telephone Company, after deducting management expenses last year, still reached 46 yuan and 2 jiao, which is the highest among the telephone businesses in the adjacent cities of China and Japan. In addition, among the employees of the Shanghai Telephone Company, the number of foreign personnel with extremely high salaries is very large. Although the company is operated by foreign capital, the highest positions have to be held by foreigners, but there are still many positions under senior officials that are irrelevant to the power of affairs, and it is the company's own policy to attract local talents in the same position. Therefore, in the future, when personnel with considerable training and technical expertise can be hired locally, the company should implement this policy as much as possible. "

In addition, the experts believe that the depreciation calculation method adopted by the telephone company, that is, 4.5% of the total assets of the company are depreciated each year, is still considered reasonable and suggests that this calculation should continue until there are other instructions in the future experience.

Section 2, A: According to the experts, there are currently about three types of telephone charging systems in general use, namely subscription (or unlimited call method), tiered counting, and pay-per-call. The experts have a detailed discussion on the advantages and disadvantages of the above three methods, but they believe that the subscription method is only suitable for smaller telephone systems. As for the breadth of Shanghai, the large population, and whether the service is considerate, it depends on the widespread installation of sub-stations, and the subscription system is no longer suitable. According to the experts, the universal price of unlimited supply is based on the average application of all large and small users. The result of this universal average price is that small users are discouraged and large users are used as much as possible. However, the abuse of large users not only damages the function of their own telephones, but also hinders other users who want to talk to them. The so-called "busy line" is because it is busy, so external calls cannot be connected, and those who talk to it regard it as "equal to closing the door" because they cannot answer many times, or they have to switch to other homes after a few calls. Therefore, merchants who often have busy lines invisibly lose many customers, but there are also considerable losses if the telephone cannot be connected many times. The cost is actually shared by all users, large and small, and the public suffers the loss. "

In Shanghai, as a result of adopting the unlimited call subscription method, all the disadvantages have been pointed out one by one in the expert report, and it is said that in addition to the users who are careless and abuse them at will, there are also those who install residential telephones for business purposes, and the company has presented a lot of evidence. The experts said, "In view of the widespread installation of merchants in this port, it will not help to cancel the pay-per-call system for commercial telephones only, because after such a change, all calls originally made on commercial telephones can be carried out on residential telephones that are charged on a subscription basis. It is also useless to allow users to freely choose the charging method, and after repeated trials in other places, large users will continue to adopt the unlimited subscription system, while small users will adopt limited numbers or pay-per-call methods, because large and small users each choose the method that is beneficial to themselves. " The experts further stated that because the supply of telephones can be abused at will, the number of user calls increased by a factor of one between 1930 and 1934, and the company's capital and operating expenses also increased sharply as a result. "All these extra expenses, which are caused by the extremely high number of calls, must be borne by each user, regardless of its size, on average. Therefore, if this universal and uniform charging method is not changed for a long time, the disadvantages for small users will increase day by day. Now, in order to remedy this, we deeply feel that there is no better way than to adopt a new charging system that makes the price paid for the supply somewhat related to the actual use. "

The experts further stated, "The stage counting method may be used as a transitional method from the subscription system to the pay-per-call system, but the stage counting method also has its shortcomings, and the price of the call often varies by several yuan due to the number of calls. Therefore, this system is absolutely unacceptable and very few people adopt it. Therefore, our conclusion is that the pay-per-call system, which includes the number of calls in the basic stage, is the most suitable method. All users in Shanghai, whether they are businesses or residences, should uniformly adopt it. "Our proposal is that users in Shanghai, whether they are businesses or residences, should uniformly adopt the pay-per-call method based on the price of the supply, because we firmly believe that this method is the most beneficial to society."

Page 10

Section 2, B: Regarding the matter of setting prices so that the Shanghai Telephone Company can enjoy a net profit of 8.2% on its profit investment, the experts considered several other matters before making a decision. The first point is about the impact on the number of calls after adopting any pay-per-call method. The telephone company has agreed to a reduction of 37.5%. The experts believe that this point is reasonable. Therefore, their conclusion is that adopting the pay-per-call system, including the number of calls in the first stage in a certain basic call fee, and reducing the charge for each additional call is the most practical method at present. The experts then proceeded to calculate the necessary prices so that the pay-per-call method could generate the desired benefits and find the percentage of its interest, but one item was reserved, which was that US government income tax, general management fees, and annual depreciation of 150,000 yuan were not included in the calculation. If these expenses can be spent by the company under the business item in the future, there will be a reduction of nearly 2% in net profit. According to this calculation, what the experts believe is necessary is that commercial telephones should be priced at 11 yuan per month for 150 calls in the basic stage, and residential telephones should be priced at 7 yuan per month for 100 calls in the basic stage. In addition, whether it is commercial or residential, a fee of 3 fen will be charged for each additional call. However, the experts deeply feel that the Shanghai Telephone Company should be willing to accept a slightly lower item, so that the economic depression will ease slightly in the future, or even if the ministry disappears, the company's profits will not exceed what it deserves, which will lead to the need for another investigation to seek a further reduction in the company's income. Therefore, the experts prepared another price list, which can obtain a net profit of 8.54% in the initial implementation. It is hoped that the company can temporarily accept this method, that is, commercial telephones are 10 yuan per month, which can make 150 calls, with an additional charge of 3 fen per call, and sub-lines are 5 yuan per month. Residential telephones are 6 yuan and 5 jiao per month, which can make 100 calls, with an additional charge of 3 fen per call. In addition, the telephones that have already implemented the pay-per-call system will be calculated in the same way as other commercial telephones, that is, 10 yuan per month to make 150 calls.

The report further stated, "When drafting the price list, it was necessary to reduce the number of calls by 37.5%, but if the number of reductions exceeds this estimate, the company's profits will not be able to obtain the expected number. However, considering various situations, we deeply feel that there is no way to obtain a closer calculation than this. We have also used the experience of telephone businesses in other places that have changed from the subscription system to the pay-per-call system as a reference. We also know that the current number of calls is extremely high, and the decline in the number of calls after the implementation of the new system will inevitably be greater than the original number of calls. Furthermore, it is extremely obvious that the call fees paid by small users in the current price list will be lower than what they pay now. According to our records, if the telephone prices before April 1 of this year are used, then 47% of residential users and 41% of commercial telephones will pay lower call fees in the future. If the current temporary price increase is used, then 59% of residential users and 50% of commercial telephones will be able to save on call fees in the future. From this, it can be seen that after the implementation of the pay-per-call system, the call fees will not generally increase as rumored by the outside world. "

As for other items in the price list, the experts also intend to modify them. The modified prices include the following items:

Each rotary telephone will be charged an additional monthly fee of 5 jiao, which was originally set at 1 yuan and 4 jiao and 7 fen. The installation fee was originally set at 13 yuan, 9 jiao, and 9 fen, and is now set at 10 yuan. Sub-lines and indoor sub-machines were originally set at 2 yuan, 1 jiao, and 9 fen, and are now uniformly 1 yuan. The reconnection fee was originally set at 2 yuan and 8 jiao, and is now set at 2 yuan.

The above items are all lower than the original prices. In addition, there are

Private lines, patch cords, sub-lines, etc., which were originally calculated by line. It is stipulated that each half air mile, or less than half air mile, is 12 yuan per line. If it exceeds half air mile, an additional 1 yuan will be charged for every tenth of a mile, or its remainder. The telephone is 1 yuan per unit.

The monthly rental fee for private switchboards was originally 1 yuan, 6 jiao, and 3 fen for 10 lines, 3 yuan and 5 jiao for 15 lines, 7 yuan and 3 jiao for 25 lines, 9 yuan, 4 jiao, and 9 fen for 36 lines, 10 yuan, 9 jiao, and 3 fen for 47 lines, and 12 yuan and 4 jiao for 58 lines. The current rental fee is 5 yuan for 10 lines, 7 yuan for 15 lines, 10 yuan for 25 lines, 12 yuan for 36 lines, 14 yuan for 47 lines, and 16 yuan for 58 lines.

The above special line prices are greatly reduced compared to the prices proposed by the telephone company in January of this year. Those who rent private lines can get direct and agile private calls, and the telephone company has no other income besides the rental fee. Otherwise, if the special line does not exist, the user's calls must pass through the company's sub-station. If there are many things, installing one more line has appropriate income, so when setting the price of this special line, the supply obtained by the tenant has to be taken into account. The rental fee for private switchboards has been slightly increased, but the company has suffered great losses under this item. This small increase can slightly reduce the company's losses. Furthermore, the additional price of the rotary telephone has been reduced by almost two-thirds, and the sub-line sub-machine has been reduced

More than one-half. Therefore, the increase in the rental fee of this switchboard is not a concern. "

The report concluded, "We deeply hope that the Shanghai Telephone Company can accept the above items. When the profits are insufficient in the future, it can be re-discussed in accordance with Article 14 of the franchise contract."

The above is a summary of all the answers to the matters investigated within the scope of the telephone experts' powers. In addition, there are several important issues that are closely related to the telephone business in this port, but are not within the scope of the investigation. The experts have the following opinions:

The experts said, in addition, there are several matters that are not within the scope of our investigation. We would like to express our opinions as follows in view of the earnest expectations of all parties:

The call fee question is a troubling issue of call fees between users of the Shanghai Telephone Company and the Chinese Telephone Bureau. We have no precedent to refer to for telephone systems operated by the two authorities, between which users can make free calls without paying. However, under the existing method, users in one system must report their numbers for the purpose of recording before the call is connected. Therefore, all kinds of malpractices and fraudulent abuses are obvious to everyone. Users often have to pay call fees for others without making a call, which is extremely unfair. This malpractice can be avoided if direct dialing can be carried out between the two systems.

The long-distance telephone connection problem - China's long-distance telephone is operated by the Chinese government. When users in adjacent areas want to make long-distance calls, the call must first be connected to the manual switchboard of the telephone company's central station, where the switchboard operator asks the original caller for their telephone number and the telephone number to be connected. After the switchboard operator records both numbers, they dial to the Zhabei long-distance telephone office, where the Chinese Telephone Bureau switchboard operator also asks for the telephone numbers of both parties in the same way, and then connects the call. This procedure is extremely cumbersome and repetitive. If the local and long-distance telephones are affiliated with the same authority, only one station is needed, and there is no need for two stations. Technically speaking, setting up one more station is adding to the trouble, and because of this additional station, the sound has been greatly reduced during long-distance calls, and there are many obstacles and delays in machinery and work. In terms of time, it is also extremely uneconomical, so this redundant station is like adding five wheels to a car, which is counterproductive.

The Chinese authorities have no separate long-distance telephone stations in the Public Concession. The obvious reason is that since the franchise for business in the concession has been granted to the Shanghai Telephone Company, if the Telephone Bureau sets up a sub-station in the concession, it may be related to the company's sovereignty. However, on the other hand, for the sake of service and verification, the Shanghai Telephone Company does not allow its users to directly connect to the Telephone Bureau's long-distance line, and the company's personnel record the number of calls. Therefore, in case of difficulties, the person responsible to the user is not the Chinese Telephone Bureau, but the Shanghai Telephone Company. From this, it can be seen that this inappropriate method of setting up stations by both parties to handle long-distance calls will continue to exist if the company and the Telephone Bureau do not yield to each other. Technically speaking, the long-distance telephone line should be as close to the user as possible, which means that the Chinese Telephone Bureau's line should end at the Shanghai Telephone Company's long-distance telephone switchboard. If this method cannot be established, then in our opinion, the most appropriate method is to allow users in the concession to directly call and connect with the Zhabei long-distance telephone station, and the telephone company can send accounting personnel to the station to record the number of calls to show credibility. Either of these two methods can save costs and make the sound clearer during calls, because the number of connection points has been reduced by one. Therefore, we advocate that the telephone authorities of both parties should consider this matter deeply, find a way to reach an understanding, and seek to eliminate the existing bad methods.

"The telephone question of building roads outside the boundary is that the price paid by telephone users in the area of building roads outside the boundary seems to be sufficient to limit the development of the telephone business to residents who have to install telephones. Naturally, the blame for this situation does not lie with the Shanghai Telephone Company, because the call fees charged by the company are the same as those of users in the concession. As for the collection of additional fees, the company not only has no profit to gain, but also has to collect and pay on behalf of others, which is cumbersome and full of complaints. Taking the North District as an example, the Chinese Telephone Bureau in that area could have provided telephones, but the additional fees must be collected by the Telephone Company on behalf of the Chinese Telephone Bureau as a tax for the Chinese Telephone Bureau's abandonment of telephone rights. Since the Chinese Telephone Bureau allows users to install concession telephones, users can save 5 fen per call. This issue is still under negotiation between China and foreign countries, so for the time being, we will not give a detailed discussion on this complicated issue, but what we want to say is that the people in the area of building roads outside the boundary have heard a lot of complaints about the heavy burden.

Qingdao Business Circle Organizes Fruit Production Company 85

—To Establish a Model Orchard—

Qingdao Correspondence: The local geology and climate are quite suitable for fruit production. Unfortunately, farmers adhere to old methods and do not know how to improve, resulting in poor quality products and limited sales. Prominent figures and capitalists in the city, in order to develop the local fruit industry, have organized the Qingdao Fruit Production Co., Ltd. to engage in the planting of fruits and vegetables, storage, and transportation. The capital is set at 60,000 yuan, fully subscribed by the promoters, and has been paid in full and deposited in the Shanghai Bank. The promoters have already submitted an application to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration and forwarded it to the Ministry of Industry for registration. The document submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau states, "Submitting an application for the registration of Qingdao Fruit Production Co., Ltd., organized by fundraising, in order to develop the local fruit industry and assist rural construction, in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law for limited liability companies. We have raised funds to organize Qingdao Fruit Production Co., Ltd., to engage in the business of planting fruits and vegetables, storage, transportation, and processing and manufacturing of ancillary matters. The total capital is provisionally set at 60,000 yuan in national currency, divided into 600 shares, each share at 300 yuan, fully subscribed by the promoters. A temporary office is located in the Bank of Communications Building on Zhongshan Road in this city. A list of promoters is prepared and submitted to your office for review. We humbly request approval for registration. The promoters are Peng Dongyuan, Deng Yiguang, Ye Zigang, Qi Yunzhi, Xi Dongsheng, Sun Zhenwu, Zhou Zhijun, Lin Fengqi, Yi Yongfang, Ge Mengyu, Ouyang Hong, Lu Wenfeng, Gu Dingfu, Yao Shenba, Wu Tuian, Cheng Jingzhi, Song Qiangming, Zhou Yanjing." Furthermore, the company's proposed plan is as follows: "The Qingdao geology and climate are particularly suitable for fruit production. Currently, peaches, plums, apples, grapes, and other varieties are already showing some success in Qingdao. Unfortunately, farmers adhere to old methods and do not know how to improve. If varieties are not selected and pests cannot be eliminated, the resulting products will be poor and sales will be limited. In view of this, the company will first engage in establishing a model orchard to cultivate, improve varieties, and apply scientific cultivation methods simultaneously. At the same time, we will plant both Chinese and Western vegetables to promote rural production. We will also establish storage warehouses to preserve large quantities of fruit produced using scientific methods, so that they can be distributed leisurely in domestic and foreign markets without being affected by weather or human factors. Before the model orchard of the company produces fruit, we plan to first engage in transportation and sales, both to promote the existing fruit production of the city, improve the livelihood of farmers, and to study transportation methods to seek commercial rationality. Therefore, transportation and sales are also one of the company's main research and improvement tasks. As for establishing factories to manufacture canned goods and brew wine, these will be carried out in order depending on the future management effectiveness and environmental needs, in order to enrich people's lives, so that everyone can taste both sheep dates and sorrowful pears, and fine wines can be obtained without seeking them from outside. The development of fruit production in the city and the recovery of rural resources will depend on this."

Nanhui

Execution by Shooting of a Repeat Barbiturate Injection Offender

Shi Fenglou, a resident of the Eighth District Central Township, had a long-standing barbiturate injection habit. He was previously detained and ordered to undergo rehabilitation and released on bond. However, after his release, he continued to inject. The Public Security Bureau investigated and brought him to the county, ordering him to be examined by the smoking cessation center. It was reported that the offender was indeed a repeat offender with an addiction. He was then sent to the Zhenjiang Garrison Command for interrogation. A telegram was received from the province sentencing the offender to death, approved by Chairman Chiang, and ordered to be brought back for execution. The county government ordered Mou Yizhi, the leader of the water patrol team, to go to the province to bring him back. The county government, seeing that there were many drug dealers and injection offenders in the Eighth District, ordered the Public Security Bureau team to escort the offender to Datuan Town in that district on the 21st for execution by shooting as a deterrent. At the same time, the county party headquarters and the county government sent several personnel to promote drug prohibition in order to draw the attention of the general public.

Songjiang

County Magistrate Investigates Smoking and a Smoker Resists with Violence

After the new county magistrate, Li Leng, arrived in Songjiang, he devoted himself to improving the Baojia system and prohibiting smoking. Li went to various sales and smoking locations himself to conduct inspections. On the morning of the 23rd, in Shouji's sales and smoking location on Changqiao Street, he discovered Wang Yunhai smoking without a license. He ordered the clerk of the location to guard him and wait for the police to take him into custody. Unexpectedly, Wang Yunhai suddenly attacked Li and escaped during the commotion. The county government has now summoned the owner of the location to turn over the escaped Wang Yunhai for interrogation. The clerk, A Gen, has already been summoned. The county's smoking prohibition committee was previously reorganized by order of the province and is no longer under the smoking prohibition section. The former county magistrate selected Wang Zhewu, Cai Zhongyu, Sun Shiheng, Lu Shushu, Li Zufu, Li Xiuzhe, and Zhou Zhanqi, seven people, as members of the county's smoking prohibition committee, and submitted them to the provincial smoking prohibition committee for approval. Now, Magistrate Li has prepared letters to invite them to serve.

Suzhou

Thorough Investigation of Agricultural Bank Staff Embezzlement

The director of the treasury department of the Suzhou Farmers Bank, Wang Cainan, embezzled 150,000 yuan and fled without a trace. The situation was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that the bank manager, Zhu Qingzeng, collected Wang Cainan's photos and sent them to the head office on the 23rd, offering a reward for his arrest and negotiating with his guarantors. It is said that Manager Zhu and the business director, Fang Anzhi, have resigned. The head office, finding Wang Cainan's sudden embezzlement and escape strange, has sent Xu Jun to Suzhou for a thorough investigation to clarify the truth. According to news from banking circles, Wang Cainan's embezzlement was not accidental. There was considerable planning beforehand, and it was definitely not something Wang Cainan could have done rashly on his own.

Wuxi

Provincial Committee Goes to Rural Areas to Survey Autumn Famine

This county's fifth district, Yanqiao, sixth district, Zhangjingqiao, ninth district, Beiqifang, tenth district, Luoshe, and other townships have all experienced white grubworm famine this year. The districts reported to the county government and forwarded the reports to the provincial government, the Ministry of Civil Affairs, and the Ministry of Construction. Qiu Xudong was dispatched to the affected townships to conduct a survey and report. Recently, the Ministry of Civil Affairs dispatched Chen Yuchu, the director of the Public Security Bureau, and the Ministry of Finance dispatched Qiu Xudong, the chief of accounting, and the Ministry of Construction dispatched Tang Xixiang, the director of the sericulture experiment field. On the 23rd, they went to the Yanqiao area in the fifth district, the Beishangfang area in the ninth district, and the Luoshe area in the sixth district to conduct a joint survey. They are scheduled to go to the Zhangjingqiao area in the sixth district to inspect the autumn famine.

Changzhou

Commissioner of Supervisory Office Arrives in Changzhou

The Jiangsu Provincial Supervisory Office, in order to understand the political situation in various counties, has dispatched commissioners to inspect various counties. The commissioner dispatched to Wujin is surnamed Pan. He has arrived in Changzhou for several days and is conducting a secret inspection. His name is not announced. In the afternoon of the 22nd, he inspected the Public Security Bureau. The reception room of the bureau did not show his name card, but only showed the badge of the Supervisory Office. He was accompanied by Inspector Wu Shengfang and others for a week before leaving.

Changshu

Agricultural Bank Manager Embezzles Funds and Flees

The Farmers Bank on County South Street in this county was the first branch established by the Jiangsu Province. Chen Herong from Suzhou was appointed by the province as the bank manager. He has been in office for five or six years. The business has developed and is highly regarded by the province. Unfortunately, Chen had extensive social connections in Changshu, resulting in significant losses to the bank's funds over the years. Unable to make up for the losses, Chen absconded with over 80,000 yuan. The deputy manager of the bank noticed this and reported it to the province for instructions. The head office was extremely angry. On one hand, it ordered Chen to be wanted. On the other hand, it appointed Li Huihua to come to Changshu to succeed as bank manager. Li arrived in Changshu on the 22nd to take office. It is also learned that Wang Cainan, the treasury director of the Suzhou branch, also had a similar incident. It is said that there is a connection with the Changshu branch.

Jiading

Record of the Second Trial of the Assault on Police Case

The case of the friend of the Yichangyong shop throwing away pear residue, and the auxiliary policeman Chen Yangjie intervening, causing a dispute over slapping the counter and an assault on the police, was heard for the second time on the 21st by the county trial officer Shan Longbao, who ordered all parties involved to be summoned. The audience was still very crowded. Chuan Mengxian denied participating in the assault, but out of consideration for the injured policeman, he agreed to give the injured policeman Zhuo Dengwen 40 yuan in medical expenses. The court declared the debate on the assault on the police in front of Yichangyong concluded and awaiting sentencing. Regarding the assault on the police in front of Jiading Bank, because there was an auxiliary policeman named Chen Zhixiang who was not examined at the time, but recently died suddenly in a Shanghai hospital, it is necessary to inquire with the hospital for proof of the cause of death to determine whether it was related to the injury before further investigation. Fu Mengxian, Qian Xiaoci, Zhai Yonghua, Zhang Shunhua, and Zhao Baozhang were still released on their original bail. Li Xuefu, Shen Yuzhen, Wang Fuquan, and Zhang Zhongyun were remanded in custody.

Yangzhou

Chaste and Virtuous Girl Drowns Herself

Teng Huaizhen (age 19), daughter of Teng Guangxin, a farmer in Naxiang, Jiangdu, was deeply saddened by the loss of her mother last year and attempted suicide several times, but was saved by Guangxin. He then tried his best to find a son-in-law for his daughter. In March of this year, she was betrothed to a man surnamed Tang, Ziyongbao. Unexpectedly, Yongbao died suddenly of illness before the auspicious day arrived. Huaizhen became even more despondent and discussed with her father her wish to become a nun, but her father did not agree. She was unhappy all day long. On the morning of the 21st, she suddenly threw herself into the river. She was spotted and people called for help, but she had already passed away. The body has not yet been recovered.

Jingjiang

Resolution of Dispute in Fresh Meat Industry

In Jingjiang's urban area, the fresh meat industry was in dispute due to the collection of slaughter taxes and the crackdown on the sale of offal from the countryside. All the meat shops went on strike, holding their ground for many days. Yesterday, under the mediation of Xiong Shiyuan and others, the offal tax was contracted by the guild, with a total tax of 40 yuan. Business has now resumed as usual.

Nantong

Stabilization of Native Cloth Market Turmoil

Nantong's native cloth industry, in order to seek improvement and concentrate cloth collection, specially established a native cloth market. Weavers, due to misunderstandings, caused disturbances and damaged the interior, and also clashed with the police, causing a great uproar. After mediation by the extermination political organs and the use of Baojia publicity, the turmoil subsided. The native cloth industry has jointly established standards: new machine cloth is eight zhang long per bolt, two chi and two cun wide, and weighs at least 85 liang; old machine cloth is six zhang and eight chi long per bolt, two chi and one cun wide, and weighs at least 65 liang. The county government has issued a notice strictly prohibiting fraud to maintain the reputation of Nantong cloth.

Hangzhou

Resolution of Highway Strike Turmoil

The Jiang (Shan) Pu (Cheng) highway on the border of Zhejiang and Fujian provinces experienced a strike by cargo merchants due to the Fujian Provincial Government doubling the road investment, which was equivalent to doubling the freight costs. The highway business was greatly affected. After the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau tried to mediate and agreed on remedial measures with the Construction Department of Fujian Province, the merchants agreed and the strike turmoil came to an end. The road's cargo transportation has returned to normal.

Xiaoshan

Provincial Telephone Bureau Takes Over Telephone Services

The telephone service affiliated with the Yong'an Electric Company in this county has been in operation for seven years. Recently, the number of subscribers has gradually increased to nearly fifty, so the business is considered to be developing well. Recently, the Provincial Department of Construction, because the telephone part of the company did not apply for registration in advance and the business was not well-managed, ordered a ban. Subsequently, the Zhejiang branch of the National Private Electrical Federation applied for supplementary registration, but was rejected. On the 21st, the Xiaoshan branch of the Zhejiang Provincial Telephone Bureau took over the transfer and other matters. As of the 21st, Xu Guangchen, the telephone engineer of the bureau's urban telephone project, and five workers transported materials and wires from Hangzhou, preparing to install lines in various places. On one hand, they have cut off the communication lines of the Yong'an Company. On the other hand, they have installed large new telephone switchboards in the branch. Starting on the 22nd, the bureau has gradually started to transfer telephone calls for the subscribers.

Haimen

Robbers Kill on the Road

Sheng Baoyun, the clerk of the Yufeng Flower Firm in Chuanliugang, Fifth District, carried 1,000 yuan in paper money from Jiulong Town back to the firm yesterday (the 21st) morning. While traveling near Yuanhe Town, he was suddenly blocked by four robbers who pulled out sharp blades and stabbed Sheng to death, robbing the money and escaping. The local villagers saw this and gathered more than ten people, each with farm tools, to chase after them. One robber lost his footing and fell into the river, where he was captured by the villagers, beaten to death. The remaining robbers escaped with the stolen money. The firm learned of this and reported it to the county government. In the afternoon, Chen, the trial officer from Shan, went to inspect the scene, ordered the firm to take Sheng's body back for burial, and the Fifth District Office to bury the robber's body in a coffin, and ordered the police to strictly arrest the fleeing robbers and bring them to justice for interrogation.

Fuzhou

Tong Hangshi Goes to Northern Fujian for Inspection

Tong Hangshi, the president of the Provincial High Court, in order to rectify the judiciary and reform prison administration, previously personally visited various counties in Southern Fujian to conduct on-the-spot investigations, and reported the matters that should be promoted and reformed to the Judicial Yuan, which was highly praised by the authorities. This time, he did not hesitate to work hard and went to various counties in Northern Fujian for inspection. He arrived in Pucheng on the day of the symbol and arrived in Jianou on the day of the issue. In addition to inspecting the court and judicial offices one by one, he also examined the county government's handling of judicial matters. After returning to the province, he will comprehensively assess the judicial situation of the entire Fujian Province and formulate concrete improvement plans to serve as a reference for judicial administration in other provinces of our country.
