Local News

Shanghai Boy Scouts Hold General Mobilization for Flood Relief Fundraising - Decision Made to Hold External and Internal Fundraising Days Starting November 9th 86

This year's floods have affected the Huaihe and Han rivers successively, and the disaster is even more severe than in the Republic of China Year 20. The disaster area covers more than a dozen provinces, with tens of millions of victims, displaced and suffering unspeakable hardships. People from all walks of life have been donating money and efforts to help, but even with these efforts they are like a drop in the bucket. The Shanghai Provincial Flood Relief Association believes that the disaster is so severe that relief cannot be delayed. In addition to appealing to all parties for donations, various entertainment activities have been held one after another, with all proceeds going to relief. Yesterday, a general mobilization of the city's Boy Scouts was launched for fundraising. It is now learned that the plan has been finalized to mobilize the Boy Scouts to raise funds from November 9th to the 17th. The 9th and 10th will be the Boy Scouts' external fundraising days, and the 11th to 17th will be the internal fundraising days. At that time, the Huaren and Zujie authorities will be requested to assist. The following is the implementation plan for the Shanghai Boy Scouts' General Mobilization for Flood Relief Fundraising in various provinces: (1) The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Chinese Boy Scouts is ordered by the General Association of Chinese Boy Scouts and requested by the Shanghai Flood Relief Association to organize a general mobilization for flood relief fundraising in various provinces. (2) The preparatory work for the city's Boy Scouts' general mobilization for fundraising will be jointly handled by the personnel appointed by the Council and the Flood Relief Association. (3) The date for the city's Boy Scouts' general mobilization for fundraising is set from November 9th to the 17th, a total of nine days. The 9th and 10th will be the Boy Scouts' external fundraising days, and the 11th to 17th will be the internal fundraising days. (4) On the Boy Scouts' external fundraising days, donations can be solicited from residences, shops, foreign firms, institutions, hotels, amusement grounds, etc. within the areas designated by the Council from 8:00 am to 10:00 pm daily (but absolutely avoid soliciting donations along the road). (5) On the Boy Scouts' internal fundraising days, donations can be solicited from relatives and friends by the Boy Scouts at their leisure after work. (6) Boy Scouts participating in external fundraising will be granted leave by the Council on behalf of the schools or service agencies. (7) Donation tickets are divided into four types: one jiao, two jiao, one yuan in silver dollars, and two jiao and four jiao in small silver coins, printed by the Flood Relief Association and distributed by the Council for use. (8) Before and after the Boy Scouts' General Mobilization for Flood Relief Fundraising, propaganda should be carried out as much as possible to awaken the public and facilitate the fundraising. The methods include news advertising, leaflets, etc., which will be handled by the Flood Relief Association and the Council. (9) On the day of the Boy Scouts' external fundraising general mobilization, the Flood Relief Association will contact the municipal government and the authorities of the Public and French Concessions in advance to arrange for traffic and protection to facilitate the operation. (10) A commemorative badge will be issued to each group and Boy Scout participating in the fundraising, and special rewards will be given to those with excellent results (the reward method will be formulated separately by the Council). (11) During the Council's external fundraising, a temporary office will be set up at the Eight Immortals Bridge Youth Association to facilitate contact with the participating Boy Scouts. (12) The donations collected by each Boy Scout group will be handed over to the Council for remittance to the Flood Relief Association at any time.

Social Affairs Bureau Strictly Prohibits the Use of Sun Yat-Sen’s Name or Portrait on Trademarks 87

And Requires That Trademarks for National Products Must Not Be Entirely in Foreign Languages

Regarding the prohibition of using Sun Yat-Sen’s name or portrait on trademarks and the requirement that trademarks for national products must not be entirely in foreign languages, the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau previously received an order from the Ministry of Industry to correct and strictly prohibit this. The Social Affairs Bureau has published a notice in the newspaper, requiring all merchants to correct this by the end of June of this year, otherwise, they will be severely punished if found or reported. Now, the Ministry of Industry has three interpretations regarding the prohibition of using Sun Yat-Sen's name or portrait on trademarks: (A) Those who violate the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the Trademark Law, even if they have been registered, should be revoked. (B) If there are certificates obtained with the consent of Sun Yat-Sen during his lifetime, they can be approved for registration and use in accordance with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 8 of the Trademark Law. (C) The two characters "Zhongshan" are already used as place names, but since they are Sun Yat-Sen's alias, they shall not be used as trademarks in accordance with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the Trademark Law. It is also heard that the Sun Yat-Sen portrait Zhongshan brand trademark previously approved for registration by the Shanghai Daming Glasses Company was determined by the Ministry of Industry to be in conflict with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 2 of the Trademark Law. In order to respect Sun Yat-Sen's portrait and abide by the law, the Ministry ordered the Trademark Bureau to revoke this registration. It is also learned that the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau is currently sending personnel to investigate and solicit reports of whether anyone is still using Sun Yat-Sen's name or portrait as a trademark, and whether national products are entirely labeled in foreign languages. Those who dare to deliberately violate the rules will be severely punished.

Joint Water, Land, and Air Transport Conference Concludes Yesterday 92

More Than Forty Proposals Approved in Three Sessions

The Joint Water, Land, and Air Transport Conference for the Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai), Huhang (Shanghai-Hangzhou), and Huhangyong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo) railway lines concluded yesterday at 4:30 PM after holding three sessions and approving over forty proposals related to train schedules, freight rates, and other matters. Deputy Director of the Railway Bureau, Wu Shaozeng, attended the closing ceremony to express his gratitude, and representatives from various related parties were present. The atmosphere was warm with enthusiasm for discussing transport matters. The details of the conference and the resolutions are recorded below:

Three Sessions

The joint conference held three sessions. The first session took place at 2:00 PM the day before yesterday, with forty-one representatives attending. Xiao Weiguo chaired the session, and Tang Xiongjie served as the recorder. Ten proposals related to train schedules and freight rates were approved before the meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The second session was held at 9:00 AM yesterday, where twenty-one similar miscellaneous proposals were resolved. The third session began at 2:00 PM in the afternoon, where ten miscellaneous and temporary proposals were approved. After the meeting, Deputy Director of the Railway Bureau, Wu Shaozeng, attended and delivered a speech, stating that the bureau convened the meeting to promote joint transport along the lines and expressed his gratitude to the representatives for attending, sharing their opinions, and jointly strategizing. He hoped that all related parties would earnestly assist the bureau in implementing the resolutions to complete the joint transport undertaking.

Train Schedule Proposals

The two railway lines held a joint water, land, and air transport conference, totaling three sessions, with over forty proposals. These were categorized into four groups: "A. Train Schedules," B. Freight Rates," C. Miscellaneous," and "D. Temporary Motions." (A) Train Schedules: (1) Proposal to increase stops for boarding and alighting on both up and down trains. Resolution: The railway bureau will carefully consider this when changing train schedules. (2) Proposal to add fourth-class carriages to scheduled trains. Resolution: The railway bureau will appropriately allocate vehicles after considering increasing the number of carriages. (3) The three companies jointly operating transport between Xinchang, Shengxian stations and the Shanghai North and South stations have reduced ticket prices, originally hoping to attract passengers, but have not seen any improvement. It is proposed to change the Shanghai-Hangzhou fourth-class train to depart Shanghai at 11:00 AM and arrive in Hangzhou at 3:00 PM, and also offer discounts on fourth-class tickets to recover joint ticket sales. Resolution: (1) The proposal to change the fourth-class train schedule is approved in principle. The railway bureau will comprehensively consider all aspects and make appropriate modifications when changing train schedules to meet the needs. (2) The issue of reducing ticket prices should be discussed under the category of freight rates. (4) Proposal to change the schedule of the 74th Shanghai-Changzhou and 73rd Changzhou-Shanghai third and fourth-class trains to benefit passengers. Resolution: The railway bureau has already reviewed and revised the schedule of the 73rd local train, which is largely consistent with the proposal, so no further discussion is needed. As for the schedules of the 74th and 72nd trains, a comprehensive consideration of all aspects is necessary, so no changes will be made for the time being. (5) Proposal to compile and print a joint transport timetable. Resolution: Approved. A booklet and a single sheet should be printed, including information on the mileage and fares of various highways and ships, as well as travel tips, to benefit travelers. The required expenses, excluding advertising revenue, should be distributed according to the number of each department's needs.

Freight Rate Proposals

(B) Freight Rates: (1) Proposal to reduce third and fourth-class ticket prices. (2) Proposal to appropriately reduce fares on the Wudan (Wuhu-Danyang) and Zhenli (Zhenjiang-Lishui) Ludanjing (Luhe-Danyang-Jintan) sections of the Beijing-Shanghai line to develop joint transport business. (3) Proposal to reduce fares to benefit travelers (additional proposal). (4) Proposal to appropriately reduce third and fourth-class ticket prices between Shanghai, Kunshan, and Qingpu. The above four proposals, together with the second section of the third proposal under train schedules, "Discussion on discounts for Shanghai-Hangzhou fourth-class trains," were discussed together. Resolution: The railway bureau will conduct a detailed study and make appropriate arrangements, and suggest that the Ministry of Railways consult with relevant ministries to stipulate the basic freight rates for each railway, highway, and ship, and uniformly regulate them to avoid price competition. (5) Proposal to uniformly add round-trip tickets to joint transport shipping companies. (6) Proposal to allow the issuance of round-trip joint transport tickets for trains and ships to facilitate passengers. The above two proposals were discussed together. Resolution: The railway bureau will give detailed consideration and make appropriate arrangements.

Miscellaneous Proposals

(C) Miscellaneous: (1) The Zhenjiang New Transport Joint Transport Company requests permission to independently prepare and ship goods from the Zhenjiang transfer station for direct shipment from the original ships in the Jiangbei Joint Transport to Zhenjiang, in order to attract freight from the northern routes. Resolution: The railway bureau will directly negotiate with the New Transport Joint Transport Company to resolve this issue. (2) If there are any changes to the passenger transport regulations, the joint transport agencies should be notified immediately to facilitate planning. Resolution: (A) The phrase "passenger transport regulations" in this proposal should be changed to "all regulations related to joint transport." (B) All parties should exchange all regulations related to joint transport, and if there are any changes, they should notify each other ten days in advance. (C) In the future, any changes to all regulations related to joint transport by all parties will be implemented on the 1st, 11th, and 21st of each month to ensure consistency. (3) Joint transport luggage and packages must be delivered to the joint transport station earlier than the luggage and packages arriving at the station on the railway line to avoid passengers waiting and causing difficulties for the arrival station, in order to facilitate traffic. (4) Proposal to request each station to immediately load joint transport luggage onto the train and deliver it to the joint transport bus station and pier in advance. (5) Joint transport luggage should be mutually notified to the connecting stations or delivered on their behalf and transported with the train to allow passengers to pick it up at any time to facilitate passengers. The above three proposals were discussed together. Resolution: The transfer station should give priority to transferring joint transport luggage, packages, and goods. When necessary, the connecting stations should be notified of each other. (6) Luggage and packages loaded onto the train must be placed according to the arrival station, and the luggage compartment must be locked when the train departs, and servants and laborers are not allowed to carry them inside to prevent malpractice and protect the reputation of the railway. Resolution: All parties should make every effort to strictly crack down on this, and the railway bureau will draft crackdown measures to solicit opinions from all parties before implementing them. (7) The types and quantity limits of items that should be transported as packages must be stipulated to allow each other to follow the regulations and avoid disputes with passengers. Resolution: Refer to the methods stipulated by the Ministry of Railways, and each railway will handle it at its own discretion. (8) The return journey of the round-trip joint transport tickets should be re-linked according to the joint transport section so that one can tear off and collect them separately after completing one route to prevent passengers from fraudulently boarding the train again. (9) The round-trip joint transport tickets should be prohibited from using temporary tickets to prevent the station from being unable to tear off and calculate the cost during the audit. (10) The joint transport section tickets and group tickets should be divided into abundant linked styles to prevent the arrival station from being unable to tear off and calculate them, which is convenient for auditing. The above three proposals were discussed together. Resolution: Adopt the linked style, and the cost of printing tickets will still be distributed according to the original method. (10) (1) The joint transport waste tickets should be kept by the receiver. Resolution: It should be handled as usual. On the one hand, the railway bureau will conduct a more detailed consideration. (12) The monthly report of joint transport business revenue should be sent to each other for verification. Resolution: Approved. (13) The joint transport payment does not fulfill the stipulated date. (14) The Railway Bureau Shipping Bureau jointly transported ticket money. It is proposed to deduct it daily until the end of the month, when both parties will verify the calculation. (15) Modify the method of paying the joint ticket on a daily basis. (10) (6) The ticket account should be settled within a time limit. The above four proposals were discussed in combination and resolved as follows: A. The monthly business revenue is stipulated to be paid clearly by the 20th of the following month. B. The accounts of each highway and each shipping bureau shall be submitted to the Railway Bureau before the 10th of the following month. C. All shipping bureaus that have not signed a new standard contract with the Railway Bureau should sign it as soon as possible so that the methods are consistent. (17) Please increase the commission to 3%. Resolution: The Railway Bureau and the Shipping Bureau will resolve it through direct negotiation. (18) Those who handle passenger joint transport should also handle luggage and package joint transport and widely solicit customers to expand business. Resolution: Approved in principle, and each party will review and handle it at its discretion. (10) (9) All luggage or package freight rates and all joint transport methods should be handled in accordance with the off-road regulations within the possible scope. Resolution: The mountains will negotiate and handle business vigorously. (20) The scope of joint transport should be expanded as much as possible to benefit passengers. Resolution: The Railway Bureau will draft implementation methods and solicit opinions from all parties before handling them. (10) (21) Please send a monthly statistical report on joint transport services to each agency on a monthly basis. Resolution: Approved. (20) (22) It is proposed that each public highway bureau and each shipping bureau should closely liaise with the business offices of the Railway Bureau and mutually instruct each other to receive and deliver service cases. Resolution: The Railway Bureau will formulate methods and send them to each highway bureau and each shipping bureau, and reply with detailed opinions before the end of November of this year. All those who agree to handle the receiving and sending business will implement it from January 1, 25. (20) (23) For those who handle joint transport on the same route with both parties (such as the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and the Jingwu Automobile Company and the Jiangnan Railway Jingwu Line all have joint transport routes. The joint transport stations of each route should list the price lists of both parties at the ticket office to facilitate passengers. Resolution: Approved. (20) (24) It is proposed that each highway and each shipping bureau promote freight joint transport. Resolution: Approved in principle. The Railway Bureau will solicit opinions from each highway and each shipping company before handling it. (20) (25) The monthly report form of public buses should be sent to the accounting office on schedule. Resolution: A. This case should be changed to a monthly report form of a public bus company, which should be sent to the accounting office on time to facilitate liquidation. B. The monthly report forms of the Railway Bureau and each company must be sent to each other before the 10th of the following month. (20) (26) The passenger tickets, package tickets, and luggage tickets collected by each public bus company must be sent to the accounting office together with the list on a monthly basis. Resolution: Approved. (20) (27) Unify the method of charging handling fees by public automobile companies. Resolution: A. "Handling fee" in this case should be changed to "transfer fee." B. The transfer fee shall not be charged in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Railways.

Temporary Motions

(D) Temporary Motions: (1) The long linked receipt for luggage and bag receipts should be delivered at the same time as the luggage and packages to facilitate auditing at any time. Resolution: Approved. The Mountain Railway Bureau ordered its subordinate to pay close attention. (2) A request was made to discuss whether the Zhenjiang station director could be temporarily notified to dismantle one of the freight cars passing through each train if there are empty cars in order to load them quickly. Resolution: The Railway Bureau and the New Transport Joint Inspection Company will meet in person to negotiate and resolve it. (3) The Railway Bureau's freight yard has a customary storage period of seven days. May I ask you to change the storage period to ten days or fourteen days? It has been found that merchants in the Huaihe Lixiahe area transport large quantities of goods from Huojiaqiao to Shanghai by ship. Because Jianglun freight is transported to the upper warehouse of major ports, the storage period is stipulated to be fifteen days. If the Railway Bureau can extend the storage period, the merchants will benefit greatly. Please discuss this case. Resolution: It will be handled in accordance with the current method for the time being. (4) The Joint Transport Station of the Railway Bureau and our company (designated as the Danyang Railway Station as the Joint Transport Station) intends to allocate office space to facilitate convenience. Resolution: The Railway Bureau and Zhen Danjing Lishui Long-Distance Automobile Company will meet to negotiate. The Department stipulates discounts for the sale of ordinary and student joint transport group tickets. Resolution: Approved in principle, and all parties will review and handle it at their discretion.

Zhejiang Negotiates with Shanghai Banks for a Loan of 500,000 Yuan 94

To Help Fishermen in Various Coastal Areas

After the completion of various buildings, docks, and folk straw sheds in the Shanghai Fish Market of the Ministry of Industry, it will start operating in the middle of next month, and an opening ceremony will be held on a regular basis. The winter fishing season will begin next month, and during this period, there will be a lot of fish production along the coast of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. However, according to news from the fishing industry, fishermen in the coastal areas of Zhejiang usually have to borrow money from ice-fresh fish ships to go fishing and sell their fish to fish transport ships and sell them wholesale in Shanghai. In recent years, due to the general economic downturn, bank loans have decreased, and some fishermen have not been able to go fishing, resulting in a sharp decrease in production, which has had a significant impact on the economy of the people in various coastal areas of Zhejiang. Therefore, Zhejiang Province is negotiating with banks for a loan of 500,000 yuan to provide relief. At the same time, the Fish Market will also negotiate with the banking sector for ice-fresh fish transport to transfer loans to various fishermen.

Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association to Hold Elections Today 98

The election of two directors of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association, representing the rickshaw pullers, will be held this afternoon (Thursday) in accordance with the regulations of the board of directors of the Mutual Aid Association and the constitution approved by the Board of Directors of the Public Concession. Previously, on the 11th of this month, the 400 rickshaw puller electors were drawn at the Mutual Aid Association Headquarters on Dongjiaxing Road under the supervision of Mr. Yu Qiaqing of the Public Concession, Mr. Jin Runxiang, representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and Mr. Yan Chengde, representative of the Chinese Taxpayers Association. All 400 of these electors have been notified by special letter of the election location and date, and the names and license numbers of the drawn electors have been published in Chinese newspapers for public knowledge. Today is the date of the election, and for the sake of prudence, Mr. Yao Zengmu, Deputy Chief Inspector of the Chinese Police Department of the Public Concession, has been specially invited to be the general supervisor. In addition, the only people who can participate in today's election ceremony are the following three types: (1) 400 rickshaw puller electors, all of whom must pass the inspection of their license armbands to enter the venue; (2) Directors of the Public Concession, members of the Mutual Aid Association's custodian committee, directors of the board of directors, and permanent staff; (3) Journalists. The patrol room will send detectives to maintain order at the time. At the time of the election, under the supervision of the general supervisor, the names and license numbers of the electors who have arrived will be written on the blackboard. The number of electors is stipulated to be at least 25 (the election will not be held if the number is insufficient). After the number is sufficient, the general supervisor will announce (1) the purpose of the election, (2) the position of director is an honorary position with no salary, (3) the election procedure is absolutely free. All registered rickshaw pullers have the right to be elected. Before the electors start the election, they can first propose the names and license numbers of the candidates. The names and license numbers of these candidates will be written on a blackboard, which is different from the blackboard on which the names and numbers of the electors are written, and it will be placed where everyone present can see it. When the number of candidates nominated reaches a considerable level, the general supervisor will announce the end of the nomination, and then each elector will vote in turn, selecting two of the candidates. This election ticket will be recorded on the blackboard by the general supervisor or his representative until all the electors have finished voting. Then, the general supervisor will count the votes and announce the two candidates with the most votes as the elected directors. If the number of votes is equal, the matter will be decided by a show of hands. The general supervisor has the right to make appropriate changes to the above methods when necessary.

Public Buses Will Run Between Shanghai and Qibao. The Shanghai-Qibao Route is Scheduled to Start Construction Next Month. 99

Qibao is a large town in western Shanghai, and electricity and telephones have been connected to this port. However, transportation between Shanghai and Qibao has always relied on steamships and rickshaws. The terminal of the British merchant Hongqiao Road public bus is still four miles away from the town. The municipal and county authorities believe that the population of the town is increasing, and more and more people from all walks of life are going to invest in real estate and businesses every year, and it is urgent to actively develop it. Now that Qinggang Road Dongxi has been built, the local gentry plans to build a branch road from Qibao Town, connecting Qinggang Road Hongqiao Road, directly to the concession, which has been approved by the competent authorities and is scheduled to start construction on November 1. It is reported that after the completion of the project, the Shanghai-Qibao public bus will be opened. It will only take 25 minutes from Qibao to the center of the concession, and there will be more than 20 round trips every day. The transportation will be more convenient.

Continued Hearing of the Major Post Office Robbery Case; Li Yi-sheng and Li Xue-shi Granted Bail, Others Remanded in Custody Awaiting Next Wednesday's Hearing 100

On the morning of September 9th, the Shanghai General Post Office was suddenly invaded by a gang of audacious robbers who made off with over 91,000 yuan in cash and banknotes. The security guards escorting the large sum, Lü Rui-lin, and the old clerk Yuan Bing-shu, were shot and killed, while Zhou Yu-chen was wounded by gunfire. Subsequently, the police successively apprehended over a dozen suspects. After investigation, those not implicated were released, while Ji Ren-tang (also known as the Monk Wu Kong), a man from Funing, and one woman, were prosecuted by the police according to the law and handed over to the First Special District Court for investigation. This newspaper has repeatedly reported on the matter. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shu-zi opened the court again, ordering the defendants Ji Ren-tang, Qiu Guo-bin, Li Yi-sheng, Li Xue-shi, Wu Pan-gui, Zhou Yao-shi, Liu Dao-sheng, Ji Wen-bin, Wang Chen-shi, Ji Chen-shi, and Chen Qiu-shi to be brought before the court.

In the continued hearing, the first witness, a Mr. Xu, was summoned. He was questioned about the cotton quilt seized by the police on a certain steamer when Wang Chen-shi and others were apprehended. Xu stated that he could not determine whether it belonged to his wife. Subsequently, Officer No. 5910 from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who was on duty at the post office, was brought to the stand and questioned about his time on duty at the post office on the night of September 8th and on September 9th. Following this, the Western Detective Chief from the Disraeli Road Police Station reported on the investigation into Wang Chen-shi's deposit of 1,000 yuan at the Jin Cheng Bank. Furthermore, Yang Bing-qi, the director of the Revenue and Expenditure Department of the General Post Office, testified that the banknotes stolen from the bureau that day were all mixed denominations. Therefore, even if

stolen money was found on the defendants, it would be impossible to identify it as the original loot. In court, defendant Ji Ren-tang was interrogated. He confessed that he had previously been sentenced to one year and three months of imprisonment for arms trafficking. He was released in October of the year before last and then became acquainted with Wang Chen-shi, with whom he cohabitated at No. 327, Siwenli, Datong Road. Ji Chen-shi was his aunt. The court then presented the confession the suspect had made when arrested in Funing and after being brought to the police station, detailing how he and his accomplices planned the robbery beforehand, and how Liu Xiao-si and Li San opened fire during the robbery, while he seized the hemp sack containing banknotes that the old clerk was carrying, escaping with the loot to the home of a Mr. Liu on Yucai Road in Zhabei for distribution. Unexpectedly, most of the stolen money was

stolen and fled with by Li San, with him and Liu Xiao-si only receiving small amounts that were given to his concubine Chen-shi, and distributed to Qiu Guo-bin and Ji Chen-shi, each receiving several hundred yuan. The next day, he and Liu Xiao-si fled back to Funing. These statements were presented to him for confirmation, but the defendant completely denied them, firmly asserting that he had nothing to do with the robbery and was unaware of it. He claimed that Ji Chen-shi and Qiu Guo-bin were framing him due to a grudge because Wang Chen-shi had become involved with another person and had separated from him. However, Wang Chen-shi confessed that she had been cohabiting with Ji since last month and had never separated. She also detailed the course of Ji Ren-tang's gang robbery, stating that they had only conceived the idea six days prior.

Those involved in the conspiracy were Ji Ren-tang, Liu Xiao-si, Qiu Guo-bin, and a Mr. Wang, who discussed it three or four times, always meeting at her house. On one occasion, a security guard from the post office was also involved in the discussion, but she had never seen the security guard before. On the evening of September 9th, after the robbery, Ji took her to an unfamiliar place, where she received 7,000 yuan. She then gave 3,500 yuan to Liu Xiao-si, 250 yuan to Ji Chen-shi, and 200 yuan to Qiu Guo-bin, and kept 1,000 yuan for herself. The next day, Ji, Liu Xiao-si, and Yang Er-ma-zi (Zhou Yao-shi) returned to their hometown. She went part of the way with them,

returning to Shanghai by boat on the 19th. She then purchased a gold ring engraved with her name. On the 20th, she deposited 1,000 yuan at the Jin Cheng Bank, intending to withdraw the money using the gold ring's seal. At that time, Ji Chen-shi and Qiu Guo-bin both wanted to return to their hometown, and they asked her to go with them. She then carried 1,000 yuan back home for Ji Ren-tang, placing the money under her pillow. The deposit slip for her 1,000 yuan, however, was not taken; she sewed it into the lining of her clothes and hid it in a trunk in her Shanghai residence. When questioned, defendant Zhou Yao-shi gave evasive answers. Qiu Guo-bin admitted that the Monk Wu Kong gave him 200 yuan. After Judge Jiang questioned the remaining defendants one by one, he ordered Li Yi-sheng and Li Xue-shi to each post a 500 yuan surety, while the others were remanded in custody separately to await the next hearing on Wednesday afternoon.

Huang Automobile Company Declares Bankruptcy Yesterday: Sluggish Business, Financial Difficulties, 50,000 Yuan in Debt; Entrusts Lawyers and Accountants to Declare Liquidation According to Law 101

A Central News Agency report states that the China Public Huang Automobile Company, located at No. 534, Pushi Road, Shanghai, was originally founded by an American merchant. In 1928, it was taken over by Chinese businessmen. It currently has one hundred new and old cars and specializes in rental services. In recent years, competition within the industry has been fierce. After attracting customers by lowering prices, although business has been brisk, income has not met expenditure. Furthermore, a dispute over unpaid debts to the Asia Petroleum Factory has severely damaged its reputation. Yesterday, due to financial difficulties, the board of directors decided to cease operations and convened a meeting to handle the salaries and deposits owed to drivers and employees. After negotiations with the responsible parties, a resolution may be reached today. It is reported that the company's debt amounts to 50,000 yuan and is currently being liquidated according to law by entrusted lawyers and accountants. The details are recorded below:

Founding History

The Public Huang Automobile Company has been established for many years. It was initially operated by an American merchant, but due to poor business performance, it declared bankruptcy. The American court announced a public auction, and it was taken over by Chinese businessmen for a bid price of 110,300 yuan, collecting a fixed capital of 100,000 yuan and a working capital of 50,000 yuan. The head office was established on Pushi Road in the French Concession, and branch stations were subsequently added to various thoroughfares throughout the city, totaling eleven locations. It currently has approximately one hundred new cars, all painted yellow, which are quite eye-catching. Two years ago, when oil prices were low, business was very good.

Difficulties

In recent years, the business of renting out automobiles has flourished, leading to widespread price cuts to attract customers. However, with the gradual rise in oil prices and heavy tax burdens, many businesses have found it difficult to cover expenses. Although the company has been able to maintain operations, it has long been unprofitable, resulting in long overdue dividends. Two months ago, it was sued by the Asia Company in the Second Special District Court for owing approximately 10,000 yuan in oil debts. Although a settlement was reached with the condition of "paying off past debts and purchasing with cash in the future," it suffered a significant loss in reputation, leading to the termination of credit for oil purchases. Furthermore, car rentals were not easily collected on time, gradually leading to financial difficulties.

Decision to Close

At that time, the company convened a shareholders' meeting to discuss the difficult situation. It was decided to authorize the board of directors to handle the matter, and if absolutely necessary, to cease operations. Recently, due to fierce competition in the industry, prices were lowered to only 80 cents per 20 minutes, resulting in income not meeting expenditure. The salaries of the company's employees have been in arrears for a month. The day before yesterday, due to the depletion of working capital, operations ceased in the afternoon. That night, the board of directors decided to cease operations and appointed lawyer Guo Cheming and accountant Shen Jiazhen as representatives to liquidate according to law.

Declaration of Liquidation

Yesterday morning, a notice was posted at the entrance of the head office, signed by lawyer Guo Cheming and accountant Shen Jiazhen on behalf of China Public Huang Automobile Co., Ltd., declaring liquidation. The notice stated that, according to the company's board of directors, the company was unable to rotate its capital due to the impact of the economic depression. A shareholder meeting had decided to cease operations and liquidate, and the law firm and accounting firm were appointed as liquidators to handle the liquidation matters. In addition to accepting the commission and reporting it, the company's creditors were requested to bring their debt certificates to the accounting firm for registration within 15 days for verification. Debtors were also requested to send the amounts owed to the accounting firm for verification and receipt within 15 days, otherwise legal action would be taken. Furthermore, anyone interested in taking over the company was requested to contact the accounting firm. This announcement was made on October 23, 1935.

Employee Wage Claims

Approximately 300 company employees had not been paid their salaries for last month. Drivers had also each paid a deposit of 50 yuan. Upon seeing the company cease operations yesterday, they became alarmed and negotiated with the current manager, Zhang Xutang, who persuaded them to wait for liquidation. Police officers were dispatched by the French Concession police to maintain order, and fortunately, no incidents occurred. In the afternoon, ten employee representatives held a meeting with accountant Shen, lawyer Guo, and company representatives in the French Concession police station, but no results were achieved. It is reported that consultations will continue today and a solution may be found. The employees have also submitted petitions to the Municipal Drivers' Association and municipal party and government agencies for review.

Lu Xihou and Others Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment Each in Fraud Case 102

Following the collapse of the China Industrial Bank, the Shanghai Municipal Council's lawyer, Ru Bao-yi, filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court's Criminal Division against the bank's chairman, Lu Xihou, and key staff members Lu Mengxiang, Sun Xiren, and Lu Zutong, on charges of fraud. The trial has already concluded, and details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Qian Hongye, the presiding judge of the Criminal Division, ascended the bench in Criminal Court No. 1 and pronounced the verdict. The main text of the verdict states that Lu Xihou, Lu Mengxiang, and Lu Zutong, knowing that the matters were false, caused public officials to record them in official documents under their charge, causing harm to others. Each was sentenced to six months of imprisonment. Lu Xihou and Lu Mengxiang were found not guilty of other charges. Sun Xiren was found not guilty. During the appeal period, all remained on their original bail.

United Shipping Company Successfully Trials Navigation to Yancheng 103

Due to the impact of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's joint transportation operations with the Longhai Railway and the sluggish market, the United Shipping Company's business has been severely affected. In order to seek a way out and develop, it recently received approval from the Longhai Railway Bureau to handle non-joint transportation goods at Lianyungang and made meticulous plans to open up a new route to Yancheng, as well as ports such as Wanfu and Funing. This time, it specially dispatched the Zhengzhou steamship directly to Yancheng, and it is reported that it has safely arrived at the port. Yancheng is located in the heart of Jiangsu Province and is rich in agricultural products. Steamships have never reached the area before. The company previously pioneered the Haizhou route, which led to the prosperity of the local market. Now, it is pioneering the Yancheng route. The future prosperity of the port can be expected. If the company continues to work hard to develop shipping, it is truly commendable.

Zoo's Tiger Dies of Lung Disease; Tuberculosis Is Fiercer Than the Tiger; Lungs Found to Be Decayed After Dissection; Taxidermy by Instrument Factory 104

The tiger at the Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road died after suffering from pleurisy while undergoing external treatment. The zoo had posted a notice outside its enclosure stating, "The tiger is currently ill." According to information gathered by a Datong News Agency reporter from the zoo, the tiger died a few days ago. It is reported that the tiger had been purchased from Guangxi by the former Municipal Public School Garden for 950 yuan. It was moved to the Municipal Zoo when it opened and displayed there. When the zoo noticed that the tiger was gradually weakening, it immediately reported it to veterinary consultant Wang Zhao-qi (Chief of the Second Section of the Health Bureau), who transported it for treatment, but it was ineffective. After it died, a dissection was immediately performed, revealing that the lung disease had reached the third stage and the lungs were severely decayed. The Eastern Instrument Company has been commissioned to prepare a taxidermied specimen. The zoo also plans to find another tiger to fill the vacancy.

Yesterday at 1:45 AM, in the still of the night, a young woman in fashionable attire suddenly threw herself into the river from the Waibaidu Bridge at the mouth of the Suzhou Creek. At that time, pedestrians had not completely disappeared from the road, and some had seen her jump into the water. Laundry Apprentice Crushed to Death by Car; Coroner Morrison Performs Autopsy; Jin Amao Detained for Interrogation 106

He Yi Tai Coal Store at Number 853 East of the Rihui Bridge outside Longhua Road in Shanghai South sent a driver Jin Amao (37 years old, from Chuansha, residing in a bungalow in the Xishenjia Ham, Albert Road, French Concession) at the morning of the 22nd, drove a number 227 truck loaded with coal to send to customers in the northern part of the city. At 11:20 at noon, the driver Jin Amao drove to the side of Ningbo Hall on Balili Bridge Road in the French Concession, heading north from the south. When he arrived at the Airlike Road intersection, a number 10 tram of the French company's Route 5 going to and from the Ximen North Station also headed north from the south. When it stopped near the Ningbo Road station in front of the truck, Mo Ruisheng (16 years old, from Shaoxing), an apprentice from the Nanhua Chang Laundry Store opened by Chen Jinchang from Shaoxing at Number 540 Huacheng Road, Min’guo Road in the French Concession, came out to collect clothes at Yuqingli, Xinxibridge Street (that is, Balili Bridge Road). Apprentice Mo walked along the east wall of the Ningbo Hall on Balili Bridge Road, heading north. At a point of over ten feet north of the Airlike Road intersection, he suddenly walked diagonally to the northwest, intending to cross the road. At that time, Jin Amao's truck intended to overtake the tram and drove straight north past the east side of the tram. Unexpectedly, apprentice Mo walked diagonally to the center of the road and could not avoid it. He was hit by the right fender of the truck, and his left hand was crushed by the wheels. His chest was also injured. Instantly, fresh blood spurted from his mouth. The patrolman saw the scene and immediately brought the driver Jin Amao and the truck to the Mailan Police Station. At the same time, he immediately sent an ambulance to take the injured person to the Guangci Hospital. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died upon arrival at the hospital. The body was moved to the mortuary of Tongren Fuyuan for an autopsy. At that time, it was impossible to investigate the name and family of the deceased. Until yesterday morning, the deceased's shop owner Chen Jinchang went to the mortuary to identify him and reported to the police. At noon, Wang Ren, the prosecutor of the Second Special Court, accompanied forensic doctor Wei, secretary Peng Yi, and others to the morgue to confirm the body and ascend the case. The police dispatched detectives to send the defendant, driver Jin Amao, to the case. The official questioned Jin about the circumstances of the accident. The deceased's shop owner Chen Jinchang reported that the deceased's family was in Shaoxing and a letter had been sent to notify them. He could not lead the corpse for collection on behalf of them; they would wait for the family members to arrive in Shanghai. Witness Yu Fusheng, a French tram driver, and Sun Wu and lawyer Fei Wenpin did not arrive. Prosecutor Wang proclaimed that Mo Ruisheng had died from injuries caused by the truck, and the body was handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Hall to collect it on their behalf for the family to collect. The defendant was sent to the court by the police department for legal handling. After the autopsy, the police sent the defendant Jin Amao to Criminal Court No. 1 of the Second Special Court. Judge Xiong questioned him, and Yuan Jia from the police department said that the defendant caused death due to negligence in his work, and the police investigation was not completed. He asked for an extension of the deadline to investigate the case and sue for trial. Defendant Yan Linqing defended the lawyer. The court verified the report, questioned the defendant, and then instructed that the hearing be postponed to 2 pm on the 28th, and the defendant would be remanded in custody. It is reported that the defendant's family is poor. His wife died last year, and he has an elderly father in his seventies and two young children to support. Now that the defendant is in custody because of the accident, the livelihood of the elderly and young at the door will be difficult from now on.

Zhou Shoutang, a native of Ningbo, was the manager of the Qingdao branch of the Huakang Military Uniform Store at No. 230 Xizang Road. Switching Moldy Cigarettes; Fighting Leads to Death; Chen Bingquan Dies Tragically; Body Verified by Court 108

Chen Bingkui, a native of Hangzhou, 44 years old, lived at No. 493 Guangdong Road, worked as a professional "da chang" (that is, those who blow and sing to attract attention for general news stores). On the morning of the 16th of this month, Chen went to Ruichangxiang Tobacco and Paper Store at No. 64 Beihai Road to buy a pack of Ding Ding brand cigarettes. When he carried it back to smoke it, he suddenly found mold spots on the cigarettes. He took them back to the store to exchange them with the staff Jiang Huai (22 years old, from Wuxi). Jiang refused. The two sides started arguing. Then the two fought near the store. Later, Chen was defeated and returned home injured. At 11:00 AM of the same morning, the pain was unbearable, so he went to the store again to negotiate. After someone reported the incident to No. 2522 Chinese constable stationed nearby, Chen and Jiang were brought to the Laozha Police Station together. Deputy Chinese Detective Zhang Yuanjing and detective Xu Dezhong were ordered to investigate. Then Chen was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, and a public prosecution was filed against Jiang in the First Special District Court. On the evening before last, at 8:50 PM, Chen died due to the worsening of his injuries. The body was moved to the mortuary on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Tang, the prosecutor of the First Special Court, accompanied two forensic doctors, Wei and Zhang, and secretary Wang Zuyi to the morgue to verify the body. First, the detectives reported the previous situation, saying that the defendant had only been prosecuted for injury crimes. Now that Chen had died of his injuries, the indictment against the defendant had been changed. Jiang Huai said that the Ding Ding brand cigarettes that the deceased held were just in batches yesterday and would not be moldy. Because they were not purchased in my store, I did not allow him to change them. He scolded me and pulled me out. At the door of the leather store at No. 66 next door, he was injured when he hit the wooden frame of the store because he used too much force. Then the leather store owner persuaded him to leave. Later, he called a few people to come, and I was afraid of extortion, so I went to the police station. He denied hitting him and causing injury. The wife of the deceased, Chen Zhushi, said that the deceased was beaten and injured, and later went there. He only saw him leave in a rickshaw, but did not call anyone. She asked for an explanation. After Hua constable No. 1322 reported the situation, Tang Jun confirmed that the deceased, Chen Bingkui, male, had died of injuries during his lifetime. The body was handed over to his representative, Chen Zhushi, to sign and return to the coffin.

Armed Robbers Resist Arrest, Gunfire Frequent on Changbang Road Yesterday Morning; Three Robbers Flee after Looting, Open Fire to Resist Arrest Mid-Way; One Robber Captured in Tavern, Three-Year-Old Child Injured 109

Around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, armed robbers resisting arrest suddenly occurred near the junction of Changbang Road and Chongqing Road in the Public Concession. Gunfire rang out frequently for a while, and passersby fled in panic. As a result, one robber was caught, and a stray bullet injured a child, whose condition is very critical. Details are recorded below:

Sudden Appearance of Three Robbers

Around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, three robbers suddenly appeared at the Wanlong Tobacco and Paper Store at No. 28 Gujia Lane, Luban Road, French Concession. One robber was wearing a Western suit and carrying a pistol. At that time, the store owner Zheng Shouyin and the store's employees were fast asleep and were awakened by the robbers who forbade them to make a sound. They were robbed of approximately 500 yuan in large and small coins.

Flight with Looted Goods

The three robbers fled together towards Hualong Road. At that time, the two robbers wearing Chinese clothing split up and fled south, while the robber in the Western suit with the gun ran north. The owner of the store, Zheng Shouwangyin, had already tracked them out and urgently reported to the local patrolman, who blew his whistle and chased closely. The robber knew things were going badly and immediately fled north.

Frequent Gunfire

When they were chasing to Changbang Road near Edward Road, the robber was about to cross the Public Concession when he was spotted by the patrolman there, who drew his gun to intercept him. Seeing this, the robber immediately raised his gun and fired at the patrolman, who returned fire. Thus, gunfire rang out frequently on Changbang Road, and passersby fled in a panic. Both sides fired more than a dozen shots at each other.

Fleeing into a Tavern

After a while, the robber ran out of bullets and was unable to hold on. He took the opportunity to escape into Male Lane and then slipped from the lane into the back door of the Dahonglou Tavern and went straight into the store hall. At that time, the tavern's employees and apprentices were sound asleep. In desperation, the robber used his quick wit to squeeze into an employee's quilt, hoping to get lucky.

Captured Without Resistance

At that time, the detectives saw the robber flee into the lane. Since only the back door of Dahonglou was not closed, they were sure that he had fled into the store, and they immediately rushed in to search. The robber surrendered and was taken to the Chengdu Road Police Station. After the Western Detective Chief questioned him in detail, the robber confessed that his name was Li Dianbing, 24 years old, from Shandong, and he admitted that he had ganged up to commit the robbery.

Child Wounded by Bullet

He also confessed the names of many accomplices. When the detectives went to arrest them at the addresses provided, the robbers had already heard the news and fled. During the shootout, a three-year-old child named Dai Agou was injured by a stray bullet, and his condition is very critical. Currently, the Chengdu Road Police Station and the French Police Station are working together to track down the remaining members of the gang.

Yu Qiaqing Continues to Wire for Cessation: Xuchang Company Purchasing Tobacco 110

Collaboration between Tobacco Gathering Industry and Cigarette Industry to Prevent Foreign Economic Aggression

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai previously received a report from the Tobacco Industry Association stating that the Xuchang Company was being manipulated by foreign merchants to monopolize tobacco purchasing. They telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and the Ministers of Finance and Industry, requesting a ban. Subsequently, Yang Peiqing, the founder and shareholder of the Xuchang Company, issued a statement exposing the company's inside story, further revealing the truth. Now, it is reported that Mr. Yu Qiaqing, considering that this case concerns foreign invasion of the inland economy, has again telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Finance and Industry, urgently requesting their intervention to stop it. At the same time, the Tobacco Leaf Association also hosted cigarette merchants, explaining everything. Details are recorded as follows:

Yu Qiaqing Continues to Wire for Cessation: Xuchang Company Purchasing Tobacco

Distributed to Military Committee Chairman Chiang, Executive Yuan President Wang, Finance Minister Kong, Industry Minister Chen Junjian: Tobacco leaves are produced in the Xuchang area of Henan. Tobacco merchants from Beijing, Tianjin, Shanghai, and Hankou, as well as cigarette manufacturers from various ports, regularly purchase there. No fewer than 300,000 Chinese people rely on this for a living. Years ago, the British American Tobacco Company, through its Chinese staff, set up a factory in Xuchang to collect tobacco, manufacture it, and sell it, monopolizing and oppressing the people, causing them suffering. Fortunately, the authorities of the province discovered this and immediately ordered it to stop, preserving the livelihoods of the Chinese people. Unexpectedly, now some people are colluding with foreign merchants, reviving the old trick. Initially, the Xuchang Company came forward to plan it, and then, under the name of the Yu-Su Cured Tobacco Factory, gradually transferred control to the British American Tobacco Company. Now, they have gathered huge funds to set up a factory there, and are already heavily purchasing tobacco, planning to sweep everything away. The industry association sees this as a foreign economic invasion, and if it is implemented, the livelihoods of the Chinese people will surely be cut off. Therefore, they are appealing to all parties to jointly stop it. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, after investigating and clarifying the facts, telegraphed on their behalf, and Yang Peiqing, a shareholder and founder of the Xuchang Company, also declared that collusion with foreign merchants was inappropriate, revealing the truth and stating that he would never recognize it. However, recently it has been heard that those colluding with foreign merchants dare to use the name of the Tobacco Leaf Improvement Committee to decorate their words and deceive, hoping to achieve their private goals. Because this matter concerns the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people, and many of those engaged in this are from Ningbo, due to the deep friendship with our hometown, we dare not suppress the information. Therefore, we urgently appeal to your seats in the Yuan and Ministries to quickly take charge and issue orders to the Henan Provincial Government to vigorously stop it, so as to avoid harming the local area and maintain the livelihoods of the people, benefiting the masses. We all deeply appreciate and praise you. Yu Hede of the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai bows respectfully.

Tobacco Leaf Industry Reception

The Shanghai Tobacco Leaf Industry Association hosted cigarette factory owners last night at the Shipping Club. Dozens of people attended. First, Chen Chenglun, Chairman of the Association, and Wang Zuoting, representative of the Executive Committee, delivered speeches, stating that the Xuchang Company is nominally a Chinese business but in reality a tool of foreign economic aggression, and that both the tobacco leaf industry and the cigarette factory industry will suffer from it, hoping for cooperation to stop it, and so on. Then, Yang Peiqing, the founder and shareholder of the Xuchang Company, reported on all the contents of the Xuchang Company and the process of transferring sovereign industry into the hands of foreign merchants, detailing how Wu Tingsheng colluded with foreign merchants, lost national sovereignty, and damaged the legal interests of shareholders. Leaders of cigarette factories stood up to speak, saying that after listening to Mr. Yang's statements, they knew all the inside stories of the Xuchang Company, and especially understood that Mr. Wu Tingsheng's so-called tobacco leaf improvement was not for public good but for personal gain. Considering the public interest, we must do our best to resist his actions. Then, Yu Qiaqing stood up to speak, saying that for the sake of the country and compatriots, Qiaqing had to speak out righteously. While the tobacco leaf industry is primarily harmed by this matter, the cigarette factory industry is also greatly harmed because foreign tobacco companies have strong capital, light raw material prices, and advance payment of unified taxes also gives them an advantage. Therefore, the cost of production is reduced, and the torrent of dumping cannot be resisted. If they are further allowed to manipulate the raw materials of the domestic tobacco industry, then in the future, the raw materials needed by Chinese cigarette factories will be difficult to obtain. Even if they are available, they will not be affordable at high prices. Once the raw material market is occupied, they can raise prices or suppress prices, adapt to changes, and do whatever they want. Therefore, the harm to the cigarette factory industry is very serious. Furthermore, the company purchases tobacco leaves based on low prices as the principle and high prices as the exception. Tobacco farmers also suffer no small amount. Today, the cigarette factory industry and the tobacco leaf industry are gathering together, hoping that everyone will unite and cooperate sincerely to determine concrete measures to stop this matter. Finally, those present discussed all the countermeasures and proceeded actively.

The Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company, large in scale and well-equipped, is a domestic national product factory with a long history. Previously, due to insufficient capital turnover, it suspended operations this spring. Now, it is being operated by a banking consortium formed by the business community in this city. It reopened yesterday. Details are recorded as follows:

Organizing a Banking Consortium to Support Resumption of Business

The company's factory is located at Gaolang Bridge on Huade Road. Since last winter, due to rural bankruptcy and weak purchasing power, inventory piled up. Furthermore, with the sudden economic collapse of society, capital was difficult to turn over, and it had to suspend operations, which has been the case for half a year. Now, the business community in this city, in order to support the national product industry and relieve unemployed workers, has specially organized a banking consortium to operate the company. The organization has been successfully formed. The name of the banking consortium is "Huiye." The office is located at No. 8, Dongfukang Lane, Tianjin Road.

The Banking Consortium's Notice of Reopening Yesterday

The factory reopened yesterday morning. All accounting and management matters are handled by personnel dispatched by the banking consortium. The banking consortium's notice is as follows: Respectfully announcing that our banking consortium, in order to support the production of national products and relieve unemployed workers, has specifically pooled funds to operate the Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Company, scheduled to reopen for business on October 23. We have hired many specialized technicians to carefully research and strive to improve our products, and we also offer printing and dyeing services for all kinds of cotton cloth at exceptionally low prices. Any cotton cloth merchants who entrust us with printing and dyeing services for gray cloth are welcome to come to our banking consortium's office for contact. We will serve you sincerely. Hereafter, all purchases of various materials must be based on the banking consortium's seal. We hereby declare this. We hope you will take note.

Zhang Xiuzhe Returns Home After Completing His Studies 116

Studied in Japan for Ten Years and Authored Extensively

Mr. Zhang Xiuzhe, a graduate of the Graduate School of Tokyo Imperial University in Japan, has been studying international law, diplomatic history, international politics, and other issues in Japan for about ten years. Recently, his monumental work in Japanese, "The National Government, Diplomacy, and Diplomatic Administration," was published in Tokyo, causing a sensation in Japanese academic circles. It was praised as a rare masterpiece in diplomatic history. The first edition of the book sold out within days. Among them, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government purchased ten copies, and the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs specially purchased fifty copies to distribute to its embassies and consulates in various countries as a reference for understanding Chinese diplomacy. The General Staff Headquarters of the National Government also purchased twenty copies, and the Minister of Interior Huang Fu purchased fifty copies, the Beining Railway Bureau purchased twenty copies, etc. Other pre-orders were extremely crowded, showing the importance that China and Japan attach to the book. The book is the first publication by a Chinese student on political and diplomatic issues written in Japanese. The arguments are all based on the Chinese position, introducing the revolutionary diplomacy of the National Government and explaining the Kuomintang's foreign policy without omission. In particular, it advocates that Japan must first abolish consular jurisdiction in China as a sign of sincerity in resolving China's diplomatic problems. Zhang graduated from the Department of Diplomacy of National Jinan University and is a researcher at the International Law Society. Yesterday, he returned home after completing his studies, and relatives and friends came to see him one after another. It is heard that he plans to leave for Beijing within days. It is said that Zhang's works are now also available for sale at the Neishan Bookstore at the bottom of North Sichuan Road in this city. In addition, Zhang has also authored "Secret History of Japanese Diplomacy," "Outline of International Law," and "Chronology of Important Political and Diplomatic Events of the National Government," all of which are the crystallization of Zhang's research in Japan.

Guangdong Miss's Maid Abuse Case Opens 119

Righteous People All Testify in Court, Prosecutor Has Already Filed Indictment

The case of Miss Tan Huizhu, a Guangdong native residing in Deren Lane, Xingjia Bridge, in this city, who abused her maid, has attracted much attention from the public since it was exposed by righteous people and the China Children's Welfare Association. On the 3rd of this month, Prosecutor Zhang Zi of the District Court formally filed an indictment with the Criminal Court. On the morning of the 22nd of this month (i.e., the day before yesterday), the judge opened the court to hear the case. Zhang Yueru, an officer of the China Children's Welfare Association, also went to attend the hearing. The details are recorded below.

Opening of the Hearing

First, the bailiff brought Tan Huizhu to the court. The judge asked her about her age and origin, and then stated the prosecutor's charges of illegally injuring the maid Xuejuan. According to Tan Huizhu's testimony, she denied the injury and claimed that Xuejuan was her cousin. Then, the maid Xuejuan was questioned, but because of her age and language barrier, she did not understand much. Then, Zhao Baoqing, the gatekeeper of Deshi Lane, was questioned. According to his testimony, Tan Huizhu had been living in Deren Lane for more than three months. She often abused the maid Xuejuan. In early September, she used a red-hot iron hook to burn multiple areas of her face. Then, the reporter Tan Guanman was questioned. According to his testimony, Tan Huizhu was his neighbor and kept a maid Xuejuan, whom she often abused. If she did not comply with her wishes, she would whip her. In early last month, she used torture and burned Xuejuan's face with a red-hot iron hook in many places. Because he felt sorry for Xuejuan, he specially reported it to the China Children's Welfare Association, asking them to find a way to help her, entirely out of righteousness and humanity. Finally, the household registration police officer from Yongxing Road Police Station was questioned. According to his testimony, on September 10, he accompanied a representative from the China Children's Welfare Association to investigate Tan Huizhu's abuse of her maid and the burning of her cheeks, which was indeed the case. The weapon, the iron hook, is still stored in the police station for record. After the judge finished questioning, he announced the adjournment because further investigation was necessary. A hearing was scheduled for another day. Tan Huizhu was released on bail of one thousand yuan in cash. If she cannot pay bail, she will be remanded in custody.

Original Indictment

"Defendant Tan Huizhu, female, 20 years old, from Dongguan, residing in Deren Lane, Xingjia Bridge. The defendant in the case of obstructing freedom and injury, Detective No. 3578 of the Republic of China, has been investigated by this prosecutor and is deemed to warrant prosecution. The defendant's criminal facts and evidence, as well as the relevant legal provisions, are listed below: (1) Criminal Facts: Tan Huizhu is from Guangdong and resides at No. 17, Deren Lane, Xingjiaqiao Road, in this city. Last summer, she bought a maid named Xuejuan (now 8 years old) in her hometown for service. On the morning of September 1, Tan Huizhu ordered Xuejuan to light the stove, and because the charcoal fire was flying around, she used a charcoal fire to brand Xuejuan's right cheek. The matter was reported to the neighbor Tan Li, who informed her husband Tan Guanman to report it. The case was sent by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. (2) Evidence and Legal Provisions: Xuejuan has been examined by a forensic doctor and found to have a light white superficial scar on her left cheek, the size of a broad bean, surrounded by a cloud-like brown halo, the size of a copper coin. On her right cheek, there are two light white superficial scars, shaped like silkworms, surrounded by a cloud-like brown halo, approximately the size of a silver dollar. It is determined to be a burn from a hot object. Tan Huizhu's parents and Xuejuan all stated that it was a charcoal fire burn, caused by the ashes flying up when Xuejuan was lighting the charcoal stove. However, she claimed that the secretary of the neighborhood went to secretly investigate. According to the report, Xuejuan is indeed Tan Huizhu's maid and is often abused. It is confirmed that the burns were inflicted. Zhao Baoqing, the gatekeeper of the neighborhood, was questioned and stated that Tan Xuejuan is indeed a maid and that he heard people in the neighborhood say that the maid's face was burned and that the young lady of the house was very fierce, etc. The statements of Tan Li are consistent with the statements of Zhao Baoqing and the investigation report. From this, it can be seen that Xuejuan's burns are evidence of Tan Huizhu's abuse. Moreover, the injuries to Xuejuan's cheeks are not insignificant. It is unreasonable for Tan Huizhu's parents to say that it was done by the neighbor Tan Li but remain silent all along. Moreover, the report in this case was made by the husband of Tan Li, which shows that it was a retaliatory act. Based on the above, the defendant has committed the crimes under Article 296, paragraph 1, and Article 286, paragraph 1, of the Criminal Code and should be prosecuted in accordance with Article 230, paragraph 1, of the Code of Criminal Procedure. Respectfully submitted to the Criminal Court of this Court."

Russian Fish Weighing Fraud Case Trial Record

Each Defendant's Testimony; Awaiting Summons of Soviet Russian Assistance Association Representative

Last winter, the salted fish industry in this city purchased 50,000 piculs of salmon from the Soviet Russian Assistance Association Foreign Firm. During the weighing at the wharf, there was a fraud of 6,700 piculs, worth over 70,000 yuan. Now, Zhu Xusheng, Chang Junfa, Zhao Lianfang, and others who jointly committed the fraud, feared that once the matter was exposed, they would be suspected of joint fraud. Moreover, the case of tax evasion was serious and should be reported. Therefore, on July 14, they surrendered to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, which was instructed to transfer them to the Local Court Procuratorate. Prosecutor Xiao Jin'ying conducted several investigations and concluded that the defendants Zhu Xusheng, Chang Junfa, Zhao Lianfang, Weng Zhaofang, Ye Zhenchang, Zheng Yunsheng, and others should be released on bail. Meanwhile, a public prosecution was filed according to law. The facts of the crime were that defendants Weng Zhaofang, Ye Zhenchang, and Zheng Yunsheng all opened fish shops. Last year, they ordered 50,000 piculs of salmon from the Soviet Russian Assistance Association Foreign Firm. On November 13, December 23, and January 6 of this year, when the fish ships delivered the fish at the Yangjiadu Wharf, Weng Zhaofang and others ordered Zhu Xusheng to consult with workers Chang Junfa and Zhao Lianfang, and shipping clerks Ye Zhenqin and Zhang Benhua, etc., to lift the carrying poles when the fish boxes were weighed, so that the quantity was reduced. A total of 6,700 piculs of fish were obtained from the three ships, worth 70,000 yuan in foreign currency. Presiding Judge Wu Deying had held court to examine the case but had not concluded it and was awaiting further trial. Now, it is learned that at 2:00 PM yesterday, Judge Wu specially opened the third session to hear the case. The lawyers Zhu Yakui, Zhang Shizhao, and Peng Yuanxun, etc., who had been hired by the defendants, arrived in court one after another to defend them. First, the wharf coolies Chen Shiyi, Chen San, Pan Huaiyu, Song Changhong, and others were summoned to the case. According to their testimony, when the salmon arrived at the wharf, they were responsible for carrying it. Chang Junfa, Zhu Xusheng, Ye Zhenqin, and others secretly instructed them to commit fraud. When carrying the fish for weighing, the ropes were not completely loosened, so that the quantity could be reduced. They were promised that after the salmon in the warehouse was sold out, they would be given a share of the fraudulent profits. But now it has been sold out for a long time, and they have not yet been paid. The official asked if the foreign weighers were present at the scene. They answered yes. The official asked if the foreigners interfered when they did not loosen the ropes. They answered that they did interfere, but Ye Zhenqin told them to be bold and do as they were told, and that he would take responsibility for everything. The official asked how much each coolie was paid per day. They answered that they were paid 100 copper coins per day and a bonus of one yuan. Next, Chang Junfa testified that each box of salmon should weigh more than 70 pounds, but due to the fraud, it only weighed more than 60 pounds. Then, Zhu Xusheng testified that Ye Zhenchang and Ye Zhenqin were brothers, and Zhang Benhua was Ye's brother-in-law, so Zhang was assigned as the bookkeeper. They ordered the coolies not to loosen the ropes. It was found that the salmon was purchased by Huafu Fish Shop, Shenfeng Fish Shop, etc. Because they were not familiar with Russian, Ye Zhenchang, the owner of Zhenda Foreign Firm, came forward to order the fish. Next, Zhao Lianfang testified that he was a shipping clerk. Huafu Fish Shop was organized by 24 fish shops. Next, Zhang Benhua testified that he was a shipping clerk for Zhenda Foreign Firm. The salmon was ordered by Zhenda Foreign Firm, and the fish shops turned to Zhenda to buy it. Next, Ye Zhenqin testified that he used to be in the fish business and is now in the newspaper business. When the salmon arrived at the wharf last year, he was responsible for copying the goods at the wharf. Zhao Lianfang was the shipping clerk for Huafu Fish Shop. Huafu Fish Shop was organized by 26 fish shops and specialized in salmon business. The salmon was ordered by Zhenda Foreign Firm from the Soviet Russian Assistance Association. The official asked if Huafu Shenfeng Fish Shop ordered it but used the name of Zhenda Foreign Firm to purchase it. He answered no. Next, Zheng Yunsheng testified that he was the manager of Shengji Fish Shop at No. 83, 16th Pier. The official asked what position he held in Huafu before. He answered that he was a purchasing agent. The manager of Huafu was surnamed Fang. Huafu was formed by 26 fish shops. Next, Weng Zhaofang testified that he was 53 years old and a traveling salesman for Jieshun Salted Goods Shop on Gualou Street outside Xiaodongmen. This lawsuit was instigated by someone. Next, Ye Zhenchang testified that he was the manager of Zhenda Foreign Firm. The official asked why Zhu Xusheng, Zhao Lianfang, Chang Junfa, and others were suing him. He answered that they wanted to blackmail him and buy out the wharf coolies. The official said that according to him, they were blackmailing him and buying out the wharf coolies, but they had not yet succeeded in blackmailing him and had to spend their capital first. At this point, the court said that there would be no debate today. The representatives of the Soviet Russian Assistance Association would be summoned to court for questioning to verify the facts. The defendants were still released on their original bail.
