Education News

China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture to Discuss Free Education Funds 125

Investigation of National Secondary School Problems Still in Question

Special Dispatch from Beiping: The Board of Directors of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture will hold its second general meeting of the year in Shanghai on the 26th. The directors in Beiping, Li Shizeng, Hu Shi, Jin Shuchu, Zhou Yichun, and Executive Secretary Sun Hongfen, etc., left Beiping for Shanghai around the 20th. Director-General Ren Hongjun, who also serves as the president of Sichuan University, flew from Chengdu to Shanghai on the 19th by Eurasian giant aircraft to attend the meeting.

Four Items on the Meeting Agenda

The meeting agenda has been decided by the Executive Committee, mainly including four items: (1) Work reports from the Secretary-General, Accounting, and Documentation departments; (2) Discussion on how to handle the Ministry of Education's request for the Foundation to subsidize 150,000 yuan for compulsory education expenses; (3) Discussion on how to proceed with the investigation of national secondary school problems, or whether to postpone it; (4) The Foundation's rules of procedure were drafted when the Foundation was established in 1920 and are quite outdated and not very applicable to the current situation. In order to reorganize internal work, the Foundation decided to promote the discussion of how to draft new rules of procedure at this meeting.

Compulsory Education Funding Problem

The compulsory education funding subsidy problem is the most difficult to resolve among the issues to be discussed at this meeting. The Ministry of Education originally convened a joint meeting of various Boxer Indemnity organizations to promote and universalize compulsory education in the country, and it was agreed to request the Foundation to subsidize 400,000 yuan. However, when the Foundation held its annual meeting in April of this year, it discussed the matter. As a result, the Foundation felt that due to the economic downturn in recent years, its finances were already insufficient to allocate and it was unable to raise this large sum, so it rejected the request. Later, the Ministry of Education reduced the amount to 150,000 yuan and still requested the Foundation to subsidize it. The Foundation felt that it could not refuse, so it planned to allocate funds from the foreign exchange fees saved over the past two years, but it could only raise 70,000 to 80,000 yuan, which was still half of the planned amount. Therefore, this meeting will raise this issue for discussion.

Dr. Monroe's Proposal

Dr. Paul Monroe, President of the International Education Research Association, Dean of the Teachers College of Columbia University in the United States, and Director of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, came to China this year. In view of the rapid development of secondary education in China in the past ten years, but due to regional differences, the levels are uneven, and the Ministry of Education lacks investigation. The Ministry of Education only investigated national secondary education up to 1930. In order to have accurate investigation and improve it, Dr. Monroe proposed that the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture should carry out this work, and famous educators could be invited from the United States to help voluntarily. The Foundation also considered this matter to be very important, but it was not easy to carry out and required the employment of many specialized personnel. It was estimated that it would take more than a year to complete and would cost 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. Therefore, it will be discussed how to proceed under the current situation of insufficient funds, or whether to suspend it.

Polish Government Subsidy for One Chinese Student to Study in Poland 126

Ministry of Education Formulates Selection Method

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the national and provincial universities and independent colleges with engineering departments on the 22nd, stating: "According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' document No. 9240 on October 2nd, 1935, and the Polish Minister's note on September 24th, the Ministry of Education of this country, in order to enhance cultural relations between China and Poland, plans to establish a scholarship for the academic year 1935-1936, with 250 Polish zlotys per month, specifically to subsidize one Chinese student to study in Poland. According to the opinion of the Ministry of Education of this country, this subsidy is limited to twelve months and will be given at the beginning of the academic year, that is, starting from October 1st, 1935. However, if the selected student wishes to study at any university in Poland, the Ministry of Education plans to add some subsidies for tuition fees. If the student does not wish to attend classes at any university, he/she may go to Poland after October 1st, and the subsidy will be calculated from the date of his/her arrival in Poland, deducting twelve months. In addition, student subsidies are paid monthly, and students can start receiving them after reporting to the Higher Education Department of the Polish Ministry of Education upon arrival in Poland. Round-trip travel expenses to Poland are to be borne by the students themselves, but they can live in student dormitories. As for the method of selecting this subsidized student, the Minister believes that it is best for the Chinese Ministry of Education to liaise with the Polish Embassy in Shanghai to handle it. The above-mentioned points are requested to be forwarded to the Ministry of Education of your country. The Minister also hopes that this proposal will make the cultural relations between China and Poland closer. Accordingly, please investigate, etc." The number of students for this subsidy is now stipulated to be those studying civil engineering or mechanical engineering. The Ministry will provide 800 yuan in national currency for travel expenses to and from the country. Regarding the application qualifications and selection methods, eight regulations have been formulated. In addition to separate orders, a copy of the "Measures for Selecting Subsidized Students to Study in Poland" is enclosed for the school to be informed.

Attached: Measures for Selecting Subsidized Students to Study in Poland. 1. Number of students: one. 2. Departments: Civil Engineering or Mechanical Engineering. 3. Amount of subsidy: 250 Polish zlotys per month subsidized by the Polish Ministry of Education, plus some tuition fees, and 800 yuan in national currency subsidized by the Chinese Ministry of Education for travel expenses to and from the country. 4. Term: Tentatively set for one year. 5. Application qualifications: Applicants for this subsidy must have graduated from the Department of Civil Engineering or Mechanical Engineering of a national or provincial university of engineering or a national or provincial independent college of engineering, have held technical positions related to their field of study for more than two years, and be in good health. They must also be recommended by their original school, with a limit of two recommendations per school. 6. Application deadline and procedures: Before November 5th, the school must send six copies of the recommended students' academic transcripts and work performance, along with two recent 4-inch half-length photos, to the Ministry. 7. Selection method: Determined by examination. A. Examination date: November 15th. B. Examination subjects: A. English, German, French, or Polish (choose one). B. Calculus. C. Applied Mechanics and Strength of Materials. D. Hydraulics and River Engineering or Principles of Machinery and Mechanical Design. C. Examination location: Nanjing Ministry of Education. 8. Departure date: Before January 10th, 1936.

Shanghai Employment Guidance Association Hosts Welcome Banquet; Experts Express Their Opinions

Since its establishment, the National Academic Work Consulting Office has spared no effort in consulting, investigating, and introducing jobs, and has achieved considerable results. Recently, the new director of the office, Mr. Wang Zhaorong, came to Shanghai to meet with leaders from all walks of life in order to connect with them and promote the prospects for registered personnel. Subsequently, Pan Yangyao, Shou Yicheng, Liu Zhanen, Cheng Jicheng, and others expressed their opinions: (1) Visit leaders in the industrial and commercial sectors to solicit their opinions on hiring specialized technical personnel and university graduates, and compile them into a book so that job seekers can follow them. (2) Request the banks to jointly raise funds for small industrial loans so that those with specialized skills or special inventions but lacking funds to start a business can have the opportunity to obtain loans to start a business. (3) Communicate more with those in charge of personnel departments in various agencies and banks to broaden employment opportunities. (4) Set up more offices to facilitate communication. (5) The Office should convene a national discussion meeting of national experts and job guidance and referral agencies every year for publicity and to gather ideas. (6) For university graduates who have been successful in starting their own businesses, a detailed investigation should be conducted on the process of starting the business and the path to success, and the results should be published to encourage university graduates to start their own businesses. (7) Expand publicity so that all parties understand the situation of the Office. The meeting ended around 2:00 PM.

The Problem of Study Load and Teaching Time for Middle School Students (Part 3) 132

— Yi Ping

Currently, the weekly teaching hours stipulated in our country are 36 hours for the first three semesters of junior high school, 25 hours for the fourth semester, 36 hours for the fifth semester, and 35 hours for the sixth semester (each of these includes scout training). For senior high school, the weekly teaching hours are 34 hours for the first three semesters, 33 hours for the fourth semester, and 31 hours each for the fifth and sixth semesters. Vertically, these regulations do not exceed the historical stipulations of our country. Horizontally, they are slightly more than those of middle schools in France and Italy, and less than those in Soviet Russia. They are roughly the same as those in England and Germany. As for the total number of hours spent in class and self-study for junior high school students, it is stipulated as eight hours per day, totaling 48 hours per week. For senior high school students, the total number of hours spent in class, self-study, and extracurricular activities is stipulated as ten hours per day, totaling 60 hours per week. Although this regulation cannot be directly compared, it is not unreasonable. First, junior high school students are younger and need more rest for their physical and mental development. Therefore, the spirit of the "three eights system" for labor is adopted, setting the weekly workload at 48 hours. Apart from the 35-36 hours of teaching, they can have 12-13 hours of self-study. The distribution ratio is about one to three. Within the teaching time, some subjects require more self-study, while others do not require self-study or require less. By averaging out the differences, it is generally acceptable. Although extracurricular sports and activities are not included in the school's self-study time, their nature is light and relaxing, which is a good way to regulate the heavy workload. The amount of time can be determined and used by the school at its discretion. Second, the teaching hours for upper grades in middle schools in various countries are more than those for lower grades. The current system in our country has fewer teaching hours for senior high school than for junior high school, and fewer teaching hours for upper grades of senior high school than for lower grades. This does not violate the general trend, but is because the content of senior high school subjects is deeper, faster, and more complex, and students have stronger self-study abilities. Therefore, more self-study time should be allocated to each subject. Although the teaching hours are less, the total daily workload increases from eight to ten hours.

In fact, the weight of the study load cannot be simply explained by the number of teaching hours. There are too many factors related to the study load. First, there is the issue of teaching materials. The teaching of a certain subject for the same one hour can have simple content, not requiring much pre-class preparation or post-class review, or it can be very complex, requiring multiple times the amount of time for cloud learning. The teaching materials for each subject should be appropriately stipulated according to the total teaching hours of the subject and the estimated self-study time, considering the students' level, so as to avoid the drawbacks of uneven depth and being insufficient or unable to be taught completely. The teaching materials for each teaching hour should also be appropriately allocated, avoiding situations of improper emphasis or uneven load. This distribution of teaching materials is what the curriculum standards should achieve first. The current middle school curriculum standards for each subject inevitably vary in detail, with some being more specific and appropriate, and others being exceptionally empty and difficult to follow. They urgently need to be reviewed. Some say that if we were to stipulate in more detail, then that would be detailed teaching materials. Whether it is an outline or detailed specifications, the substance and quantity of teaching materials for each subject still need to be carefully studied and clearly stipulated or supplemented, so that there is a correct basis for the quantity of each time unit in learning. Second, there is the issue of textbooks. How to deduce a concrete teaching material from a teaching material outline and express it to students in a way that is easy for them to understand and learn is the skill of textbook compilation. How to review textbooks to select the best and eliminate the worst, so that poor textbooks disappear from schools, is the work of reviewing and approving textbooks. These two aspects are what the country and society should plan well for the youth's study load. Third, there is the issue of teaching aids. The equipment of laboratories, libraries, workshops, and all teaching instruments is undoubtedly closely related to the learning process. To improve teaching efficiency and reduce the study load, teaching equipment is absolutely indispensable. Fourth, there is the issue of education. Teaching materials, textbooks, and teaching aids are all static, while teachers are dynamic. Without teachers to use them, everything is external. With diligent teachers, everything comes alive, and good teachers can also make up for various deficiencies, exert the highest efficiency in teaching, and reduce the study load. Fifth, there is the general discipline situation of the school. A good school life can encourage interest in learning and promote effort in learning everywhere. The personality of each young person is well understood by the faculty and staff, and the entire life of each young person is noticed by the faculty and staff. Individual difficulties are corrected, and physical and mental fatigue is regulated. The learning process can progress smoothly, so how can there be any unbearable burden?

The teaching materials, textbooks, teaching aids, teachers, and general discipline situation mentioned above are all basic factors of the study load. To reduce the current study load of middle school students, a detailed study should be made of these five aspects, and then a solution can be obtained. Otherwise, simply focusing on the current middle school teaching hours, which are not unsuitable, and trying to reduce them, not to mention that any reduction will not reach any special stage, even if it is greatly reduced to a discounted level, while other basic factors related to learning remain the same, I believe, I am sure, the study load of middle school students will not be reduced in any way. We naturally cannot unconditionally support the current education system with an attitude of clinging to the old and defending the obsolete, and wish it longevity. But when we discuss a problem, we should grasp the core of the problem, and not engage in superficial arguments. If we only discuss the study load of middle school students from the perspective of teaching hours, we are really addressing the symptom and not the cause. If we further criticize the current middle school teaching hour system based on shallow observations and erroneous facts, then that is a fool's errand. (The End)

Little Man (73) 135

— Original by Ms. Alcott of the United States, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Little Tandy never forgot his old friend. Upon hearing that name, he struggled out of his father's arms and ran with nimble steps to the door, looking at the sun-drenched plaza spread with fine grass, with a look of longing on his face. He ran back, skipping and jumping, and stubbornly said as before (because he always said this after each expectation and disappointment):

"My Donald will come, old." (Note)

"I really think we should keep him here, if only for Tandy's sake. He likes him so much. Maybe the child's feelings can do what we haven't been able to do."

"I sometimes have that feeling too, but since the children have been making such a fuss and almost burned down the whole house, I think for safety's sake, we have to remove that spark, at least send him away for a while," Mr. Pei said.

"Lunch is ready, let me ring the bell," Robert said, and played a solo on that "instrument," so fiercely that he couldn't even hear himself talking.

"Ten Nans are also OK, as long as you want, my dear, and can accommodate all the naughty children in the world without anyone taking care of them.

"Ten Nans are also OK, as long as you want, my dear," Mr. Pei replied, in his great compassionate heart.

(Note) Will come, old - coming soon

Minutes of the Second Preparatory Meeting of the China Sports Society 144

The Preparatory Office is located in the Sports Hall of Nanjing Central University; Hao Gengsheng is elected as the Chairman of the Preparatory Committee.

The second preparatory meeting of the China Sports Society was held at the Shanghai Central Stadium at 1:00 PM on October 18. The record is as follows: Hao Gengsheng, Shen Siliang, Wu Yunrui, Cheng Dengke, Zhang Jiwu, and Shao Rugan attended. Hao Gengsheng chaired the meeting. Resolutions: (1) It was decided that the preparatory office will be located in the Sports Hall of Nanjing Central University. (2) Hao Gengsheng was elected as the Chairman of the Preparatory Committee. (3) Hao Gengsheng, Wu Yunrui, and Cheng Dengke were designated to design and carry out the central research work within the next year. (4) The inaugural meeting of the association is tentatively scheduled to be held at the same time as the sports discussion meeting to be held by the All-China Sports Association next year. (5) The association will apply to the Ministry of Education and the Academia Sinica for preparatory funding to facilitate its progress. The draft articles of association are as follows: Article 1: The name of this association is the China Sports Society. Article 2: The purpose of this association is a purely academic research institution, with the purpose of researching sports academics. Article 3: Association Affairs: Holding sports discussion meetings, sports academic lectures, editing annual reports and other publications related to sports academic groups, and creating sports circulation libraries, etc. Article 4: Members (1) Any organization willing to study and promote sports, after being reviewed and approved by the Council of the association and submitted to the Congress for approval, may become a group member of the association. Group members pay an annual fee of ten yuan and have the right to elect and be elected as directors and enjoy the right to all publications issued by the association. (2) Any individual willing to study and promote sports, after being introduced by two or more members and reviewed and approved by the Council of the association, may become a member of the association. Individual members pay one yuan per year, or those who pay twenty yuan at one time will be permanent members, have the right to elect and be elected as directors, and have the right to receive all publications of the association. Article 5: Board of Directors: The association may hire several directors to form a board of directors to guide the association's affairs and raise funds for the association. Article 6: Staff: 1. The Council of the association is composed of twelve individual members and three group members, who are responsible for all association affairs. One-third of the directors are re-elected by correspondence every year and can be re-elected. The detailed rules will be formulated separately. 2. The association has three standing directors and one chairman, who are elected by the directors to be responsible for all association affairs. (3) All staff members of the association, except for those specially hired, are honorary positions and are not paid. Article 7: Organization: The association has a general office, a general affairs department, a translation department, a research department, a publicity department, an introduction department, a communication department, and a savings department. Except for the general office, which is managed by the Council, the other departments are managed by the Organizing Committee of the Congress. The detailed rules will be formulated separately. Article 8: Meetings: The association's meetings are divided into the following three types: (1) The association holds a general meeting once a year, which is convened by the Council. (2) The Council meets once a month to discuss all matters related to the association's affairs, which is convened by the chairman of the board. (3) The association may convene temporary meetings by the Council when necessary. Article 9: Branches: Members of the association in various places who number more than 2,000 may organize branches. Their articles of association will be formulated separately. Article 10: Supplementary Provisions: Matters not covered in these articles of association may be proposed by more than eighteen members of the association and amended by a resolution of the Congress, and submitted to the competent education administrative agency for record.

Shen Bao Domestic Goods Weekly

Let's Turn Over the Basin and Take a Look 148

— Yang An

Mr. Zhang Boling, the principal of Nankai University, is a leading figure in the education and sports circles of the country. One day, at a banquet held in the International Hotel's domestic goods factory to welcome the female athletes of the National Games, he delivered a wonderful speech promoting domestic goods, which won continuous applause from the audience. Everyone said that this "high-ranking Mr. Zhang" truly has vision, insight, and is willing to work wholeheartedly to promote domestic goods. Mr. Zhang said, "If our goods are not as good as others, we can only feel ashamed and encourage ourselves to make our goods better than others. If our goods are more expensive than others, we can only feel ashamed and strive to make our goods cheaper than others." It is important to know that promoting patriotism through words is not universally applicable in China, where culture is not yet developed. Loving exquisite goods and being greedy for cheapness are human nature, and cannot be changed simply by promoting it verbally. How easy is it to prevent people from buying cheap goods and purchasing exquisite items? Even the clothes I wear now have been carefully considered. Because I couldn't find domestic woolen fabric for my Western-style trousers, I made them from silk fabric, which I think is quite good. It all depends on whether everyone is willing to have some spirit of sacrifice and determination. What is most painful is that the Western word for China comes from the production of porcelain, but now the side dishes in Western restaurants are not Chinese-made. Everyone, turn over the basin and take a look. Is this a Chinese product? Is the tablecloth on the dining table a Chinese product? Is the black tea and milk in the cup a Chinese product? Is the piece of paper a Chinese product? I'm not here to spoil the fun or to blame the hotel owner. This is our common shame. As a country that has produced porcelain for thousands of years, we don't even use our own dining basins. Whose fault is this? Whose responsibility is this? Everyone already knows that promoting domestic goods and building up physical fitness are both ways to revitalize the nation. Everyone has a responsibility. If everyone strives to use domestic goods and manufacture domestic goods from now on, perhaps we won't see a single foreign product at the next welcome party. Only then will I not have wasted my words today." Mr. Zhang was sincere and earnest, and everyone was moved. They believed that this was a thorough and heartfelt speech. I hope everyone will chew on it and reflect on it. Compared to empty slogans and commotion, it might be more effective.

The Alarm That "Rice" Accounts for the Top Spot in the Customs Import Surplus 149

— Zhang Mengzhao

Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four essential elements of people's livelihood! In ancient times, the saying "the people regard food as heaven" was well-known to everyone. Farmers, who account for more than 80% of the country's total population, are still unable to be self-sufficient in food and rely on others! This is truly a painful thing!

Amidst the enthusiastic calls for promoting domestic goods, we read the report from the International Trade Bureau to the Ministry of Industry regarding the international trade situation in the first half of the year. What is saddening is that "the total value of foreign goods imported in the first half of the year is estimated at 288,736,000 gold units. Due to the low gold price, although it has decreased compared to the same period last year when calculated in national currency, it has increased by 7% when calculated in gold units. Among them, the import with the greatest value is - rice - totaling 11,186,960 quintals, worth over 43,359,000 gold units." The conclusion is that "China's imported goods have always been cotton, hardware, rice, kerosene, and wheat, with very little change. In the first half of this year, except for kerosene, which decreased, rice, cotton, hardware, and wheat remained the four major pillars of imports. In China, where industry is not yet developed, the import of hardware is not surprising, but the import of agricultural products is so huge that it is the greatest crisis in our foreign trade."

When we see the above figures for "rice" imports and the conclusion, we are truly startled and frightened!

The confrontation between Britain and Italy is escalating, and the prospect of a second world war is imminent! Looking back at our national defense situation, what is it like? What is the state of the national economy? What about agricultural production? Then I dare to shout loudly, we are just waiting to die! Isn't that so? In terms of national defense, there are no strategic fortifications, no modern military equipment! As for the national economy, floods are everywhere, and hundreds of thousands of people are affected by disasters. In terms of agricultural production, fields are submerged! In areas where rice and paddy crops are abundant, there has been a sudden outbreak of white planthopper pests, and all efforts have been in vain! If there is no foreign rice to provide relief, starvation will inevitably ensue! However, if our ports are once blockaded due to a world war, the situation of fish in a pot will be complete, and what is left but to perish?

Therefore, the "rice" problem should be addressed quickly in agriculture by preparing for a rainy day. In areas with good harvests, we should quickly prevent pests. In submerged fields, we should urgently dredge and improve water conservancy to turn barren land into fertile land! Cultivating domestic rice and promoting domestic rice is an urgent and unavoidable matter in promoting domestic goods! I look forward to it! Wang Shouqiu

Bleaching Method of Straw Pulp (Part 1) 151

— Tianxu Wo Sheng

I was visited by Mr. Jin Runxiang and Mr. Zhu Mei of the Minfeng Paper Mill, who inquired about the cost of making newspaper from straw. I hereby record the outline as follows:

Mr. Zhu described the process: Initially, 13% solid caustic soda was used to digest straw, with each digester holding 80 dan (a unit of weight) and requiring 12 hours. Later, 10% lime was used for 4 hours, the straw was taken out and washed, then put back into the digester and 13% liquid caustic soda was used for 4 hours. After pulping and bleaching, the cost of materials per 100 catties of paper was calculated at 5.9 yuan, which is about 100 yuan per ton or 4.5 fen per pound. For ordinary newspaper, each ream of 37 pounds would cost about 1.7 yuan in materials. Adding the papermaking process, it is impossible to compete with imported products in terms of price. If not bleached, each ton of straw pulp would require 40 dan of straw. Boiling with lime to dissolve and bleaching the yellow water into pulp would only cost 24 yuan. Therefore, the difficulty lies in the bleaching aspect, etc. Therefore, I will briefly describe what I have experienced as follows:

Making pulp from straw is actually more than three to one. Considering buying straw in the city, it costs about 3 yuan per 1,000 catties. 10 pounds of sodium sulfide should be used, costing about 6 jiao. The initial pulp yield is about 400 catties, so 30 pounds of sodium sulfite should be used, costing about 3.9 yuan, and 8 pounds of hydrochloric acid, costing about 4 jiao 8 fen. Adding the above together, multiplying by five to make one ton, it costs only 39.9 yuan. The actual cost of coal and electricity is no more than 6.75 yuan, so the cost is at most 50 yuan. Each pound costs 2.5 fen, and ordinary newspaper costs less than 1 yuan per 37-pound ream. Adding the cost of the papermaking process, even with double shifts, it is at most 1 yuan. If each ream earns 2 jiao, it is also considerable. However, the procedure should be divided into three steps. Turning straw into pulp using sodium sulfide and lime does not add much cost. However, using lime takes a long time. If operating in the countryside, it is not a problem. If operating in a factory, time is valuable and space is costly, so speed is economical. The purpose of using sodium sulfide is to convert the starch into sugar liquid, making it easier to decompose and prevent it from becoming paste. Therefore, steaming for three hours is sufficient to remove the pulp. Although the amount of the mixture is as mentioned above, using pounds per catty, it accounts for 10/1000, but the amount of dilution has a significant impact on the finished product. If it is too strong, more straw will adhere to it and cause it to rot. Therefore, it is advisable to dissolve it with an appropriate amount of water first, so that the straw stalks are moistened.

As mentioned above, the yield of the first step is actually more than 40%. If only the yellow water is bleached from each 100 catties of straw, more than 60 catties can be obtained after drying. However, after pulping with a beater and performing the bleaching process, the yield is greatly reduced, and only 40 catties can be obtained. If the work is not done carefully, the amount of loss cannot be generalized. For example, if steaming is excessive, more of it will become paste, which will escape from the mesh during beating and washing. Therefore, using five times the amount as a ton is actually the minimum, as 4,000 catties of straw are needed to make one ton of pulp. If 2,000 catties of pulp are bleached into one ton, it contains only 80%, depending on the skill of the operator, which should not have major deviations. No work can be done solely based on words, as words are like medicine in a prescription, only showing a standard. For example, when cooking rice, the method is shown, with a certain amount of rice, a certain amount of water, and a certain cooking time, but the result often fails, either cooking into porridge or burnt rice, which is not consistent. Therefore, the bleaching process cannot be handled by rural farmers, and should be done by the factory.

There is more than one type of sodium sulfite. It is advisable to use "acidic sodium sulfite," also known as "sodium bisulfite," with the formula Na2HSO3. The commonly sold sodium sulfite is not acidic, with the formula NaSO3, and is not suitable for use. The effect of bleaching is the opposite of bleaching with "calcium hypochlorite." The effect of sodium sulfite is to remove oxygen from the material to decolorize it, while the effect of calcium hypochlorite is to release oxygen and acidify the material to decolorize it. Therefore, the finished products are equal, but the effects are different. Because the cost is low, those who use it to make newspapers only need to use sulfite bleaching and do not need to use hypochlorite bleaching. However, its drawback is that it easily absorbs oxygen from the air and turns yellow over time. Therefore, imported newspaper inevitably turns yellow over time. The shortcoming of sulfite wood pulp is this, while its advantage is that the cost is lower. If hypochlorite bleaching is used, the amount must be doubled, and the amount of hydrochloric acid must be doubled to sulfuric acid, and the time required is also doubled, so the cost is increased, which is not cost-effective for use in newspapers.

Worth Promoting: Rayon Made from Sorghum Straw 152

— Zhao

Those who suddenly see my title will surely say, "Why are you so ignorant? And mistake imported rayon for domestic goods? Why don't you think more before writing?" The reporter says that imported goods are what we learn from. Just like today's automobiles and steamships, transportation tools, aren't they all derived from the boats and carriages first invented by our Yellow Emperor? Now, there is rayon made from domestic sorghum straw! How can we not be happy? I deeply hope that Ms. Feng Yunhe, who is determined to succeed, will achieve her goal!

Qingdao Correspondence: Ms. Feng Yunhe is from Lijin, Shandong. She graduated from the National Peiping Women's Normal University. In 1926, she was sent to the United States by the Shandong Provincial Department of Education to study industrial chemistry at Ohio University. She graduated in 1933 and obtained a doctorate. She then went to Germany to study printing and dyeing. Because she was heartbroken by the huge amount and value of rayon imported into China, she was eager to find a way to reverse this profit. Therefore, she worked hard to research the use of abundant and low-value plants produced in China to manufacture rayon. This spring, she successfully tested rayon made from sorghum straw. Compared with imported products, the test properties were even better. Currently, Ms. Feng is studying silk-making machines at the Kahn Meinz factory and will soon return to China to raise funds to set up a factory in Qingdao or Jinan, etc.

Sorghum is different from glutinous rice. Sticky sorghum can be used to make wine. In the north, sorghum is commonly called "shushu," and there are red and white varieties. Cui Bao's "Notes on Ancient and Modern Times" states that sorghum is glutinous rice, etc. "Jie" sounds the same as "jie," meaning the stalks of grain after removing the skin. In the north, sorghum stalks are called "shushu jie," which is used in river engineering (from the Dictionary of Origins). In 1934, customs statistics showed that imports of rayon reached 19,050,000 taels, which is shocking! Rayon is mixed into domestic silk fabrics almost everywhere! Even in remote rural areas, it is ubiquitous! What is most painful is that even the female workers who work hard in domestic factories to manufacture domestic goods often unknowingly wear cheap and beautiful imported rayon! The same is true for women in towns and villages!

Now, the entire country is uneasy about the deflation after the silver rush and worries that China's monetary system will be linked to the gold pound, the US dollar, or the Japanese yen! I don't know that China's customs import surplus has been tens of thousands of yuan every year, and it has long been linked to the gold pound, the US dollar, or the Japanese yen, and it has already dug its own grave! The expansion of rayon to the point of being linked to the clothing of villagers is just one example! The reporter hopes that the entire country and financial giants will quickly work together to support Ms. Feng's domestic straw-made rayon factory to achieve its early success!

Writing to Overseas Students 153

— Quan Jia

Overseas students must read newspapers every day. You probably can't help but notice the large-print headlines in the news columns that frequently mention the amount of the import surplus! At times, I believe that when you try domestic goods, you often resent that Chinese products are so disappointing. Now, you have left your homeland for a long time to study abroad. In the current time of national economic depression, overseas students may be the only beacon of light! Therefore, I would like to offer a few words of contribution with the hope that overseas students will work hard to promote domestic goods!

(1) Be a model of using domestic goods. In the country, we see that almost all foreigners use their own national goods. I remember one gentleman saying that a Japanese family living in Hongkou used, ate, and wore everything sent from their homeland. One day, that gentleman went to that family's house and saw that they were only eating pickled radishes and the like. He asked him why he was so frugal today, since he used to eat meat and fish regularly. The Japanese person said, "My national goods haven't arrived yet!" Overseas students, due to practical difficulties, cannot do what that Japanese person does. However, daily necessities or clothing should be selected from domestic goods. You should know that wearing domestic clothes on the streets of a foreign country is very glorious. Chinese students mostly spend a lot of money to buy foreign goods and make them into expensive clothes, and foreigners often laugh at the fact that Chinese people don't have their own clothes. Overseas students should take an oath: "If I don't wear Chinese clothes, I would rather never eat a meal or drink a cup of tea!" When a comrade uses Chinese goods, overseas students should all shout in unison: "Me!"

(2) Strive to promote and introduce Chinese goods. The first reason why Chinese goods often cannot gain a foothold abroad is that there is no promotion. The second reason is the counter-promotion of the other party. I believe that overseas students have a wide range of friends abroad. Please try to promote and introduce the advantages of Chinese goods so that your friends develop a concept of trusting Chinese goods. Recently, there have been organizations such as overseas trade groups. If we add the efforts of overseas students to promote them, the results will be great.

(3) Invent and improve on your own. Overseas students are all intellectuals. Naturally, you have the ability to improve the areas of domestic goods that you are dissatisfied with. Please have an interest in inventing or improving domestic goods, which is also very important.

In short, overseas students are also a type of student. This year is the year of domestic goods for students. Overseas students should take the lead and assume the mission of the year of domestic goods for students. Don't be blinded by the prosperity of overseas countries and forget the weak and powerless Chinese national industry. Overseas students in today's extraordinary era can no longer be casual. Please give us good news from the domestic goods industry before you return to China. That is my hope!

Domestic Goods Doctor 154

— Ji'an

Who in City S doesn't know that Mr. Huang is a domestic goods doctor who is determined to use domestic goods?

Indeed, Mr. Huang is truly an authentic domestic goods doctor. Mr. Huang is truly a believer in using domestic goods. He would rather abandon anything he uses, eats, wears, or any other necessities if they are not domestic goods. Even if he accidentally misused foreign goods due to a moment of carelessness, he would always remember it, express twelve points of regret, and deeply resent the clerk who deceived him.

Mr. Huang is not only very serious about his personal use of domestic goods, but he is also exceptionally enthusiastic about the movement to promote domestic goods. Therefore, no matter what domestic goods promotion association, ×× domestic goods association, he seems to be the licorice in the medicine, and he participates in all of them. Whenever there is a meeting, he must also take the stage to give a speech, talking at length about his way of promoting domestic goods. As a result, Mr. Huang was elected as a member and ×× chairman of the ×× domestic goods association. At first, he always expressed that he was unable to bear the burden of the general public's recommendations, but in the end, for the sake of the domestic goods movement, he had no choice but to accept the position after repeatedly declining.

He strongly opposes people wearing suits, leather shoes, eating Western food, and riding in cars. Those who don't know him scold him behind his back, saying that he is unpatriotic and a would-be slave. Those who do know him, Mr. Huang teaches them honestly and unceremoniously to their faces, saying things like "Propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame are the four pillars of a country! What kind of system is it to combine Chinese and Western styles?" He rambles on and on, making the other person feel very uncomfortable, often blushing and retreating meekly.

Therefore, everyone calls Mr. Huang a domestic goods doctor. Mr. Huang is also happily complacent. Although the title of "domestic goods" has not been heard of among the titles of doctors, our Mr. Huang is now unanimously recognized as a domestic goods doctor.

Letter to the Editor 155

Dear Editor,

Mr. Xu Qingwen, the secretary and general affairs officer of the Shanghai National Products Factories United Association, passed away due to illness at Renji Hospital on the eighth of this month. The association recognizes that he served the national products industry diligently and exceptionally for ten years during his lifetime. His surviving children are all young and require financial assistance for their upbringing. Therefore, the Executive Committee has resolved to hold a memorial meeting at the Chenxiang Pavilion near the Old North Gate on the 27th of this month. Beforehand, the association will notify all member factories, requesting that condolences be offered in cash to provide some practical benefit to the orphaned children. Although notices have already been sent, there may be omissions. I respectfully request that you, sir, have pity on their plight and publish this draft so that comrades who have not received the obituary may see this and offer donations. This is a matter of charity, and I trust you will agree. With respectful greetings,

Sun Choucheng

Finance A Chorus of Buying, Gold Price Nearing 1,000 Yuan, Major Players Chasing Purchases, Shorts Desperate, Peak Reached 997.9 Yuan, Result: Soared by 22.7 Yuan 156

Yesterday's gold market saw a historic surge. Those who sold long positions the previous day rushed to buy back in. Speculation about domestic finance was rife, and sentiment was inherently bullish. Sellers disappeared from the market, and the atmosphere was one of universal buying, with a strong sense that the price would break through the 1,000 yuan barrier. The price soared to a high of 997.9 yuan before supply became available, the Hong Kong market eased, and the local exchange market turned flat due to bank sales, leading to a pullback. However, the final trend remained bullish. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets saw declines in London and stability in the U.S. The forward silver price in Menterie fell by 7 hao to 2 li. Exchange rates rose slightly, and London gold rose by 2 pence. The pre-market trading opened higher at 73 yuan, but there was a lack of long supply, and shorts were frightened. Buying momentum quickly built, with major players such as Shen Feng chasing purchases. Suppliers in the market were at a loss, and the price rose step by step to 86 or 87 yuan before Hengyu and others took advantage of the high price to supply, bringing it down to 81 or 82 yuan. Fuxing, Yongda, and Decheng continued to buy, and the price rose again to 85 or 86 yuan. After the high opening in the morning, the Central Bank announced its exchange rates, with both the British and U.S. rates declining. The customs gold unit surged by 3 cents, and the standard gold price was quoted at 960.8 yuan, remaining firm. Subsequently, Chinese merchants, such as those from Guangdong, all bought U.S. dollars. Banks' willingness to sell was weak, and the trading was extremely tight. Rumors circulated that customs gold bonds would be issued at a rate of 2.5 national currency yuan per customs gold unit, further boosting sentiment (the actual rate was 1.899 national currency yuan per customs gold unit). The market was entirely dominated by buyers, and sellers largely disappeared, leading to repeated price increases, breaking through the 90 yuan barrier and reaching 997.9 yuan. HSBC's exchange rates also declined by 0.25 and 0.5 yuan. Later, as banks took advantage of the high price to supply and the Hong Kong market gradually hardened, sellers began to appear. The circumstances of the current long-term consolidation, and the various trends in the market, have been reported in this newspaper before. Regarding all Ningbo loans, the responsible loan officer in Ningbo said that in the current Shanghai market situation, how easy is it to recover loans? And even if there are reliable people who want to open new accounts, they dare not try easily. The main idea from Ningbo is to recover the loans that can be recovered, and roll over the loans that cannot be recovered. However, Ningbo will not be able to remit current funds to Shanghai again in the future. In short, it will only receive funds and not lend them. According to the reporter's investigation yesterday, 80% to 90% of the Ningbo bank's loan officers have arrived. Only a small number of one or two banks have not arrived, and their loan amount is also very small. As of yesterday, the total amount of Ningbo bank's loans consolidated had already exceeded half, estimated to be over 13 million yuan. The amount of Shanghai bank's renewals is approximately 30 million yuan.

Gauze Rises by One Yuan Two Jiao Three Fen; Forward Contracts Fetch Five Yuan Foreign Currency

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 170

— (Huanglian)

"Any soft object, when subjected to pressure from another object, will contract in volume. However, this contraction is temporary, not permanent, because even though it is suppressed by another object, it has not lost its elasticity - resistance.

Therefore, the stronger the external pressure on a soft object, the greater the resistance. If the pressure is small, the resistance will also be weak!"

Furthermore, for example, a rubber ball bounces higher the harder it is thrown, and vice versa.

The above physics is extremely common and known to all. Therefore, we are not worried about the increasing severity of the national crisis - which can be said to be an increase in pressure - because worry is useless. We are only saddened by those who do not know shame and only seek pleasure, those whose minds have become wooden, because "this group" is probably already missing their elasticity - resistance. This is the greatest crisis for China's future!

Betrothal 171

— Jia Chen Sheng

In the North, children are called "wawa" (娃娃). The "wawa betrothal" (娃娃親事) written about in this article is a peculiar custom in the North, and can also be said to be a special page in the complex history of Chinese marriage.

The reality of "wawa" is like this: the North was later in developing, and the obstinacy of the common people is very profound. The concept of valuing men over women is even more severe. Parents regard male children as extremely precious, while they view female children as worse than dirt. Therefore, in relatively wealthy families, if they have a son late in life, not only is it rarer than anything else, but the first important issue is that when the child is only one or two years old, they quickly spend some money to find a wife for the child who is already of marriageable age to come home. This is considered fulfilling the great responsibility of being a parent.

When the girl arrives at the boy's house, she first greets the in-laws with the etiquette of a child, and regards her husband as a younger brother. So, the obligations that this daughter-in-law must fulfill are like those of a nanny hired by others. She is fully responsible for the diet and daily life of this young husband, dressing and feeding him during the day, and sleeping with him in her arms at night. Moreover, all sewing, cooking, washing, sweeping, and other household chores are the responsibility of this daughter-in-law.

When this young husband grows from a child to a teenager and becomes an adult, a propitious day is chosen to formally hold the wedding ceremony. However, this pair of ideal people consists of a young man of only twenty years and an aging woman. Fundamentally, the wife is one or two decades older than the husband. Such old yin and young yang couples are not surprising in the North.

However, being able to raise her husband to adulthood and actually live together in harmony, this woman, despite having worked hard for more than a decade and wasted her youth, is still considered greatly fortunate. If the young husband dies young, the woman must remain chaste and a widow for the rest of her life. She will also be cursed as a jinx, a husband-killer, and a family destroyer until she dies. This is truly a tragic event in the world, devoid of humanity. This strange custom of "wawa betrothal" is still prevalent in Qingyuan, Guangping, and other counties in Hebei Province.

Night Boat 172

— Wei Jing

This time, following a friend, I took a night boat and experienced life in the last century again.

Under the moonlight, in a waterway squeezed between sloping hills, it was progressing by the pulling force of four strong men. The sound of water "嘩拉嘩拉" came rhythmically from under the boat. The shore was so quiet that only the barking of dogs and the very eerie hooting of owls came from afar. Otherwise, there were no sounds. The grass on the shore swallowed the feet of those pulling the boat. Sparse tree shadows resembled ghosts, pouncing on the gunwale of the boat. The boat was crowded with people. In the small cabin, there were about forty passengers, men and women, old and young, rustic and beautiful. My friend and I took the small room, which consisted of only two rooms in the entire boat. Although there was only a bunk barely big enough for two people, it was much more comfortable than the three or forty people in the general cabin. Not only could we sit, but we could also stretch our legs and lie down, and we even had a private Mobil lamp.

My friend started snoring as soon as the boat moved. I couldn't fall asleep. At one o'clock in the middle of the night, amidst the mixed snoring in the general cabin, I suddenly heard a sharp scream from a woman. I was startled and poked my head out to take a look. In the dim light of a Mobil lamp, I saw that the passengers who had woken up were all grinning at a woman in her thirties. The woman's face was flushed, and she seemed to want to cry but didn't open her mouth.

At this time, my friend also woke up and said with a smile, "Too common. When I take a night boat, I always see this kind of thing related to moral issues nine out of ten times. Once, um..." He offered me a cigarette, lit it, and we smoked in silence, cutting off the topic.

The sounds in the cabin subsided. The sound of the water under the boat was again "嘩拉嘩拉". The four people pulling the boat, probably to relieve their fatigue, began to hum vulgar mountain songs one after another.

Glimpses of the Imperial Incense 173

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

"I wonder if the Old Buddha is happy today?" He first probed Li Lianying.

"Why do you ask that? Let me tell you: the Old Buddha is in the worst mood today!" Li Lianying said arrogantly. "If you have anything to report, no one can guarantee whether she will get angry or not."

"You are right. I don't know whether I will be beaten or scolded after I report this matter. But I dare not not report it," the gardener said with a crying face. "If I don't report it today, and the Old Buddha finds out tomorrow, will I be able to keep my head!"

"Hmph! You have a point! But after you go up and report it, she might get angry, and you still won't be able to avoid having your head chopped off!" Li Lianying laughed coldly as if very pleased. This person was originally a heartless and inhumane creature. Relying on the Empress Dowager's favor, he did not regard these little eunuchs as human beings. Every time a eunuch or palace maid angered the Empress Dowager and was ordered to be dragged out for torture, Li Lianying always showed a look of secret joy in his heart. If the Empress Dowager wanted to have someone arrested and beheaded, he was even more delighted. "Now, tell me what is the matter that you plan to report?"

At this time, the gardener was already scared pale. Hearing Li Lianying's tone, he wanted to stop talking, but he also knew that he had already said too much and could not take it back. Even if he really stopped talking, Li Lianying would definitely use torture to force him to tell the truth. (443)

Little Western Paradise 174

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Episode 20: Struggling for Life to See His Beloved Grandson, Hugging and Crying in a Famine Year, Recalling the Past, Planting Wheat Leads to Disaster

Yueying said that in the past two years, the store still had a little business. But during that year of famine, those passing by were all refugees, and foreign merchants doing business could not be seen for months. If you weren't a local, you wouldn't go into a shop run by someone from Hunan. So my dad closed the shop and stopped doing business, focusing solely on farming. Mrs. Zhou said: Wasn't there a drought? How could farming produce any grain? Yueying said: That's right, in the first year, we didn't harvest any grain at all. We still had some stored grain. The people in the area, because there was no harvest that year, didn't eat things like they used to. They didn't eat pot cakes and steamed buns even once every ten days. They always used flour mixed with water to make a paste to drink. After a while, drinking the thin paste left people feeling weak and powerless, so they could only make pot cakes once or twice, but they had to add wheat bran to the flour. Later, by early spring, even with the addition of wheat bran, it still felt like they were eating too much wheat flour, so they dug up some grass roots from the mountain ridges, chopped them into small pieces, and mixed them with the flour to make food. The amount of flour decreased more and more, and the amount of grass roots increased more and more. Later, what they ate wasn't pot cakes, but grass root dumplings. By the third or fourth month, it still hadn't rained a single drop from the sky. Everyone looked up at the sky all day long, feeling not only sad but also very scared. If there was no more grain on the ground, wouldn't the people in the area all starve to death? So my dad said that if it continued to be dry like this, even grass roots might not be available to eat. There was only one way: to quickly return to our old home in Hunan. But our old home in Hunan was several thousand li away from Gansu. Even if we just ate along the way, it would cost no less than twenty or thirty yuan to get there. So there was only one stupid way: to bring our own dry food and eat it while walking. (247)

Biographical Sketches of Notable Figures

The Heroic Woman of France (Part 1) 175

— Hai

Our country's famous actor, Mei Lanfang, with his God-given handsome features, plays female roles so vividly and realistically. When he performs on stage, every gesture, every movement, every word he utters is feminine, making it almost impossible to tell that he is a man. In recent years, his footsteps have reached Japan, America, and various other countries, and everyone who sees him is delighted and full of praise, hence the title "Heroic Woman." However, offstage, he resumes his male attire and lives his life as a man. It is unheard of that in the era of Louis XV in France, there was a knight who did not perform on stage but dressed as a woman and lived a woman's life for as long as forty years? This is truly a rare and wondrous event that must be recorded.

This heroic woman was the Chevalier d'Eon, who held the position of commander in the heavy cavalry regiment of France. He had a slim and petite physique, was delicate and lively, and possessed a thick head of hair as fine as a beautiful woman's silken tresses. Even more peculiar was that his eyes contained a great deal of tears, ready to flow at any moment. In the court of Louis XV, he was famous for his handsome looks, and thus, entrusted with a diplomatic mission, he was sent to Russia. At that time, the Empress of Russia had always been unwilling to receive French men, and d'Eon was unable to gain an audience, which greatly distressed him. Suddenly, he remembered that he had once dressed as a woman at a costume ball, and he decided to wear women's clothing to seek an audience with the Russian Empress.

He went with a graceful and charming demeanor. Due to his inherent beauty and realistic makeup, there were absolutely no flaws. The Empress's maids all thought he was a French lady-in-waiting and invited him to their dressing rooms to share their private thoughts and secrets, telling him their love stories, unaware that he was actually a bearded man.

Later, he was sent on a secret mission to England. A wealthy family in London held a special welcome party, attended by ambassadors from various countries and lords and nobles, making it a grand occasion. Among the many male and female guests, there was a Countess Daschkova from Russia who recognized d'Eon at first glance. It turned out that she had often interacted with him in St. Petersburg. Now, seeing him suddenly dressed as a man, she was very surprised. Thus, the story of his dressing as a woman in Russia spread.

At that time, the social circles of London were swept up in a gambling frenzy. Everyone put up a lot of money to bet on whether d'Eon was actually a man or a woman, and they gave d'Eon 15,000 gold pounds, demanding that he give the final verdict. He was very angry, and suddenly tears streamed down his face. Blushing, he lowered his eyelashes shyly and said that he was indeed a woman, but he had been dressed as a man since childhood because his parents had no sons, and this was a way to console their feelings. Immediately, people spread this news, and everyone believed it to be true, while d'Eon secretly chuckled in the dark. Tired of London, he wanted to return to his homeland of France.

At this time, the grandson of Louis XV was in power; this young Louis was very humorous. He said that when d'Eon returned to France, if he resumed the attire of a cavalry commander, then he and the Goussy family would have old grievances and would inevitably have to duel and shed blood; therefore, he had to return dressed as a woman—otherwise, his pension would be revoked.

Although this was the young king joking with him, the means were very ruthless. D'Eon had debts in England, which he relied on his pension to cover. Hearing the threat of revocation, how could he not be anxious? Thus, he had no choice but to obey the young king's order. The young king, out of sympathy for his plight, allowed him to wear the Cross of Saint Louis, which he had previously received for his bravery, and kept for him the full set of uniform and military handguns, sabers, bayonets, etc., from his cavalry regiment, as souvenirs.

Upon returning to Paris, he followed the young king's orders and went to a clothing store he had designated, where he had many women's silk dresses and skirts made, and began to dress as a woman. He hesitated for a moment, feeling unbearable in his heart, and cursed, throwing aside the colorful women's clothes and putting on his old regiment uniform again, fleeing to his childhood hometown of Tonnerre, hiding in the vineyards, not daring to show his face. However, after enduring a month, plagued by financial difficulties, he had to return to Paris and, under the name of Mademoiselle de l'Eon, appeared in society.

Brief News: The Great Shanghai People's Society, a publishing organization jointly initiated by reporters from major Shanghai newspapers, has published the bi-monthly news publication "The Great Shanghai People." The inaugural issue was published on October 10th, with an initial print run of 5,000 copies, which have already sold out. Due to insufficient office space at its original location, the Society has recently moved to the Independent Publishing House at No. 5 Chongrang Lane, Sima Road. The format and content of the second issue will be even more beautiful and rich than the first, it is said.

Treating Lung Disease and Economics 176

— Physician Shen Zhaoquan

The mental anguish of treating lung disease is greater than the physical pain. The threat to one's finances is especially severe. Therefore, the economic aspect must be fully considered before undergoing treatment. There have been many tragic outcomes due to running out of funds midway through treatment.

The key to economical treatment is not saving on various living expenses during treatment, but rather saving on the overall cost of treatment. In other words, it is to achieve complete recovery as soon as possible. To achieve this goal, one must consult a formal specialist physician, thoroughly implement various therapies, strictly adhere to the doctor's instructions, and persevere in recuperation. In this way, the treatment period can be shortened, resulting in an economical outcome. If the initial treatment is incomplete, prolonging the recovery period, the result will still be uneconomical.

Some say that lung disease is a rich man's disease because treating it requires a great deal of money. This is a misconception. In fact, ordinary living expenses can achieve perfect results in treatment. Therefore, whether or not lung disease treatment can be completed does not depend on the amount of treatment expenses, but rather on whether the patient chooses the right doctor and whether he or she can put in the effort.

Treating lung disease does not necessarily require relocating or staying in a sanatorium. If one can reform one's life at home, with the help of a specialist physician, and carefully implement fundamental treatment methods, perfect results can also be achieved.

Treating lung disease is a kind of protracted war. Do not be misled by the effectiveness of relocating, wasting money, and adding to the financial burden. Therefore, for patients with limited financial resources, it is more advisable to use the money for relocation or hospitalization for long-term home treatment.

For home treatment of lung disease, find a formal specialist physician nearby and attend regular outpatient visits to seek appropriate treatment and strictly adhere to the doctor's instructions. If one can resolve to comply, the effect will be no less than that of hospitalization.

The "Long-Term Treatment Package Fee Method for Lung Disease" established by the Shanghai Municipal Sanatorium is designed for economically disadvantaged families. For mild cases, a package fee of only a few dozen yuan is required to cover medical care until recovery (including medicine, injections, consultation fees, etc.). The aim is to prevent patients from being troubled by economic difficulties, to be able to undergo treatment without worry, and to safely achieve full recovery. This method is truly a good solution to the economic problem of treating lung disease and is a boon for ordinary families.
