Common Sense for Choosing Tonics 181

— Gao Baorui

Since ancient times in our country, the concept of tonics has been deeply ingrained in people's minds. Therefore, the need for tonics is particularly high. Just look at the patients who seek medical attention, they always ask whether there are any tonics to take, which is enough to give you an idea.

When patients ask if there are any tonics, if we doctors do not have a reasonable response, they will inevitably become suspicious and say that we do not know about tonics. Therefore, such a response may be related to credibility. However, if we want to respond, there is actually nothing to recommend. Although there are countless kinds of tonics sold on the market, both injectable and oral, after trying them, there are very few drugs that are effective. So when patients ask about tonics, the result is still better to just recommend cod liver oil.

Cod liver oil is indeed good for the human body. However, if we only recommend cod liver oil, patients will think that doctors only know about cod liver oil. They are often not satisfied, and there are other good tonics besides cod liver oil.

The word "tonic" means that it can replenish what the body lacks. In other words, it can provide what the body needs. If we examine the ingredients that the human body needs, protein is the most important, followed by carbohydrates and fats. As for other inorganic salts and vitamins, the need is very small. The daily intake of food is enough to absorb and use them, so there is no need to supplement them unless it is a special occasion.

The needs of the human body are as such, but the so-called tonics sold in the market are the opposite. They mostly contain only a small amount of phosphorus, arsenic, iron, calcium, iodine, and the like, which actually do nothing. Therefore, repeated experiments have repeatedly failed, until doctors are at a loss and patients are desperate, believing that there are no tonics in the world.

In our lives, the components of our bodies are constantly being consumed. Therefore, if we do not think about continuing to live, then that is it. But if we want to continue to live, we must constantly replenish what is being consumed. However, healthy people can replenish what is being consumed from the food they eat every day and do not need to seek additional supplements. But people who are sick and weak, such as those with "consumptive diseases like tuberculosis" and "neurasthenia," cannot exert their inherent functions. Therefore, even if they eat a lot of nutritious food, such as fish, meat, chicken eggs, milk, vegetables, and fruits, what if they cannot digest it?

Moreover, among the various nutrients, such as carbohydrates, fats, inorganic salts, and vitamins, the digestion is relatively simple. Therefore, they can still get a considerable supplement from ordinary food. But protein can only be absorbed after the most laborious and complex digestion, resulting in the final product, "amino acids." Otherwise, there is no way to absorb it. Then, is it not difficult for people with weak stomachs and intestines to seek protein supplements from their daily food?

Now, let's look at the blood-tonifying, strengthening, and nourishing "Vonbour's San-Vita-Cell," which is the final digested product of protein, namely, the "amino acid" preparation. In other words, it is the essence of protein that has been artificially digested. After taking it, it can form muscles and produce blood. Even patients with poor stomachs and intestines who are unable to digest and absorb food can maintain nutrition through this. Therefore, from all aspects, I think that "Conbour's San-Vita-Cell" is a very ideal nourishing and strengthening agent.

The point of view of "Conbour's San-Vita-Cell" in manufacturing is as such. Recently, I have also conducted clinical experiments, and it is in line with the facts. Everyone I have recommended it to has said that it is effective. Alas! At this time when doctors and patients are both having difficulty finding tonics, such a good medicine has been discovered. That is why I cannot remain silent and speechless.

Free Talk

The Era Following "Ah Q" 182

— Yu Congyu

We lack the spirit to bear heavy burdens and travel far, and we lack the drive to work hard with our heads bowed. In the past, those who looked favorably upon the Chinese people called them a sleeping lion. China seemed quite pleased to consider itself a sleeping lion. But what is a sleeping lion like? A sleeping lion is, after all, not a dead lion. It is merely sleeping there. The lion's strength and vigor have not disappeared, and the small animals scurrying around it are only daring to make trouble secretly, not daring to eat its flesh. Moreover, they ultimately fear it will awaken.

However, regarding China as a sleeping lion was before the Eight-Nation Alliance. Later, the Western illusion was shattered, and a dead lion was mistaken for a sleeping lion.

But we do not admit that we are dead. We say we are merely taking a nap. "Be careful, friends, when we wake up, we will repay kindness with kindness and revenge with revenge!" Thus, China stirred. Publications such as "Awakened Lion" and "Lion's Roar" came into being, but these were merely the names of publications.

This was the May Fourth Era. At that time, everyone seemed to think you were not dead, but after scratching yourself, you fell asleep again. During the Northern Expedition Era, you seemed to wake up again, and everyone seemed to think you were not dead, but after smacking your lips, you fell asleep again.

So people concluded that even if you were not a dead lion, perhaps you were a living donkey. I remember Liu Zihou's story of the donkey in Guizhou. It seems to have accurately described the present situation hundreds of years later. The tiger sees that the donkey can only use its tail to drive away mosquitoes and flies, so it really comes to bite us to test it.

Thus, everyone realized that pretending to be a sleeping lion was useless. We were not lions to begin with, and it would be too ridiculous to wake up and become a lion, to roar with a lion's voice. So everyone shouted again: We must be camels, camels!

What is a camel? A camel is not impatient, not agitated, not afraid of hardship, holding its head high, keeping its heart low, looking at the bottomless desert, carrying an astonishing weight, not wanting to slack off, not caring about the scenery, not greedy for flowers and fruits, and not stopping until it reaches its destination. This is naturally correct. China's present state is just the starting point, the future is a bottomless desert, and the responsibility is an astonishing load. One must have the spirit of a camel. If one only wants to roar and become a lion to repel enemies from afar, or to raise a finger and become a flying knife to kill enemies from thousands of miles away, that would be just a strange dream, even when it turns into the feces in other people's intestines.

But how can we become camels? To see if China can become a camel, we must ask what China is actually like now. But this question has always been ignored. People mistakenly thought we were a sleeping lion, so we forgot that we were mice, and wanted to wake up and become a lion, and wanted to roar like a lion for people to hear. This has already led to running into walls and making a fool of ourselves everywhere. But if we see real camels reaching their destination, and we ignore the fact that we are mice, then isn't it also a dream to disguise ourselves as camels and try to carry the weight of a camel and walk the journey of a camel? — Therefore, we need a mirror. If we don't have a mirror, we should look at our reflection in the pond to see what we really are.

Ah Q represents the Chinese people, but after being beaten, Ah Q would also say, "The grandson is beating the grandfather." Now it seems that the era of Ah Q is over, because we haven't seen this kind of donkey-like ability for a long time. I seem to only see my family's "Ami."

"Ami" is our family cat. When she is pushed off the sofa, she happily plays with the yarn ball on the floor. If she is not allowed to play with the yarn ball, then she plays with her own tail—equally happy, joyful, and carefree!

Natural Description (Part Two) 183

— Qu Yi

The nature depicted in these poems is all proper. This is because Du Fu focuses on human affairs with his whole personality, and pays less attention to nature. Nature is merely used as a rhetorical device and brought into the works. Therefore, that kind of pantheistic color is avoided.

However, some authors do not attempt to deify nature in their descriptions of nature. They merely want to describe nature more vividly, and unintentionally reveal shadows of pantheism by deifying it. In order to make nature sentimental, it is necessary to use personification in writing about nature, giving nature a certain personality. Moreover, as a result of excessive exaggeration, its personality will inevitably become infinitely great. Here, nature is united with God. Li Pei Tai Fu, in criticizing Xiao Lokhov's "Virgin Soil Upturned," said:

"The reason why Xiao Lokhov stands out among many writers in our country is that he has the skill to beautifully describe nature with rich talent. The uniquely beautiful scenery on the Don River prairie, the ensemble of all the complex voices of the people who live there, the extremely delicate and flavorful shadows, and the rich changes in the colors of the southern sky—all of these are expressed in Xiao Lokhov's works. The author wields great skill, allowing readers to feel the groans of laborers in the prairie under the intense summer sun, and to feel as if they are in the silence of a winter night… In 'Virgin Soil Upturned,' natural descriptions also form beautiful poetic passages. All these descriptions, more precisely, the author's view of nature transplanted into this work, is permeated with a great, burning love for endless life. In Xiao Lokhov's case, nature is not an opposing, unrelated power. Nature is ever-changing, overcoming all obstacles in life. The life of nature is consistent with the life of humanity. Human activities and reality have their echoes and basis in nature's rolling, endless creative power. Nature is not beautified by abstract rationalism, but by the beauty of profound feeling… Humanity and nature unite, creating a primordial state filled with endless life. … In 'Quiet Flows the Don,' this unity and combination of nature and humanity is everywhere tinged with a unique shadow of pantheism. The relationship between nature and humanity transcends ordinary, natural concepts, carrying something of an object's existence. No matter when, it always expresses an attitude close to 'nature worship.' This is especially felt when explaining the relationship between humans and the land. The land seems to have a certain attraction for Xiao Lokhov. Humans and nature are connected like ropes. If the earth calls, humans respond to its call and leave. He can abandon all work and temporarily forget the aggression, first making the land fertile… In 'Virgin Soil Upturned,' there is no such pantheistic tone. The land is still seen as just a piece of land. The relationship between humans and the land is simple, with self-evident qualities. This is very good. The land, like all of nature, does not lose its charm because of this. The persuasive power of art, the poetic style of narration, only under its shelter, there is a bit of a tendency to fall into a humanistic, biological view of nature…"

This shows that even authors who hold a new worldview inevitably carry a shadow of pantheism because of their love for the benefits that nature gives to humanity when they describe nature. Although it does not hinder the greatness of the work, it is also a tendency that should be corrected. Gorky went even further, calling on poets to shout to humanity: Contend with nature! Dominate nature! He says in his article on the subject of poetry:

"Past poets, as farmers and landlords, as children of nature, and essentially as slaves of nature, were ecstatic about the beauty and gifts of nature. In the poetic attitude towards nature, the most common and obvious thing that can be heard is the voice of meekness and flattery. Even now it can still be heard. In fact, praise for nature is praise for a tyrant. In that tone, it almost always reminds people of prayer. Poets, like mutually agreed upon keeping silent, never spoke of the ugly atrocities of nature—such as earthquakes, floods, hurricanes, droughts, and all kinds of outbreaks and madness of blind natural forces that destroy thousands of people and destroy their manual labor. Poets who once wanted to 'burn people's feelings with words' (which did not succeed much) or wanted to awaken 'good feelings' in people (which ultimately did not succeed) never shouted to humanity: Contend with nature! Dominate nature! Sometimes they were indignant at two-legged despots, but they were never indignant at blind tyrants… "

Here, Gorky's meaning is very clear. Poets should never merely pay tribute to nature with praise and love. Poets must awaken people, letting them know that they have the power to overcome nature. Here, poets should first poeticize human labor, which is the fundamental pillar of culture. Poets should first give poetic realm to the group's organized efforts to change the original forces of nature through contention. In other words, poets should first give poetic encouragement to the methods by which humans, based on their will, change and imagine the energy to create "second nature." Therefore, writers must first establish such a correct view of nature so that they will not fall into the quagmire of pantheism when describing nature.

Memory 184

— Hei Ding

Batur and Gu Dongye

Dragging my tired steps, I, a ghost-like figure, finally arrived from a small Gurkha village at the foot of Mount Szak to a Nau Ho village of the Bula people near the river. On the way, I was blown by a gust of wind and snow, which caused my head to feel dizzy and heavy. My whole body was hot, like a burning fire.

Ah, I am sick.

I stayed at old man Ge Jiulie's house. At night, my thoughts were chaotic and troubled. The illness put me in a terrible situation, and I felt lost in loneliness and isolation.

The black night always enveloped these few households of the cold Nau Ho people. From the distant valleys and forests, there came a few sparse, faint barks of dogs. The clear February moonlight shone all over this quiet village. The horse was restless and trampling its hooves in the trough shed. The shadows of the trees in the courtyard were dense, and a cold wind was howling.

I did not get a peaceful sleep. It seemed as if my soul was struggling in this long black night, unable to find a home, wandering and desolate.

Ah, this vast Batu He Shuo wilderness, where can I find a decent pharmacy? Where can I find a doctor who is not very skilled in surgery? This is a microcosm of primitive society. All the enjoyments of civilized society have not yet been introduced into this ancient and remote country.

Just as I had just woken up from a nightmare, the dim room was completely filled with the faint light of a lamp. The old woman Kani Oluxi had gotten up at some point. She was sitting, hunched over, and trembling as she stroked my suffocating throat. A streak of spittle flowed from her mouth, and she murmured with a worried expression:

—Sir, wake up, wake up! We have not offended the gods!

Her voice was old and hoarse.

As she spoke, she used a withered, bony hand to push her old man, Ge Jiulie, who was sleeping next to her like a dead pig.

Old man Ge Jiulie woke up sluggishly.

Kani Oluxi then told Ge Jiulie in detail about what she had just heard about me waking up from a nightmare. Finally, she tore open her lips and said tremblingly:

—Hurry up and kneel down to the gods, and bless this gentleman with peace, just like us, so that he will have a strong body and never get sick.

Ge Jiulie followed his wife Kani Oluxi's instructions and hurriedly walked to a square earthen platform, knelt in front of the altar, and silently offered a sincere prayer there.

At this time, Ge Jiulie's son, Telingfu, and his beautiful daughter-in-law, Sha Manlijin, suddenly woke up from their sweet dreams.

They stared at me in surprise.

Kani Oluxi, on one side, was searching through the messy hair of her sixteen-year-old, crooked-nosed daughter, Daina Sai, whom she had just woken up, and on the other side, she was moving her gray and dry lips as she spoke to me. Because her mouth was devoid of teeth because of her old age, her speech was very unclear. When she saw Telinglin and Sha Manlijin wake up, she told them in detail about me waking up from a nightmare.

Sha Manlijin smiled lightly, her face like a floating red cloud. She widened her eyes at Kani Oluxi and cracked her lips:

—Are you so frightened?

Kani Oluxi smiled and said:

—Fortunately, the gentleman woke up quickly. Afterwards, I asked your father to pray for him in front of the gods again.

—The weather is cold on the road. Did you catch a cold? Do you have a fever?

Telingfu said in a melancholy and questioning tone.

—Um, um…

Smiling, I nodded.

Old man Ge Jiulie walked back from the altar, looking happy, and reached out to pick up a pipe from the ground, then grabbed a handful of tobacco from the tobacco pouch, loaded it into the pipe bowl, and smoked it facing the light. He looked at me for a while, then hesitated as if he was saying to me:

—The gods will definitely bless you, the gods will definitely bless you.

That strong, tall man, who was twenty-six or twenty-seven years old, with thick arms and a chubby face, and with two very round and bright eyeballs deeply embedded under his thick eyebrows, it was difficult to find any weakness in his appearance. Judging by his appearance, there was neither sorrow nor joy in his world. He was the typical new youth of this Batu He Shuo wilderness.

Daina Zhai, nestled in old woman Kani Oluxi's arms, shook her big mouth, drooled, and asked me like a fool:

—Hee hee, why don't you go back to your home? Hee hee…

I didn't pay attention to her. With my silence, she was about to open her mouth and nag me again, but she was scolded by the old woman, and she honestly just rolled her eyes and looked at my face.

Sha Manlijin stayed silent for a while, then asked me lonely:

—Sir, when did you come to the Batu He Shuo wilderness?

—Three months ago.

—Then where did you live three months ago?

—There is no fixed place, Duobo, Yiketulu Mountain Village, the valleys of Hada Mountain, I have been to all of them.

—There is always no place to settle down for a long time. Constantly running on the road, the wind and snow hit, it is easy to get sick. Alas…

She seemed a little lost.

I looked at them all surrounding me, and the intimate and warm voices of conversation, when I heard them, immediately gave me deep comfort and a heart-warming joy.

Telingfu was moved by the few words I and Sha Manlijin had said, and his face was involuntarily filled with strands of gloomy colors. Imagination gave him a transcendent indignation, and he looked around my body with melancholy eyes. Ah, my body was covered with a layer of travel-worn dust and the haggard shadows of dreams.

That voice, which seemed familiar to me, the caring voice of a loving mother, came out of his throat:

—Good friend, it is not easy for you to come to our Nau Ho Village. I hope you will live in our house. It is convenient, so don't be too restrained—this is my father, this is my mother, this is my younger sister, and then there is me and my wife.

He said so much to me intimately. After a while, his voice suddenly became louder, and a kind of sympathetic and powerful words strangely stimulated my heart:

—Good friend, your illness will get better, don't be sad. People who leave home must learn to be brave and decisive! Like us Bula people, like the Solun people.

This was an explosive bomb that was deeply thrown into my heart.

—Ah, ah…

My floating and throbbing heart began to be shattered by this exploding bomb!

It was still night outside. The wind was still blowing in the night.

If 185

— Luo Hong

If I were a painter, I would definitely silently, silently, use my pen earnestly to describe the lives of human beings, to paint a picture. In this picture, you can see blood-red hearts, people covered in claws and teeth, bullying each other. This one sucks the blood of that one, and that one sucks the fresh blood of another. They struggle and live in this swirling vortex, very naturally. They all sacrifice everything, even sucking the last drop of fresh blood from others, for the impulse to live.

If I were a musician, I would definitely create several musical scores, create several songs; and then let these songs spread in the streets and alleys, and in people's various paradises, so that those noble smiles would turn into cries, and those who are crying might laugh.

If I were a writer, I would definitely silently write a creation that is like a multi-faceted mirror, so that hypocrisy and ugliness would have no way to escape truthfully in front of it.

If I were a humorist, my pen would rarely have time to rest. People's lives are inherently humorous: as long as you pick up a pen, there is humorous material everywhere.

No One Knows (2) 186

— Written by Hugh Auchelcross Translated by He Wei

Louise Torrence ran out, ran across the potato field, a towel for the dishes in her hand. "How did you know I wanted to go away with you?" she said indignantly. "How did you know?"

George Willard did not answer. They stood silently in the darkness, separated only by a fence. "You go first," she said. "Father is there. I will come. You wait by the granary at the Williams' place."

This young journalist had received a letter from Louise Torrence. This letter, sent to the office of the Winesburg Eagle, was just that morning. The letter was very simple, it only said: "If you want me, I am yours." She deliberately pretended that there was no relationship between them in the darkness near the fence, which made them feel very upset. "She's stubborn, she really is stubborn," he muttered to himself as he walked down the street, passing some wasteland where rice grew. The rice was planted all the way to the sidewalk and was already as tall as the shoulder.

Louise Torrence appeared from the front door of her house, still wearing the calico clothes she had been wearing to wash the dishes, and she was not wearing a hat. The child could see her holding the handle of the door in her hand, standing and talking to someone in the breeze. That must be her father, old Jack Torrence. Old Jack was half-deaf, so she was shouting very loudly. Then the door closed, and everything was dark and silent on the narrow little street. George Willard trembled as he had never trembled before.

In the shadows near the granary at the Williams' place, George and Louise stopped. They dared not speak. She was not very beautiful, and she even had a mole next to her nose. George guessed that it must be because she would wipe her nose with her fingers after picking up the pots in the kitchen.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Conversations

The Mermaid Cried 187

— Jia Wei

The Sixth National Games, which opened on the Double Tenth National Day, at the magnificent municipal stadium built in front of the "New Shanghai" municipal government at a cost of more than one million, and with the enthusiastic support of hundreds of thousands of spectators, the famous athletes from all over the country have indeed repeatedly broken many of the Games, national, and even Far East records, which is gratifying. As for the entanglements caused by the qualification issues of athletes participating in two events in the Games; and the temporary excuses of countless athletes (even famous ones) to abandon the competition, they all revealed the true intentions and ambitions of the general public to participate in the Games. This cannot but be considered a regret and deserves the attention of the athletes and the general public - what is the true meaning of sports after all?

Speaking of the athletes in the Games, the most famous and most eye-catching, "known to women and children," is Ms. Yang Xiuqiong, the "Mermaid" from Hong Kong.

Indeed, since the "Mermaid" became famous in the previous National Games, she has truly become a popular figure and an important person concerned by everyone in society (especially the adults and brothers who admire her name and her person). I remember that after the last Games closed, there was the opening of the Shanghai-Ping Combined Transport Line, and she was invited to perform the ribbon-cutting ceremony. The old "sports enthusiast" who created Tai Chi exercises, advocated kicking shuttlecocks, and flying kites, specially prepared a carriage and personally drove her to tour the capital city to see the light. After she returned, newspapers everywhere often published news about her, especially concerned about her marriage. This year, when a swimming pool was completed in a certain place, she was specially invited from thousands of miles away with thousands of gold pieces for travel expenses to perform the opening ceremony.

This time she came, in addition to the crowds welcoming her at the pier, so crowded that male athletes had to protect her to break through, that enthusiasm, that grandeur, there were also hotels sending letters inviting her to stay for free, and providing transportation, and newspapers had special reporters to write a diary for her every day - getting up early and sleeping late, three meals a day, all copied and published without a mistake. It can be said that she received the welcome of people from all walks of life, who can match her, the darling of heaven!

However, things turned out unexpectedly. The 50-meter swimming final on the 17th was a disaster. Look: "After the 50-meter race, Miss Yang was runner-up, and no one cared about her when she came out of the water; her pink face was flushed, and her eyes seemed unable to bear the pain, she lowered her head dejectedly and went straight to the lounge, sobbing. This is the first time since the lady has enjoyed fame that she has been defeated..."

"Pink face flushed," "lowered her head dejectedly," "sobbing," how touching is that! This will worry the people who care about her.

However, in the 50-meter preliminary and semi-final, and the 100-meter freestyle and backstroke races, our "Mermaid" still set amazing new records, and indeed lived up to expectations. May the "Mermaid" strive for it!

Originally, there must be competition and rivalry on the sports field. However, this is not about being competitive and vying for the limelight for a while. This is something that every athlete must understand. Especially since we are in the era and environment of "this time, this place," everything is in contradiction, competition, and struggle... How will young people go a step further to understand society, understand their responsibilities, and prepare to participate in this greatest competition, no, struggle!

Solitary Courtyard 188

— Xinye

It was a deep autumn dusk, and the profound, solitary courtyard lay still like the night itself. All around was quiet, as if one could hear a small insect crawling across the eaves, over the petals of the begonia, and over the slender leaves of the orchid. It seemed as though the petals and leaves were trembling slightly and sighing. But soon, even this minimal sound ceased. What was left was the clear, calm night, like a gentle wave. In the hazy moonlight and faint starlight, one could vaguely make out the black shadows of camellias in the corner of the courtyard. Although the osmanthus trees outside the wall only stretched out a few branches, the wafts of osmanthus fragrance were carried over by the light autumn breeze. The faint moonlight reflected on the flowers and leaves, resembling a layer of pale green glow or silver waves floating on the water's surface.

Han, alone, draped in a sleeping gown, inserted three sticks of Fujian sandalwood into the ancient bronze incense burner on his desk, which had been neglected for a long time. He leaned against the vermilion-lacquered railing before the steps, gazing blankly at the greyish-white smoke rising from the sandalwood, curling outwards towards the window, and then disappearing into the vast, desolate courtyard.

—Ah, that ancient courtyard, it is forever lonely!

The night, that boundless night, was as vast and desolate as this courtyard, and even more like his own heart, stagnant and lost. He stood there quietly, contemplating; no, he was chewing over life, caressing the heart wounded by life. Because he needed peace, he abandoned his friends, abandoned love, abandoned everything, and fled back here from a very distant place, to this ancient courtyard.

"Squeak—squeak—squeak—." A few sharp cries squeezed out from under the courtyard steps, carrying a hint of dampness, like a piece of shattered jade rolling from afar and falling onto the moss saturated with moisture, yet disappearing like a mountain path.

—This is a lonely autumn insect without a mate—is it also feeling the sorrow of loneliness like people do?

He gradually raised his head, looking up at the sky. On the celestial curtain was a not-entirely-full, one could not even say how incomplete, crescent moon, surrounded by a large halo. The few stars beside it were twinkling playfully, reflecting in his eyes.

The old, thin chrysanthemums squatted silently in a corner of the courtyard, resembling a dying old man, so dejected, lacking the vitality of the past few days. Although the shadow of the artificial rockery still stood in the goldfish tank, one could no longer discern its exquisite and intricate peaks and cliffs, nor could one see the vibrant and lovely Puer grass on top. This bleak autumn night was like a widow's plain clothes, billowing with a faint sorrow.

His thoughts were like a wisp of smoke, drifting, aimless, circling in an elusive reminiscence; even more like a lost lone crow, merely wandering in this sea of night. A memory, a hope, and a life, like a measuring rod reaching the sky, dragged past in front, as if wanting to measure the length of this vast and indistinct journey of life, to see how long, how far, lay ahead.

Silently, he shifted his gaze back to the window. In the ancient bronze incense burner at the window, faint wisps of smoke still drifted, but the smoke was so weak that it was almost like a tiny strand of silk. The crescent moon, encircled by its halo, was also covered by a layer of clouds. And so this courtyard, this surrounding area, suddenly lost even this pale light. He placed his hand on the vermilion-lacquered railing, already damp with night dew. A chill, like a finely woven brown bug, burrowed straight from his fingertips, crawled into the depths of his heart, and coiled in his chest, gnawing at his heart. Suddenly, he shuddered, and hurriedly withdrew his hand. A withered leaf fell from the decaying old parasol tree at the courtyard gate, landing silently in front of him, brushing against the railing with a cold, soft sound; it was as if his soul had silently plunged into the abyss of emptiness and darkness.

—The days of the past, truly a long spring dream…

An old memory from the past drifted dreamily into his heart, and the accumulated sadness in his heart was stirred up. The old and new wounds of the past few years resurfaced vividly and intensely, rising up. Large, large teardrops slipped from his eyelids to the tips of his eyelashes, congealing into crystalline beads, like a drop of dew on a grassy tomb, so round that without a breeze to shake it, it would fall unrecoverably onto the steps…

—Ah, that ancient courtyard, it is forever lonely!

Notes by the Window 189

— Family Member

One Dusk

Shaking off the fatigue that had accumulated throughout the day, one suddenly felt relaxed. The room had gradually darkened to the point where one could not see clearly at arm's length, but I did not like lighting a cigarette at this time. Quietly, I moved my legs and stood by the window, silently receiving the slight chill of the evening breeze, silently appreciating the blurry outlines of the houses, the vague shadows of the trees, slowly engulfed by the dense evening mist outside the window. Before dusk arrived, there were weary travelers wandering on the outskirts of the fields, hurrying on their way to rest, and there were also black wings of crows returning to their nests, sorrowful in the dim heavens.

Like a gorgeously dressed, smiling girl, or like a terrifying nightmare, dusk brings the fragrance of roses, scattered in the warm houses, in everyone's thoughts, blooming with brilliant flowers of memory. But at the same time, she creates much sorrow and anxiety in the hearts of the wandering travelers in the wilderness who do not know where to go. And so, regarding the distant, nighttime metropolis, a charming face, in the intertwining of red lights, in a dark corner, all kinds of bizarre things are reflected, the fallen round face, I, however, ponder and appreciate with mysterious emotions.

Two Wandering

It seems like a daze, or like half a lifetime ago, it has been several years since I came to this metropolis. Now, I am familiar with many of the streets, many of the houses, and even many of the faces here, as if they were old friends. But I always feel that this is not a place where I can live for a long time. I always think that one day I will turn to another place, and that there is still a home left behind in the distant past, a hometown where I grew up. Although now I think of it very faintly and not often. Regarding my hometown, regarding my home, even when I recall it, I can only use a kind of wistful mood to feel sad and contemplate, because I don't even know when I will be able to return to my lovely hometown. Perhaps an unfortunate fate has secretly destined me only to have the hardship of an eternal journey of wandering to end this life, with no chance to see my hometown again. And in these days, from that city to this city, I am used to the solitary wandering life. I am like a small boat on the water, "drifting in all directions with the waves, able to dock anywhere," and so everywhere is home. At this moment, I am extremely tired. The long years of wandering have only given me a back full of heavy dust and a heart empty of everything, yet I have no worries, no sorrow, but at the same time no hope, no ideals, not even dreams. I know why the smoke drifts from the window, why the stars twinkle in the sky, why the lake water ripples in the wind, why the cuckoos cry in the middle of the night. Knowing these things, I am at peace with my wandering, without feeling any sadness or longing for the past.

Three City Life

Immersed in the day and night of noisy, mechanical sounds, the sounds of vehicles, all kinds of sounds mixed together to form the unique urban noise, coupled with the all-encompassing thick black coal smoke, it will really make people feel suffocated. When you go out and come back, your nose is full of dirt and your face is covered in dust. The people in the city, indeed, the clamorous noise alone is enough to make you suffer from hysteria. And gradually, your emotions become thinner and thinner, almost thinning to the point of completely losing their function. At this time, your senses become duller and duller, as if you have become a soulless machine, indifferent to everything and showing no interest at all, mechanically passing the days without any lively emotions. Life is a pool of stagnant water, never able to stir up waves, and life is even more of a burden, wasted meaninglessly. I see many people numbing themselves with strong sensual pleasures all day long, letting their spirits crawl under the yoke of material things. Time seems to stop flowing in people's eyes. It is the footsteps of time that are rapidly rushing past people, but people have not caused any surprise. And so everyone frantically, painfully, is engulfed in all the circles of ruined women and licentiousness, trying their best to climb up to the crater, but not thinking that the suppressed fire will soon erupt, and burn their bodies into ashes, the tourists laughing on the crater.

In the Hutong 190

— Green Leaf

—Impressions of an Ancient City

In ordinary days, there are two sounds in the small hutong that add to the grayness and loneliness of the ancient city: in the daytime, it is the blind fortune teller's gong, and at night, it is the night watchman's clapper. These have the charm of the Middle Ages and contain the nostalgia for a distant home.

In the small hutong, besides these ancient sounds that have been around for a long time, there is the sound of the peddler's small rattle drum, but the peddler runs around in the streets and alleys, coming once every two or three days; therefore, every day in the hutong, there are only these two sounds, knocking through other people's dreams, knocking through the heart of the ancient city.

Every day, when the sun shines on the roof ridge, the hutong is so quiet that there is not a single breeze; then the blind fortune teller strikes his fortune-telling gong, perhaps he already knows how old the girl in which family is, and which family has a lonely old widow whose son is on a distant expedition in a foreign land; he has also figured out the height of which stone in the hutong, and walks slowly in the hutong, letting the sunlight shine on his face. The fortune-telling gong in his hand "Ke dang! Ke dang!" rings and rings, echoing in the silent hutong. At this time, a little girl's shrill voice calls out to the blind fortune teller in the hutong. I know that it is the old widow across the street who has called the little maidservant to ask the blind man to predict the good and bad luck of her son abroad. In this way, making a blind inquiry can put a big stone down from the old woman's heart, right? I don't care about this foolish superstitious behavior, but I bless this lonely old widow living alone.

The hutong of the ancient city is also gray, and you often don't see a child in the daytime; if you want to eavesdrop on the innocent laughter of children to warm the heart of a wanderer, it is not possible. What there is, are gray walls with peeling whitewash, gray roofs, and gray sand: everything is painted with gray pigment, so the ancient city is also called a symbol of a person's twilight years. At dusk, the waning moon hangs on the corner of the roof, and there is not a ghost shadow in the hutong; walking step by step in the hutong, you can hear the sound of your own footsteps and the rustling of a piece of wind from your clothes. Later in the night, the old night watchman comes, knocking on the bamboo clapper in the small hutong, just like the blind fortune teller's gong in the daytime, waking up other people's dreams: and at night, the hutong only has this one sound, and only he alone rules this hutong.

Every day, listening to these two sounds in the small hutong, I often think of a folk rhyme about blind men and night watchmen in my hometown, which is full of rough rural flavor. (But in the ancient city, there is not a single folk rhyme related to the immortal-like people who live apart from the crowd). In my childhood, I and the other children often ran behind the blind man, singing that folk rhyme loudly, making the blind man only wear an awkward face, which was fun: the mood of childhood was not schadenfreude, but just to join in the fun. But now, wandering in the ancient city, listening to the sounds of the clapper and the fortune-telling gong; I have long lost the mood of a child, and I have forgotten most of this folk rhyme.

New Song Introduction 191

Parents and Children

The theme song of the cultural sound film "Parents and Children" today: High-ranking guests are seated, dancing and singing; ladies and gentlemen, colorful and excited. But, don't you see: Red land for thousands of miles, floods raging; wailing everywhere, starving people crying! Don't you hear: External insults and internal troubles, ghosts crying and gods howling; natural and man-made disasters, the starving lying in the streets! Thousands upon thousands of parents and children, separated from life and death; families broken and people dead, wailing and crying! Listen, the alarm has sounded! In danger, the land of our parents! How can we still enjoy ourselves today? We must be the "parents and children" of the times, quickly launch the angry tide of national liberation! If we don't rise up today, when will we? The rise and fall of the nation, all depends on us!

Opening "Fruit Report Follow-up Visit"

The imperial inspector Mao Longxing is in high spirits, and looks around with a romantic air, very heroic. The master and servant duo travel along the riverbank. They call for a flat boat and the oars sing a lullaby. The river water is turbulent and the wind is light. Xiangcheng is faintly visible and the road is far away. The young boatman is named Wang Xi. He pushes a pole to guide the boat. They chat and ask each other questions. They relieve boredom in the boat. He visits a sworn brother in the city. The two words "South Building" are his surname, Diao. Unexpectedly, the boatman often sighs. He pities his wife who went to the underworld last year. On the Dragon Boat Festival, he returned from Yangzhou. His wife drank wine on the roof of the building. She welcomed the eastern person into the inner room. It was a bad time and her life was difficult to escape. The steamed bun was like a soul-calling ticket. It ended the hero's life. How can the words of poisoning be said? Adultery and plotting murder is difficult to eliminate. There is already real evidence before your eyes. The adulterous woman and adulterer should be executed by slicing them into pieces. Waiting for an honest official to file a lawsuit. Otherwise, there will be trouble first. The concubine is chaste and the servant is righteous. They will avenge the master one day. Anger makes it difficult to control oneself. He jumps in the cabin several times with boots on. He visits in person.

Movie news

Some Rejoice, Some Grieve 196

"Some rejoice, some grieve," these are such heartbreaking words, especially in these times of chaos and famine. The inequalities of the world are completely exposed in these seven short words, truly great! This folk song.

The wealthy eat delicacies and wear fine silk. When they hear this folk song sung, naturally they don't feel anything. Like the Zifang couple, when they have guests and are toasting under the moon, singing this "Bending Moon" folk song is purely an offhand expression, and they don't realize it's a foreshadowing of their family's future.

If the mountain flood hadn't erupted, their family would have lived happily. They would never have had the ending of husband leaving wife, and their personalities wouldn't have changed so quickly. But things rarely go as wished in this world. No one's life story is ever just a plain record. There will always be a twist to embellish it. This five-act play "Bending Moon" also narrates the separations and reunions, joys and sorrows of life, the wickedness of human nature, and the horror of women relying solely on their husbands. After the husband and wife are separated and living different lives, on nights of family reunion, when they sing this folk song "Some rejoice, some grieve" again, they will naturally have different feelings. The husband, Zifang, lost Manzhu, but has another charming noble lady by his side, so he will naturally feel that the present is better than the past. However, for Manzhu, comparing her current situation with past happiness, she will definitely feel miserable and heartbroken.

This large-scale play movement by the Mingxing Film Company is led by Hu Die, and performed by all the male and female stars. Combined with such a sad and touching story as "Bending Moon," its sensational success is predictable—this is a good opportunity. We hope the audience who love plays will not miss it.

Maureen O'Sullivan and Zach Maclaine in "Flowers of Destruction" 197

— Nanjing Screening

A Song Presented

In "Little Aunt," there are two songs composed by Mr. Li Jinhui. One is "Under the Moon," sung by Xia Peizhen, and the other is "Flowery World," sung by Ying Yin. Both have already been recorded by Baidai.

"Under the Moon," Xia Peizhen sings in the desolate moonlit night garden, fully conveying the sad mood. As for "Flowery World," Ying Yin sings it in the peach blossom forest, leaning tipsily in her lover's arms; as light as goose feathers, as fiery as burning passion!

Song fans, please note: The "Joyful Forest" has already begun giving away these two songs. Enclose two cents for postage and send it to the Propaganda Department of "Joyful Forest" Company, No. 1 Renchang Lane, Kaizi'er Road, Shanghai, and you will receive a beautiful song score.

Silver Jottings 198

— Zhi Er

I heard people say that Yuan Shouzhi ultimately can't leave Ying Yunwei. I wonder what that means?

"Sea Burial" has stopped showing at the New Light Theater. A friend said that if Shao Zuiweng were in Shanghai, Wang Bin would definitely not have the opportunity to direct a second film. And now, in Shao Cunren's hands, I wonder if he's also judging the quality of films based on box office success or failure? I'm very concerned.

It's said that "Imperial Envoy" will follow "Wave Village" and be shown at the Jincheng Theater. Others say that "Wave Village" will be followed by "Filial Piety," which has been advertised for a long time. The two accounts are conflicting. I don't know which is true. According to the news I've obtained, "Filial Piety" is currently being dubbed. If it's ready in time, it will be released after "Wave Village." If not, "Imperial Envoy" will be shown.

It was previously said that "Filial Piety" was scheduled to be released on Double Tenth Day (October 10th). At that time, it was purely a silent film. After the screening rights for Double Tenth Day were negotiated and "Metropolitan Scenery" was shown by Diantong, a soundtrack was added.

It's heard that when "Imperial Envoy" is shown, the order of appearance will determine the ranking. On the posters, the order may be based on the number of strokes in the surnames. The rumors about Yuan Meiyun fighting for a higher ranking are probably inaccurate, because she is actually quite clever.
